# Strategy Research Decision Ledger

Created: 2026-06-05
Last reorganized: 2026-06-13
Last updated: 2026-06-15

Purpose: this file is the canonical decision index for strategy research. Keep
accepted systems, invalid-evidence rules, source/data gates, and compact
do-not-rerun conclusions here. Put long-form search notes and working
narratives in `research_artifacts/`, and keep generated reports under
`data/reports/campaigns`.

### Current Search Policy

- No rejected branch becomes active again unless a materially new filter,
  data source, execution module, or validation design directly addresses the
  recorded failure.
- For ES orderflow research, prefer corrected Sierra-compatible aggregated
  bar-level features first. True bid/ask or book-depth orderflow remains
  blocked until reliable historical `trades` plus `mbp-1`/`tbbo`/`mbo` data
  and point-in-time reconstruction are available.
- Do not use the ES 15:15 flatten or NQ long50 shortlist passes as proof of
  live eligibility. They passed only the seven shortlist-selection tests under
  the updated 2026-06-14 benchmark and both failed the fresh 2026-06-15
  `acceptance_oos_test` on PF and MAR.
- Do not use the base ES signed-flow continuation as a shortlist pass. Its
  fresh rerun failed `limited_monkey_test`, `simulated_incubation_core`, and
  `simulated_incubation_monkey` under the updated benchmark.
- The historical no-new-data ES-only independent mean-reversion candidate
  `bankruptcy_distress_reversion/ES/1m/chapter11_yoy_prior_down_long` is now
  archived as not-likely under the 2026-06-14 screen. Do not treat it as an
  active near-pass or live candidate without a materially new thesis and a
  fresh benchmark run.
- The current ranked data-gated ES mean-reversion follow-up remains: first,
  `mes_es_flow_divergence_reversion/ES/1m/afternoon_mes_large20_buy_pressure_short_2020start`
  after approved longer ES+MES `trades` history; second,
  `quote_liquidity_sweep_reversion/ES/1m/tbbo_failed_pdh_pdl_or30_sweep_reclaim`
  after an approved one-year ES `tbbo` pilot.
- There are no current production follow-up rows from the shortlist refresh.
  Any live candidate must include `acceptance_oos_test` and must write a fresh
  full-stack `campaign_test_summary.json` with `passed: true`.

### Source-Validity Guardrails

- Pre-fix Sierra cache evidence is invalid unless kept only as a metric-free
  `INVALID (pre-fix Sierra timezone cache)` audit note.
- Valid Sierra full-history evidence must explicitly use corrected `_ny`
  caches, or the row must be based on independently verified non-Sierra data.
- Sierra SCID-derived minute OHLCV is valid only as reconstructed completed-bar
  evidence after the cache builder filters bar-like contracts, timestamp issues,
  incomplete sessions, and weak side-volume coverage. Do not use raw Sierra
  `.scid` files or reconstructed minute bars for print-level sequencing,
  tick-replay fills, large-print assumptions, or exact intra-minute stop/target
  ordering without a separate source-quality audit.
- Commission, slippage, prop-rule risk, and close-position compliance are not
  tuning knobs. New candidates must flatten before the 16:59:59 ET futures
  daily close unless the user explicitly changes the policy.
- External datasets need documented release timing, no unreconstructable
  revised-history dependency, no survivorship-biased reconstruction, and enough
  live-usable history for WFA plus simulated incubation.

### Repo Consistency Watch

- `research_artifacts/third_independent_strategy_search_20260613.md` remains a
  historical support artifact for the old NQ and rejected third-strategy search
  branches. It is not current live-promotion evidence after the 2026-06-14
  benchmark refresh.

## Repository And Validation Rules

- Project structure: Python package under `src/propstack`, campaign YAMLs under `configs/campaigns`, ES roll data under `configs/data/ES`, raw/cache market data under `data/raw` and `data/cache`, generated evidence under `data/reports/campaigns`, tests under `tests`.
- Existing strategy shell: `propstack.strategy.modular.ModularStrategy` composes one entry module, one stop module, and one target module.
- Module registries live under `src/propstack/strategy_modules/`; do not treat this ledger as an exhaustive module inventory.
- YAML schema: top-level `campaign_id`, `variant_id`, `strategy_name`, `symbol`, `dataset_id`, `timeframe`, `data`, `strategy`, `core`, `benchmarks`, `core_grid`, `monkey`, `wfa`, `prop_rules`, `monte_carlo`; report root is computed from campaign, symbol, dataset, timeframe, and variant by current code.
- Test framework: `pytest`, configured in `pyproject.toml` with `pythonpath = ["src"]`.
- End-to-end campaign script: `PYTHONPATH=src python3 -m propstack.run_campaign_stages --config PATH --skip-validation`.
- Acceptance criteria: staged runner defaults in `src/propstack/research/campaign_stages.py`. The updated 2026-06-14 screenshot benchmark is canonical. A pass requires limited core grid >=100 combinations and >=70% profitable iterations; limited monkey >=90% beat net profit and >=90% beat max drawdown; WFA selected by MAR with trade count >50/year, no early exit, >=10 windows, stitched OOS PF >=1.2, MAR >=0.4, and total trades >=500; WFA OOS monkey >=80% beat net profit and >=80% beat max drawdown; WFA OOS Monte Carlo probability profit before drawdown >50%; simulated incubation core PF >=1.0, MAR >=1.0, and total trades >=75; simulated incubation monkey >=80% beat net profit and >=80% beat max drawdown; acceptance OOS PF >=1.0, MAR >=1.0, and total trades >=25 on the latest 6-month OOS window trained on the prior 24 months. Expectancy R is reported but is no longer a hard screenshot gate.
- Data assumptions: ES Databento DBN 1-minute OHLCV remains available for legacy full-history price/volume tests, but aggregated bar-level orderflow research is valid only from corrected UTC-to-New-York Sierra caches or independently verified Databento/Rithmic-style sources. Prefer strategies using 1-minute OHLCV plus `BidVolume`, `AskVolume`, `NumberOfTrades`, signed volume, buy volume, and sell volume. Defer additional Databento individual-print history requests until corrected aggregated bar-level orderflow candidates are exhausted. Existing explicit ES roll calendar `configs/data/ES/motivewave_rithmic_roll_calendar.csv`, no price adjustment, spreads excluded, America/New_York timestamps, RTH/ETH sessions from config, roll-boundary reset of previous-day levels, and warmup rules still apply.
- Execution assumptions: signals are evaluated on bar close and entered next bar open; ES tick size 0.25 and tick value 12.50; commission and slippage come from YAML and must not be reduced to force a pass.
- Same-bar ambiguity: engine resolves stop/target conflicts with 1-minute detail data on higher-timeframe runs where available; otherwise fallback is conservative stop-first.
- Prop-rule assumptions: `PropRules` tracks starting balance, daily loss limit, trailing drawdown, max contracts, best-day concentration, min trading days, payout threshold, profit target percent, and drawdown limit percent.
- Close-position compliance constraint added 2026-06-06: do not pursue any new strategy that holds an open position through the futures daily market close. User-defined close is 16:59:59 ET and reopen is 18:00 ET. New screens and staged candidates must flatten before 16:59:59 ET; RTH-style 16:00 ET exits are eligible, but overnight/ETH hold logic that crosses the daily close is ineligible regardless of performance.
- External-data eligibility updated 2026-06-09: external datasets may be used if they are reliable in real time and can be reconstructed without hindsight. Each accepted external source must have a documented publication schedule or a conservative lag, no unreconstructable revised-history dependency unless point-in-time vintages are available, no survivorship-biased reconstruction, and enough unattended public/licensed history to cover WFA and simulated incubation.
- Daily-loss benchmark update 2026-06-11: do not use `$1,500` as a hard acceptance gate for new `$150,000` account screens. It is too stringent because it equals 1% account risk and can reject a strategy after one full-risk losing trade even when configured `prop_rules.daily_loss_limit` is `$4,000`. Implemented in `src/propstack/backtest/metrics.py`: `benchmarks.max_daily_loss` is now advisory only and no longer appears in hard benchmark failures. Future screens should treat actual prop-rule daily-loss/trailing-drawdown failure as the hard risk constraint, keep worst-day PnL reported, and use `$3,000` as a warning/preference level rather than a hard rejection. Existing configs may still contain historical `benchmarks.max_daily_loss: 1500`; that legacy field alone cannot reject a new candidate.

- Sierra SCID timezone correction and ledger cleanup 2026-06-11/12: the pre-fix full Sierra orderflow cache `data/cache/orderflow/es_sierra_trade_orderflow_1m_20101214_20260610_full_rth.parquet` was built from SCID timestamps as if they were New York wall time. SCID timestamps are UTC-source values, but the cache builder filtered `09:30-15:59` before converting to `America/New_York`; therefore every strategy diagnostic using that pre-fix cache is `INVALID (pre-fix Sierra timezone cache)`, not passed, failed, rejected, near-pass, promotion, tuning, ranking, or do-not-rerun evidence. Detailed pre-fix Sierra result rows were removed from the live decision ledger instead of retaining invalid metrics. The invalidated families include stale `*_full_sierra` campaign reruns selected from the erroneous cache and derived pre-fix screens such as cross-pocket, footprint-extreme, volume-curve/signed-flow, and participation-composition diagnostics. Do not use old PnL, PF, WFA, monkey, ranking, promotion, rejection, tuning, or do-not-rerun guidance from those runs for any decision.
- Sierra cleanup enforcement 2026-06-12: an exact post-cleanup scan for known bad identifiers without a corrected `_ny` suffix now hits only this metric-free audit block: `sierra_trade_orderflow_1m_20110105_20260610_full_rth`, `es_sierra_trade_orderflow_1m_20101214_20260610_full_rth`, `es_sierra_cross_pocket_meta_signal_1m_20110105_20260610`, and `es_sierra_footprint_extreme_1m_20110105_20260610`. If any future ledger row depends on the wrong-timezone Sierra cache, delete the detailed row completely; keep only a metric-free `INVALID (pre-fix Sierra timezone cache)` note if traceability is necessary. The only Sierra full-history metrics allowed in the ledger must be explicitly labeled corrected `_ny` reruns or independently verified non-Sierra/Databento/Rithmic-style sources. One-year Databento-sourced orderflow notes that say "Sierra-compatible" refer to feature availability, not to the invalid Sierra raw cache. Corrected `_ny` reruns are corrected-data audits, not proof that the original wrong-timezone tests were valid.

## Latest Aggregated Orderflow Diagnostics

- Sierra aggregated-orderflow ingestion support: added `src/propstack/data/sierra_orderflow.py` and CLI `src/propstack/build_sierra_orderflow_cache.py` so Sierra Chart text/CSV exports can be converted into the same 1-minute cache schema consumed by `trade_orderflow_features`. Supported export fields are `Date`, `Time`, `Open`, `High`, `Low`, `Last`, `Volume`, `NumberOfTrades`, `BidVolume`, and `AskVolume`; `AskVolume` maps to `buy_volume`, `BidVolume` maps to `sell_volume`, and `signed_volume = AskVolume - BidVolume`. This cache intentionally omits individual-print large-trade buckets, so Sierra-first campaigns must keep `data.trade_orderflow_features.large_trade_sizes: []`. Priority update from user: continue searching aggregated bar-level orderflow strategies first; only recommend buying extra Databento trade/depth history after this Sierra-compatible lane is exhausted. Historical one-year rerun targets were `configs/campaigns/bar_orderflow_participation_state/variants/ES/1m/dense_rank_value_priority_ensemble.yaml`, `configs/campaigns/bar_orderflow_participation_state/variants/ES/1m/nonoverlap_rank_combo_1030_1330_1400.yaml`, and `configs/campaigns/bar_orderflow_participation_state/variants/ES/1m/rank_volume_effort_imbalance_tight_r.yaml`; the corrected `_ny` audit above supersedes that queue, so these are design references only rather than active rerun targets.

## Future Search Budget And Constraints

- Start new search work from the recorded rejected-family constraints, current
  data-gated follow-up list, and any current user objective. There are no
  accepted live-eligible systems after the 2026-06-14 benchmark refresh; do not
  treat old "continue until a pass" language or old-stack passes as active.
- Default next lane for ES orderflow research remains aggregated bar-level orderflow tested only on corrected UTC-to-New-York Sierra caches or independently verified orderflow sources. Any test built from the pre-fix Sierra raw-cache timestamp assumption is invalid evidence and must be removed from the live decision ledger or kept only as a metric-free `INVALID (pre-fix Sierra timezone cache)` audit note.
- Databento individual-print and depth features remain lower-priority diagnostics unless the user explicitly chooses the true-orderflow branch or the aggregated bar-level lane is exhausted.
- Variants per campaign: exactly 3.
- Timeframes per variant: exactly 3.
- New variant-timeframe configs per campaign: 9.
- Tunable parameters per config: maximum 2 entry, 1 TP, 1 SL, maximum 4 total.

## New Campaign 1 Plan

- Campaign: `overnight_inventory_reversion`
- Edge thesis: ES RTH opens or early drives that extend beyond overnight inventory extremes can become failed auctions when price reclaims the overnight range; the strategy fades the failed extension back toward the range/session balance.
- Research/rationale: market-structure reasoning. No external citation is claimed.
- Why ES: ES has deep overnight participation, visible RTH liquidity reset at 09:30 ET, and frequent overnight high/low reference behavior.
- Regime expected to work: balanced or mean-reverting sessions where overnight extremes act as liquidity pools and failed early auctions rotate inward.
- Regime expected to fail: strong trend days, macro/news breakouts, or persistent opening drives that hold outside overnight range.
- Variants:
  - `on_extreme_reclaim_fixed_r`: trade a reclaim of overnight high/low after an RTH sweep outside the overnight range.
  - `on_extreme_reclaim_vwap_filter`: same failed-auction entry, requiring reclaim relative to session VWAP to avoid fading strong one-way auctions.
  - `on_midpoint_reversion_confirmed`: enter only after reclaiming deeper into the overnight range, using the overnight midpoint as confirmation context.
- Timeframes:
  - Fast reclaim variants: 1m, 2m, 5m for tight auction timing and enough trade count.
  - Midpoint confirmation variant: 2m, 5m, 10m for less noise and cleaner confirmation bars.

## New Campaign 2 Plan

- Campaign: `vwap_pullback_continuation`
- Edge thesis: After ES establishes an RTH directional bias, a controlled pullback into session VWAP that rejects and closes back in trend direction can offer continuation with defined invalidation at the pullback extreme.
- Research/rationale: market-structure reasoning. No external citation is claimed.
- Why ES: ES has deep intraday liquidity and VWAP is a common institutional benchmark; trend days often respect VWAP or quickly reclaim it after shallow pullbacks.
- Regime expected to work: directional RTH sessions with orderly pullbacks and sustained participation.
- Regime expected to fail: balanced/choppy sessions, VWAP chop, news reversals, and late-day mean reversion.
- Variants:
  - `opening_drive_vwap_pullback`: require an opening-drive bias before taking the first VWAP pullback continuation.
  - `vwap_reclaim_trend_continuation`: require a sequence of closes on the trend side of VWAP, then a pullback and reclaim.
  - `failed_vwap_break_continuation`: require an intrabar break through VWAP that fails by the close, expressing trapped countertrend traders.
- Timeframes:
  - Opening-drive variant: 1m, 2m, 5m for enough entries while preserving early-session timing.
  - Reclaim/trapped-countertrend variants: 2m, 5m, 10m to reduce VWAP noise and same-bar churn.

## New Campaign 3 Plan

- Campaign: `pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation`
- Edge thesis: A fresh break and hold beyond the prior RTH high/low can indicate range expansion and continuation participation, unlike the already rejected sweep-reclaim fade of the same levels.
- Research/rationale: market-structure reasoning. No external citation is claimed.
- Why ES: Prior-session highs/lows are widely watched references in ES, and successful acceptance beyond them can attract breakout and stop-driven continuation flow.
- Regime expected to work: directional range-expansion days, gap-and-go sessions, and sessions where prior-day extremes convert into support/resistance.
- Regime expected to fail: false breakouts, balanced sessions, low-volume lunch chop, and immediate reversion back into the prior range.
- Variants:
  - `fresh_close_break`: trade the first fresh RTH close through the prior RTH high/low.
  - `break_retest_hold`: require a close through the level, then a retest that holds the broken level.
  - `gap_hold_continuation`: require an RTH gap beyond the prior RTH high/low and sustained closes outside the level.
- Timeframes:
  - Fresh close break: 1m, 2m, 5m to capture initial acceptance quickly.
  - Break-retest hold: 2m, 5m, 10m to reduce noise around the retest.
  - Gap-hold continuation: 1m, 2m, 5m to keep enough early-session observations.

## New Campaign 4 Plan

- Campaign: `rth_gap_fade`
- Edge thesis: ES RTH gaps away from the prior RTH close can overextend early and partially or fully mean-revert toward the prior close when the opening impulse fails.
- Research/rationale: market-structure reasoning. No external citation is claimed.
- Why ES: ES has a liquid overnight session and a visible RTH liquidity reset; prior RTH close is a common reference for gap-fill behavior.
- Regime expected to work: non-news gaps, overnight inventory imbalance that fades after RTH liquidity enters, and early failed directional auctions.
- Regime expected to fail: strong gap-and-go trend days, major macro/news sessions, and days where the prior close is no longer a relevant magnet.
- Variants:
  - `open_reversal`: fade when a gap bar closes back against the gap open.
  - `extension_reject`: fade only after price extends farther from the prior close and then rejects back toward the gap open.
  - `vwap_reclaim`: fade when price reclaims session VWAP against the opening gap.
- Timeframes:
  - All variants: 1m, 2m, 5m to test early gap behavior with enough observations while reducing noise on coarser bars.

## New Campaign 5 Plan

- Campaign: `opening_range_filtered_breakout`
- Edge thesis: ES opening-range breaks may become more robust when the break is confirmed by current-bar participation and VWAP context, while failed breaks stretched away from VWAP may express a distinct early range-fade edge.
- Research/rationale: market-structure reasoning. No external citation is claimed.
- Why ES: ES has deep RTH liquidity and the opening range is a commonly watched early-session reference; successful acceptance or failed acceptance around that range can attract systematic participation.
- Regime expected to work: active RTH openings with clear early auction acceptance, volume-confirmed initiative flow, or overextended failed range breaks.
- Regime expected to fail: low-volume chop, news whipsaws, days where the opening range is too wide to offer clean risk, and trend days for the inverse-fade variant.
- Variants:
  - `volume_confirmed_extension`: continuation breaks with minimum same-bar volume ratio and opening-range extension targets.
  - `vwap_aligned_fixed_r`: continuation breaks requiring trade-side VWAP alignment and cost-adjusted fixed-R targets.
  - `failed_break_fade`: inverse/fade entries after breaks stretched on the breakout side of VWAP, targeting a return through the range.
- Timeframes:
  - All variants: 1m, 2m, 5m, preserving a clean 3-by-3 comparison and testing whether a slightly slower opening-range signal reduces noise without under-sampling.

## Budget-Exhausted Conclusion

- Search budget used: 5 new campaigns, each structured as exactly 3 variants x 3 timeframes.
- Tradable pass found: no. No candidate passed all staged gates.
- Strongest rejected evidence:
  - `pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/fresh_close_break/2m`: core passed, monkey failed only on max-drawdown beat rate (88.625% vs required 90%).
  - `opening_range_filtered_breakout/vwap_aligned_fixed_r/2m`: core passed with 84/108 profitable iterations, monkey failed on net-profit beat rate (76.10% vs required 90%).
  - `pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/gap_hold_continuation/2m`: core near miss at 72/108 profitable iterations (66.67% vs required 70%).
- Confidence decision: none of these are acceptable to trade under the stated process. The near misses are useful research leads only; trading them now would violate the robustness gates.

## Reopened Search: Academic Source Requirement

- Date reopened: 2026-06-06.
- Reason: Prior campaigns were mostly market-structure hypotheses without verified academic support. New attempts must use verified academic sources and keep the full staged validation criteria unchanged.
- Full validation command: `PYTHONPATH=src python3 -m propstack.run_campaign_stages --config PATH`.
- Pass definition: all default stages in `src/propstack/research/campaign_stages.py` must pass without criteria overrides.

## New Academic Campaign 6 Plan

- Campaign: `late_day_intraday_momentum`
- Academic source: Gao, Lei; Han, Yufeng; Li, Sophia Zhengzi; Zhou, Guofu (2018), "Market Intraday Momentum", Journal of Financial Economics 129(2), 394-414, DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2018.05.009`, URL `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0304405X18301351`.
- Finding used: The first half-hour market return predicts the last half-hour market return; predictability is stronger on high-volume and high-volatility days and can improve when combined with the penultimate half-hour return.
- Evidence directness for ES: Indirect. The paper primarily tests SPY and ETFs; ES is used as the liquid S&P 500 futures proxy.
- Edge thesis: Trade the final RTH half-hour in the direction implied by earlier same-day market momentum, expecting closing flow to continue the opening information impulse.
- Why it may apply to ES: ES tracks S&P 500 index exposure, trades with deep liquidity, and is commonly used for index exposure and closing-risk adjustment.
- Why it may survive costs/slippage: The strategy trades at most once per day, uses existing ES transaction-cost assumptions, and avoids high-turnover intraday scalping.
- Expected working regime: Active, directional sessions with persistent information digestion and closing-flow pressure.
- Expected failure regime: Low-volume chop, sharp late reversals, and days where futures closing behavior diverges from ETF closing behavior.
- Translation risks: SPY closing mechanics, ETF flow, and sample period may not transfer cleanly to ES futures; ES has nearly 24-hour trading and different microstructure around the cash close.

## New Academic Campaign 7 Plan

- Campaign: `overnight_return_late_day_momentum`
- Academic source: Liu, Qingfu; Tse, Yiuman (2017), "Overnight Returns of Stock Indexes: Evidence from ETFs and Futures", International Review of Economics & Finance 48, DOI `10.1016/j.iref.2017.01.005`, URL `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1059056016301563`.
- Finding used: For US ETF and futures markets, overnight returns forecast first half-hour returns negatively and last half-hour returns positively.
- Evidence directness for ES: Direct enough to prioritize. The paper explicitly includes E-mini futures and tests first and last half-hour intraday intervals.
- Edge thesis: Trade the final RTH half-hour in the direction of the close-to-open overnight return, expecting overnight information to continue into closing flow.
- Why this is not a renamed failed campaign: Existing `rth_gap_fade` variants traded opening reversal mechanics. This campaign does not enter near the open; it waits for the final half-hour and tests the source paper's positive last-half-hour relation.
- Why it may survive costs/slippage: It trades at most once per day, uses current ES transaction-cost assumptions, and avoids intraday scalping frequency.
- Expected working regime: Sessions where overnight information remains relevant into close and closing flows extend the overnight direction.
- Expected failure regime: Full opening reversal, low-participation closes, and late-day news shocks that override overnight information.
- Translation risks: The published sample ends in 2014; post-2014 E-mini market structure and overnight information assimilation may have changed.

## Grant-Wolf-Yu Fallback Review

- Source reviewed: Grant, James L.; Wolf, Avner; Yu, Susana (2005), "Intraday Price Reversals in the US Stock Index Futures Market: A 15-Year Study", Journal of Banking & Finance, DOI `10.1016/j.jbankfin.2004.04.006`.
- Finding reviewed: Large opening-price changes in S&P 500 futures show initial continuation, then reversal after roughly 10 minutes; the abstract notes reversal profitability is reduced after transaction costs.
- Ledger overlap: Existing `rth_gap_fade` already tested open reversal, extension rejection, and VWAP reclaim gap-fade mechanics across 1m/2m/5m, all with zero profitable limited-core neighborhoods.
- Distinct-mechanic screen: Tested only the paper-specific sequence on 2021-2022 core data: large opening move, 5/10/15/20/30 minute continuation, then delayed fade to 10:30/11:00/12:00/15:30/16:00. Only 2 of 700 rough combinations were positive, both barely above breakeven with PF about 1.02.
- Decision: Do not create a full Grant-Wolf-Yu campaign. It would be mostly a renamed failed opening-gap-fade campaign, and the only distinct delayed-reversal expression is not economically robust under current costs.

## New Academic Campaign 8 Plan

- Campaign: `daily_time_series_momentum`
- Academic source: Moskowitz, Tobias J.; Ooi, Yao Hua; Pedersen, Lasse Heje (2012), "Time Series Momentum", Journal of Financial Economics 104(2), 228-250, DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2011.11.003`, URL `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0304405X11002613`.
- Finding used: Past one- to 12-month returns positively predict futures returns across equity index, currency, commodity, and bond futures.
- Evidence directness for ES: Direct for futures and equity index futures, but translated from the paper's diversified monthly holding design into a single-instrument RTH intraday implementation.
- Edge thesis: Use only completed prior RTH closes to determine a trailing trend direction, enter once near the next RTH open, and flatten by the RTH close.
- Why this is not a renamed failed campaign: It does not use opening ranges, gaps, VWAP, PDH/PDL levels, overnight extremes, or late-day intraday momentum. It is a prior-session close-to-close trend-following mechanic.
- Why it may survive costs/slippage: It trades at most once per day and uses broad multi-session trend filters rather than frequent intraday scalps.
- Expected working regime: Persistent equity-index trend regimes and crisis-trend periods.
- Expected failure regime: Sideways mean-reverting regimes, sharp overnight reversals, and periods where most trend return occurs outside RTH.
- Translation risks: The source's canonical strategy is monthly and diversified across many futures; this is a single ES RTH expression.

## New Academic Campaign 9 Plan

- Campaign: `calendar_session_seasonality`
- Academic source: Floros, Christos; Salvador, Enrique (2014), "Calendar anomalies in cash and stock index futures: International evidence", Economic Modelling 37, 216-223, DOI `10.1016/j.econmod.2013.10.036`, URL `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0264999313004781`.
- Finding used: Day-of-week and monthly seasonal effects differ between cash and stock index futures and are conditioned by market regime; the study includes S&P 500 futures.
- Evidence directness for ES: Direct for S&P 500 futures calendar effects, translated to intraday ES session windows.
- Edge thesis: Calendar effects may concentrate return by weekday and intraday session window; test whether weekday/session windows survive current ES costs and prop constraints.
- Why this is not a renamed failed campaign: It does not use opening range, gaps, VWAP, prior-day levels, overnight extremes, intraday momentum, or multi-session trend. It is a weekday/session seasonal bias.
- Why it may survive costs/slippage: It trades at most once per eligible day and uses session windows rather than high-turnover scalping.
- Expected working regime: Persistent weekday/session flow imbalance.
- Expected failure regime: Calendar anomaly decay, regime shifts, and outlier-dominated windows.
- Translation risks: The source studies daily futures calendar effects; this campaign tests intraday RTH windows and therefore relies on full staged validation.

### Campaign 9 Variants And Configs

| Variant | Timeframe | Config | Status | Result Path | Main Failure Reason |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| midweek_morning_strength | 30m | `configs/campaigns/calendar_session_seasonality/variants/ES/30m/midweek_morning_strength.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/calendar_session_seasonality/ES/1m_full_history/30m/midweek_morning_strength/campaign_tests` | failed limited monkey | Core passed exactly 84/120 profitable (70.0%); top grid net $52,815 PF 1.255, but selected core monkey beat rates were 79.625% net profit / 79.625% max DD vs 90% required. |
| midweek_morning_strength | 15m | `configs/campaigns/calendar_session_seasonality/variants/ES/15m/midweek_morning_strength.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/calendar_session_seasonality/ES/1m_full_history/15m/midweek_morning_strength/campaign_tests` | failed limited monkey | Core passed 101/120 profitable (84.17%); top grid net $70,292.50 PF 1.257, but selected core monkey beat rates were 86.65% net profit / 82.7375% max DD vs 90% required. |

Conclusion: Exhausted. Several weekday/session variants had strong 2021-2022 net PnL, but the robust candidates failed monkey drawdown beat-rate checks or WFA. The broad mixed profiles did not meet the limited core profitability breadth requirement.

## New Academic Campaign 10 Plan

- Campaign: `turn_of_month_futures_effect`
- Academic sources:
  - Carchano, Oscar; Pardo, Angel (2011), "Calendar Anomalies in Stock Index Futures", SSRN `1958587`, URL `https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=1958587`.
  - Maberly, Edwin D.; Waggoner, Daniel F. (2000), "Closing the Question on the Continuation of Turn-of-The-Month Effects: Evidence from the S&P 500 Index Futures Contract", SSRN `244085`, URL `https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=244085`.
- Finding used: Carchano and Pardo report the turn-of-the-month effect as the only statistically and economically significant persistent calendar effect in S&P 500 futures. Maberly and Waggoner are included as an explicit decay warning because they found S&P 500 futures TOTM effects disappeared after 1990.
- Evidence directness for ES: Direct for S&P 500 futures calendar effects, translated to ES RTH intraday windows.
- Edge thesis: Month-start/month-end fund-flow seasonality may concentrate positive ES RTH returns in calendar-day windows around the turn of the month.
- Why this is not a renamed failed campaign: The prior calendar campaign tested weekday/session seasonality. This campaign tests day-of-month seasonality and does not use weekday direction profiles.
- No-lookahead implementation: Uses calendar-day windows (`day <= first_calendar_days` or `days_to_calendar_month_end < last_calendar_days`) rather than future-derived last-trading-day labels.
- Rough screen: On 2021-2022 5m RTH data with approximate current costs, calendar-day proxy windows had 42/75 positive combinations; best was `last4cal_next4cal` 11:00 -> 15:30 with 131 trades, net 18,735, PF 1.31.
- Expected working regime: Persistent turn-of-month inflow and window-dressing flows that affect S&P 500 futures during RTH.
- Expected failure regime: Calendar anomaly decay, strong macro trend reversals, and edge concentration in a small number of month turns.
- Translation risks: Published tests are daily/settlement-oriented; this campaign expresses the effect as intraday RTH entries and relies on full staged validation.

### Campaign 10 Variants And Configs

| Variant | Timeframe | Config | Status | Result Path | Main Failure Reason |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

| classic_turn_window | 15m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/15m/classic_turn_window.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/15m/classic_turn_window/campaign_tests` | failed WFA | Core passed 82/108 profitable (75.93%) and monkey passed at 97.325% net / 99.7375% max-DD beat rates; WFA early-exited at window 1 because selected in-sample PF was 0.74 < 1.00, leaving 0 stitched OOS trades. |

| early_month_strength | 30m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/30m/early_month_strength.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/30m/early_month_strength/campaign_tests` | failed WFA | Core passed exactly 84/120 profitable (70.00%) and monkey passed at 96.4375% net / 99.75% max-DD beat rates; WFA early-exited at window 1 because selected in-sample PF was 0.87 < 1.00, leaving 0 stitched OOS trades. |
| early_month_strength | 15m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/15m/early_month_strength.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/15m/early_month_strength/campaign_tests` | failed core | Limited core tested 120 combinations but only 80 were profitable (66.67%), below the default 70% profitable-iteration threshold; later stages skipped. |
| early_month_strength | 5m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/5m/early_month_strength.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/5m/early_month_strength/campaign_tests` | failed core | Limited core tested 120 combinations but only 80 were profitable (66.67%), below the default 70% profitable-iteration threshold; later stages skipped. |
| expanded_turn_window | 30m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/30m/expanded_turn_window.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/30m/expanded_turn_window/campaign_tests` | failed WFA | Core passed 104/108 profitable (96.30%) and monkey passed at 96.90% net / 99.95% max-DD beat rates; WFA early-exited at window 1 because selected in-sample PF was 0.85 < 1.00, leaving 0 stitched OOS trades. |
| expanded_turn_window | 15m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/15m/expanded_turn_window.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/15m/expanded_turn_window/campaign_tests` | failed WFA | Core passed 104/108 profitable (96.30%) and monkey passed at 97.5625% net / 99.9125% max-DD beat rates; WFA early-exited at window 1 because selected in-sample PF was 0.85 < 1.00, leaving 0 stitched OOS trades. |
| expanded_turn_window | 5m | `configs/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/variants/ES/5m/expanded_turn_window.yaml` | `data/reports/campaigns/turn_of_month_futures_effect/ES/1m_full_history/5m/expanded_turn_window/campaign_tests` | failed WFA | Core passed 104/108 profitable (96.30%) and monkey passed at 98.025% net / 99.925% max-DD beat rates; WFA early-exited at window 1 because selected in-sample PF was 0.85 < 1.00, leaving 0 stitched OOS trades. |

Conclusion: Exhausted. The turn-of-month thesis produced strong 2021-2022 limited-core breadth for the classic and expanded first/last calendar-day windows, and those variants also beat the default monkey tests. However, every combined-window variant failed WFA immediately because the first 2010-2014 train window selected an in-sample PF below the required 1.00 floor. The early-month-only variants were weaker: 30m reached WFA but failed the same early-exit gate, while 15m and 5m missed the limited-core profitability breadth threshold.

### Supplemental Rejection Notes After Campaign 10

- `calendar_session_seasonality/5m/midweek_morning_strength_pf_selected`: created as a selector sensitivity check with `wfa.selection_min_profit_factor: 1.0`. Screening command: `PYTHONPATH=src python3 -m propstack.run_campaign_stages --config configs/campaigns/calendar_session_seasonality/variants/ES/5m/midweek_morning_strength_pf_selected.yaml --skip-validation`. Result path: `data/reports/campaigns/calendar_session_seasonality/ES/1m_full_history/5m/midweek_morning_strength_pf_selected/campaign_tests`. Core and monkey passed, but WFA still failed at window 1 because the best selected in-sample PF was 0.79, below 1.00.
- Turn-of-month WFA first-train selector audit: first train window `2011-01-01` to `2014-12-31` had zero PF>=1 candidates for `expanded_turn_window`, `classic_turn_window`, and `early_month_strength`. Max PFs were 0.856, 0.827, and 0.867 respectively, confirming the WFA failures were not caused by the selector tie-break alone.
- Intraday reversal/continuation after short-horizon move screen: rejected before implementation because the no-lookahead screen returned zero combinations with enough economic strength and robustness.
- Stop-managed prior-day and multi-day selloff reversal screen: rejected before implementation. Some candidates reached aggregate PF around 1.3, but WFA-style block stability was weak and OOS trade counts were too low for the default 500-trade WFA criterion.
- Existing near-miss review: `pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/2m/fresh_close_break` passed core but failed monkey max-DD beat rate and had too few trades for WFA; inspected ORB variants had core/monkey weaknesses and no credible path to the WFA PF/MAR/trade-count gates without materially broadening the failed mechanics.

## New Academic Campaign 11 Plan

- Campaign: `morning_intraday_momentum_continuation`
- Academic source: Gao, Lei; Han, Yufeng; Li, Sophia Zhengzi; Zhou, Guofu (2018), "Market Intraday Momentum", Journal of Financial Economics 129(2), 394-414, DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2018.05.009`, URL `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0304405X18301351`.
- Finding used: Opening-period market returns predict later intraday market returns, with stronger effects on active/high-volatility days.
- Evidence directness for ES: Indirect. The paper tests SPY and ETFs; ES is the liquid S&P 500 futures proxy.
- Why this is distinct from failed Campaign 6: Campaign 6 measured the source return from the prior RTH close and entered only for the final half-hour. Campaign 11 measures the completed source return from the RTH open to the 10:30 signal close and holds a risk-managed afternoon continuation window.
- Rough screen: On the available 2018-2026 cleaned ES feature sample, long entries at 10:30 after RTH-open-to-10:30 returns of at least 8 points produced the strongest candidate with a 15:30 flatten, about 523 trades, aggregate PF about 1.42, and block PFs above 1.30. The staged config adjusts stop percentages into the existing 1% risk sizing envelope rather than changing sizing.
- Expected working regime: Directional morning information flow that persists through the afternoon.
- Expected failure regime: Mean-reverting morning extremes, news reversals, and regimes where the ETF-documented effect does not transfer to ES futures.
- Translation risks: This is a broader morning-to-afternoon implementation, not the paper's exact first-half-hour-to-last-half-hour specification.

### Campaign 11 Variants And Configs

| Variant | Timeframe | Config | Status | Result Path | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| long_only_strength | 5m | `configs/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/variants/ES/5m/long_only_strength.yaml` | failed WFA | `data/reports/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/5m/long_only_strength/campaign_tests` | Core passed 98/100 profitable iterations and monkey passed at 90.725% net / 99.25% max-DD beat rates. WFA then failed: PF 1.116, MAR 0.215, expectancy R 0.056, 508 trades. |
| long_only_pf_selector | 5m | `configs/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/variants/ES/5m/long_only_pf_selector.yaml` | failed WFA | `data/reports/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/5m/long_only_pf_selector/campaign_tests` | Core and monkey passed, but WFA failed with PF 1.113, MAR 0.210, expectancy R 0.054, 508 trades. PF objective did not materially change the selected OOS behavior. |
| long_only_strong_signal | 5m | `configs/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/variants/ES/5m/long_only_strong_signal.yaml` | failed WFA | `data/reports/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/5m/long_only_strong_signal/campaign_tests` | Core passed 100/100 profitable iterations and monkey passed, but WFA failed with PF 1.105, MAR 0.195, expectancy R 0.060, and only 413 trades versus the 500-trade gate. |
| high_volume_morning_strength | 5m | `configs/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/variants/ES/5m/high_volume_morning_strength.yaml` | failed limited monkey | `data/reports/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/5m/high_volume_morning_strength/campaign_tests` | Core passed 88/108 profitable iterations, but selected core failed monkey net-profit robustness at 78.65% versus 90% required; max-DD beat rate passed at 92.05%. |

Conclusion: Exhausted. Morning continuation produced the strongest WFA trade count so far, and the long-only variants cleared the limited core and monkey stages, but WFA profitability and MAR were far below the default pass gates. The high-volume/volatility condition improved core breadth but did not beat constrained random timing strongly enough to advance.

### Supplemental Rejection Notes After Campaign 11

- `morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/5m/two_sided_open15_noon`: created as a two-sided Gao-style sensitivity check with the source window ending at 09:45 and flatten at 12:00. Core passed 98/100 profitable iterations and selected-core monkey passed at 97.6875% net / 98.6375% max-DD beat rates. WFA was stopped after the first window selected a weak 2010-2014 train profile with only 23 trades, PF 1.068, MAR 0.058, and a 2015 OOS loss of -$5,045; rejected as WFA-starved rather than a validation candidate.
- Midmonth weekday/calendar afternoon screen: rejected before implementation. Best fixed enough-trade expression was a Tuesday/Friday midmonth short from 10:30 to 16:00 with WFA PF 1.305, MAR 0.536, and 508 trades; incubation had only 67 trades. Approximate WFA selectors across related calendar candidates stitched PF at or below 0.999 depending objective, so the edge did not meet the default WFA PF/MAR/trade-count shape.
- Opening/source-return continuation screen: rejected before implementation. Best fixed expressions such as 10:30 to 15:00 long continuation after at least 5-6 points of RTH-open strength reached WFA PF about 1.26-1.28 with MAR below 0.45 and 608-686 trades. Approximate WFA selectors reached only about PF 1.17 with MAR near 0.22-0.30.
- Short-horizon intraday overreaction screen: rejected before implementation. The best 15-minute short mean-reversion candidate after a 3-point move with close-location and high-volume filters reached WFA PF 1.199, MAR 0.187, and 575 trades, well below pass thresholds.
- Late-session return-family screen: rejected before implementation. Fixed variants found isolated high-PF candidates, including 10:00 to 14:30 strength entered at 14:30 and exited 15:30 with WFA PF 1.541 and 519 trades, but WFA MAR was only 0.642 and incubation PF was 0.791. Approximate WFA selectors over 5,893 candidates reached only PF 1.234 at best, with MAR around 0.300.
- Additional raw screens rejected before implementation: Liu/Tse overnight/index-futures predictability translations, OPEX/expiration-window seasonality, fixed/adaptive session seasonality, high-frequency 5-minute bar reversal/continuation, and ETH/pre-open continuation/fade variants. Each failed either no-lookahead WFA-style stability, trade-count requirements, or cost-adjusted PF/MAR before a staged candidate was justified.
- Adaptive intraday seasonality screen: rejected before implementation. The no-lookahead rolling same-window return model found 653 core-viable combinations, with best 2021-2022 pockets around 14:00-16:00 and 15:00-16:00, but no fixed candidate survived the broad WFA/incubation shape. Approximate WFA selectors early-exited by window 2 with selected train PF below 1.0.
- Normalized intraday feature screen: rejected before implementation. Normalizing morning return, gap, VWAP distance, previous-close distance, and previous-level breaks by prior average RTH range produced 24,356 core-viable combinations and many strong 2021-2022 pockets, but no fixed candidate met broad-period plus incubation filters. WFA selectors stitched only PF 1.04-1.07 with MAR near zero.
- Path-managed normalized-feature screen: rejected before implementation. A narrower 1-minute stop/target simulation around normalized morning continuation, VWAP continuation, previous-high continuation, and gap-fade families produced 9,495 core-viable stop/target candidates. Strong previous-high continuation pockets reached core PF above 2.5, but broad WFA PF stayed near 1.0-1.15 and incubation was negative; WFA selectors were negative to roughly flat.
- Fixed time-window seasonality screen: rejected before implementation. Simple weekday/time-window long/short biases had no fixed candidate meeting broad-period plus incubation filters. Best approximate WFA selector reached PF 1.13, MAR 0.185, and 968 trades, far below the default WFA PF/MAR gates.
- Regime-conditioned time-window seasonality screen: rejected before implementation. Moving-average and realized-range regime filters improved some late-day long windows, but the best balanced fixed candidate was only around WFA PF 1.279/MAR 0.404 with incubation PF 1.282/MAR 1.427. The best broad-period PF candidate reached WFA PF 1.410 but failed incubation at PF 0.929. Selector stitched PF remained about 0.96-1.10.
- ETH/overnight hold screen: rejected before implementation. Simple ETH long holds showed a real but weak overnight-premium shape; best balanced close-hold candidate (`16:00` to `10:00`, Monday-Wednesday) reached WFA PF 1.219/MAR 0.355 with incubation PF 1.426/MAR 2.023. A narrow 1-minute stop/target path check on the best ETH windows did not improve the broad-period profile; best balanced stop-managed variants remained around WFA PF 1.18 or lower, and WFA selectors stitched only PF 1.08-1.14.
- Randomized simple-rule event search: rejected before implementation. A 30,000-iteration no-lookahead search over RTH entry/exit windows, direction modes, weekday filters, normalized morning/gap/VWAP/previous-close features, trend flags, volume ratio, and volatility filters found no approximate pass. Best fixed candidates reached only about WFA PF 1.29/MAR 0.47 with incubation PF 1.24/MAR 0.75.
- Regime-switching time-window screen: rejected before implementation. Rules that switched long/short by volatility or moving-average regime, instead of filtering one regime out, produced no fixed candidate. Best balanced fixed candidates stayed near WFA PF 1.17/MAR 0.21 with incubation PF 1.24/MAR 1.25, and approximate WFA selectors stitched PF 0.95-1.01.
- Prior-session reversal path-management screen: rejected before implementation. Timestamp-corrected close-to-next-open screening reduced the early VWAP continuation lead to weak prior-day downside reversal candidates around WFA PF 1.30-1.34 and MAR 0.46-0.55. A 1-minute stop/target path screen across prior-day reversal/fade candidates returned zero candidates meeting the approximate core, WFA-period, and incubation gates. The scratch grid did not include holds through the 16:59:59 ET futures daily close, but no candidate was strong enough to promote.
- Intraday VWAP-dislocation continuation screen: rejected before implementation. A timestamp-corrected 5-minute screen of high-volume long continuation after VWAP/previous-close displacement, with eligible flats no later than 16:00 ET, found many core-positive pockets. Best rough flat-hold candidate reached WFA PF about 1.45/MAR 0.56 with 561 trades and incubation PF about 1.95. A targeted 5-minute conservative stop/target pass on the top 40 definitions improved PF in isolated cases, but the best managed WFA MAR remained below 1.0 and incubation was not robust. Strongest managed candidates were still materially below the default WFA MAR >=1.5 gate, so no staged config was justified.
- ETH/reopen-to-same-session screen: rejected before implementation under the user-defined close rule. The screen only allowed entries at/after the 18:00 ET reopen and exits before the next 16:59:59 ET futures daily close. An initial scratch pass was discarded because it accidentally used future ETH returns, such as the 08:00 move, to decide earlier 18:00 entries. The corrected no-lookahead pass required every feature to be known before entry; best fixed candidates fell to about WFA PF 1.42 with MAR below 0.60, despite acceptable trade counts and strong incubation pockets. A corrected approximate WFA selector across 4,919 no-lookahead candidates selected all 10 windows but stitched only PF 1.25, MAR 0.29, 715 trades, and rough expectancy R 0.116. No corrected candidate was close to the default WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates.
- Prior high/low gap-hold fast-confirmation sensitivity: created `configs/campaigns/pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/variants/ES/2m/gap_hold_fast_confirmation.yaml` after reviewing the prior near-miss. It keeps the same costs, sizing, prop assumptions, and a 15:30 ET flatten before the 16:59:59 ET daily close. Screening with `--skip-validation` passed limited core with 125/125 profitable combinations; top core combo had PF 1.471, MAR 2.010, and 106 trades. It also passed limited monkey with 99.10% net-profit beat and 97.075% max-DD beat rates. A WFA-only probe at `configs/campaigns/pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/variants/ES/2m/gap_hold_fast_confirmation_wfa_probe.yaml` then failed the default WFA gate immediately: first train window selected in-sample PF 0.637 and MAR -0.267, triggering early exit before any OOS trades. Result paths: `data/reports/campaigns/pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/2m/gap_hold_fast_confirmation/campaign_tests` and `data/reports/campaigns/pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/2m/gap_hold_fast_confirmation_wfa_probe/campaign_tests`. Rejected as a core-period artifact, not a full-pipeline candidate.
- Adaptive intraday expectancy screen: rejected before implementation. A no-lookahead bucket model used only prior-session history plus current-session features known at the entry bar (weekday, prior-session direction, gap direction, range regime, and source-return bucket) to choose long/short intraday holds. The narrowed screen's best fixed adaptive expression was 11:05 to 15:55 using prior/gap/range/source buckets, with WFA PF about 1.354, MAR 0.276, 521 trades, and incubation PF about 1.082. This missed the WFA PF/MAR and incubation PF requirements by a wide margin.
- Post-RTH/pre-maintenance screen: rejected before implementation under the close rule. A rough screen of 16:00-16:50/16:55 ET post-RTH bars tested RTH-return, final-30/final-60-minute return, close-location, gap, weekday, and prior-range filters. No broad-period candidate was positive after costs; the best rows were recent-only incubation pockets while WFA-period net profit and MAR were negative. Any future use of this segment must flatten no later than the 16:50 bar close timestamped 16:55 ET; no screened result was strong enough to justify a corrected staged module.
- Late-session risk-managed source-return screen: rejected before implementation. The prior flat-hold near-signal (source strength into a 14:30 entry and 15:30 flatten) was revisited with conservative 5-minute stop/target path checks. Broad sweeps were stopped as impractical after the flat-hold evidence already showed inadequate MAR and poor incubation behavior; no completed subset produced a credible pass-shaped candidate, so the late-session source-return family remains rejected.
- Opening overreaction direct screen: rejected before implementation. A close-compliant flat-hold check of delayed opening fade/continuation mechanics found its best row in continuation, not overreaction fade: after a 09:45 high-range source move, enter 10:35 and flatten 13:00, with WFA PF about 1.228, MAR about 0.205, 697 trades, and incubation PF about 1.259. Pure time-window sanity checks were also weak; the best row was 09:45 to 15:05 long after a prior down session with WFA PF about 1.068 and MAR about 0.068. Both are materially below the default WFA PF/MAR gates.
- Intraday VWAP-dislocation fade/continuation stop-target screen: rejected before implementation. A reduced 5-minute path simulation of VWAP-distance fade and continuation variants, using next-bar entry, current slippage/commission, one or two trades per day, and 16:00 ET or earlier flattening, found no positive family. The best fixed rows were still loss-making; the top broad candidate had about 527 trades, net -18,710, PF 0.621, and MAR -0.072. The WFA selector early-exited on the first 2011-2014 train window with selected PF about 0.510 and MAR -0.234.
- Reopen-to-pre-RTH overnight screen: rejected before implementation under the 16:59:59 ET close / 18:00 ET reopen rule. Entries were allowed only after the 18:00 ET reopen bar, typically 18:05, and exits were around 09:30, so no open position crossed the closed interval. The strongest fixed recent pockets were prior-down long overnight variants with 2021-2022 core PF above 1.4 and MAR above 2.0, but broad WFA-period PF stayed near 1.15-1.20 and MAR near 0.20-0.34. Approximate WFA selection across the close-compliant family stitched only PF 1.044, MAR 0.037, 603 trades, and expectancy R 0.019. Recent incubation pockets were strong but rejected as holdout-unstable.
- Prior-only adaptive intraday ridge screen: rejected before implementation. This online model trained only on samples available before each trade, using current-session features known at the signal bar plus prior-session features, then traded close-compliant RTH windows such as 10:30-12:00, 10:30-15:30, 11:00-15:30, and 12:00-15:30. Best fixed rows still had broad WFA-period MAR below 0.20. The WFA selector did not early-exit but stitched only PF 1.012, MAR 0.011, 801 trades, and expectancy R 0.007. The final selected 2024-2026 incubation pocket was strong, but the prior WFA path was far below the default PF/MAR/expectancy gates, so no staged adaptive module was justified.
- Exact late-session source-strength neighborhood: rejected before implementation. The prior 10:00-to-14:30 source-return lead was retested with an exact narrow 5-minute stop/target neighborhood, long-only entries at 14:30, exits at 15:30 or 16:00 ET, and conservative stop-first bar resolution. Several 2021-2022 core pockets remained strong, but early-history and incubation stability were weak; the approximate WFA selector stitched only PF 0.997, MAR -0.003, 748 trades, and expectancy R 0.007. Because all exits were no later than 16:00 ET, the family was close-compliant but still far below the default WFA gates.
- Overnight high/low breakout continuation screen: rejected before implementation. This was a distinct continuation expression of RTH acceptance beyond completed overnight high/low, not the earlier overnight-inventory fade. It used only no-lookahead overnight high/low, prior RTH close, RTH open gap alignment, and same-day RTH bars; all exits flattened at 15:30 or 16:00 ET, before the 16:59:59 ET futures close. The best fixed core pockets were strong, such as gap-aligned long breaks with 8-12 tick thresholds and 32-48 tick stops to 96-tick targets, but broad-period PF stayed near 1.25-1.38 and MAR below 0.50. A narrowed objective audit over 270 combinations found no WFA pass shape: MAR selection stitched PF 1.186/MAR 0.320/751 trades, PF selection stitched PF 1.290/MAR 0.271/593 trades, and net-profit selection stitched PF 1.255/MAR 0.548/729 trades. Win rate and expectancy R also remained below the default gates, so no staged config was justified.
- `morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/5m/long_only_strength_1655_flatten`: created as a close-compliant sensitivity after the user clarified the 16:59:59 ET close and 18:00 ET reopen. The config entered the existing Gao-style 10:30 long-only morning-continuation signal but flattened on the 16:50 bar close timestamped 16:55 ET, before the daily futures close. Screening command: `PYTHONPATH=src python3 -m propstack.run_campaign_stages --config configs/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/variants/ES/5m/long_only_strength_1655_flatten.yaml --skip-validation`. Result path: `data/reports/campaigns/morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/ES/1m_full_history/5m/long_only_strength_1655_flatten/campaign_tests`. Limited core passed with 100/100 profitable combinations, but limited monkey failed: selected core beat randomized net profit in 82.025% of runs versus 90% required, while max-DD beat rate passed at 96.2125%. Rejected before WFA.

## New Academic Campaign 12 Plan

- Campaign: `volume_conditioned_liquidity_reversal`
- Academic source: Campbell, John Y.; Grossman, Sanford J.; Wang, Jiang (1993), "Trading Volume and Serial Correlation in Stock Returns", Quarterly Journal of Economics 108(4), 905-939, DOI `10.2307/2118454`, Harvard link `https://dash.harvard.edu/entities/publication/73120378-8365-6bd4-e053-0100007fdf3b`.
- Finding used: High-volume price declines are associated with stronger subsequent expected returns, consistent with temporary liquidity pressure and reversal.
- Evidence directness for ES: Indirect. The paper studies equity return-volume dynamics; this campaign translates the thesis to ES intraday futures shocks.
- Apex compliance implementation note: The backtest engine now supports top-level `apex_rules`, latest-entry rejection, pending-signal cancellation, timezone-aware Apex timestamps, forced Apex flattening on the last legal available bar before the configured deadline, and Apex violation counts in metrics and staged criteria.
- Expected working regime: High-volume liquidity shocks that revert during the same RTH session.
- Expected failure regime: Information-driven high-volume trends, strong macro continuation days, and broad markets where simple volume shock fades are too noisy after costs.
- Translation risks: Published evidence is not an ES futures intraday stop/target rule; the campaign uses a compact RTH-only implementation with no more than four tunables.

Apex audit passed with 0 violating iterations; top row had only 2 trades, so it failed trade-count/CAGR and best-day concentration gates. |

Conclusion: Exhausted. The Campbell/Grossman/Wang volume-conditioned reversal thesis did not transfer into a robust ES intraday futures strategy under current costs, sizing, Apex rules, and default staged gates. All nine required configs failed at the first gate, limited core. Apex compliance passed after the engine learned to force-flatten before early-close/reopen gaps and cancel pending next-bar entries whose next actual execution time would be after the latest-entry deadline.

### Candidate Queue Audit After Campaign 12

- Heston, Korajczyk, and Sadka (2010), "Intraday Patterns in the Cross-section of Stock Returns", DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.2010.01573.x`, skipped before implementation. The proposed `same_clock_intraday_return_memory` variants overlap the already rejected adaptive intraday seasonality screen, which tested a no-lookahead rolling same-window return model and found no broad WFA/incubation pass shape. Per the overlap rule, renamed same-window/same-slot return screens are rejected unless new evidence changes the thesis materially.
- Cross-market NQ-to-ES lead/lag screen: rejected before implementation. Source family reviewed: Hasbrouck (2003), "Intraday Price Formation in U.S. Equity Index Markets", Journal of Finance 58, DOI `10.1046/j.1540-6261.2003.00609.x`, and Lo/MacKinlay-style lead-lag cross-autocorrelation evidence. A no-write screen used completed NQ bars as a known-at-signal input and next-bar ES entries with same-day Apex-compatible flattening. Best 30m core rule (`nq_lead_es_lag`, NQ threshold 0.20%, 09:35-11:30 signal, 16:00 flat) had 2021-2022 PF 2.13/MAR 3.09, but full 2011-2026 PF fell to 1.33/MAR 0.17 and 2023-2026 incubation was negative. Best 5m full-history divergence rule had PF 1.57 but only 402 trades and MAR 0.33; the enough-trade 5m version had PF only 1.19. Rejected as a recent/core pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Cross-market ES/NQ relative-value screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Gatev, Goetzmann, and Rouwenhorst (2006), "Pairs Trading: Performance of a Relative-Value Arbitrage Rule", Review of Financial Studies 19(3), 797-827, DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhj020`, Oxford link `https://academic.oup.com/rfs/article/19/3/797/1646694`. A no-write screen traded only ES from next-bar entries using completed ES/NQ RTH cumulative-return spreads as the relative-value signal. Core 2021-2022 had strong late-day pockets, such as 15m NQ-anchor reversion at beta 0.25 / threshold 0.20% with PF 2.21/MAR 3.19 and 90 trades. Full 2011-2026 validation fell to PF 1.32/MAR 0.13 with 473 trades, and the 5m counterpart had PF 1.32/MAR 0.11 with 406 trades. A focused 1-minute stop/target path-management pass across the three strongest rules found no broad managed candidate with adequate full-history and incubation shape. Rejected as a 2021-2022 relative-value pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Realized semivariance directional screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Barndorff-Nielsen, Kinnebrock, and Shephard (2010), "Measuring Downside Risk: Realised Semivariance", Oxford University Press chapter, and Patton/Sheppard "Good Volatility, Bad Volatility" signed-semivariance evidence. A no-write OHLCV-only screen used completed intraday positive/negative realized semivariance shares from the current RTH session and next-bar ES entries. Core 2021-2022 found a strong early good-volatility continuation pocket, for example 30m `good_vol_continuation` with positive-semivariance share >=70%, minimum source move 0.30%, 09:35-10:30 signal, 11:30 flat: PF 1.91/MAR 3.80 with 102 trades. Full 2011-2026 PF collapsed to 1.01/MAR 0.00 and 2023-2026 incubation was negative. The best full-history semivariance row was a 15m 09:35-11:30 to 16:00 hold with PF 1.14/MAR 0.08 and negative incubation. Rejected as a 2021-2022 volatility pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Rolling trading-range breakout screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Brock, Lakonishok, and LeBaron (1992), "Simple Technical Trading Rules and the Stochastic Properties of Stock Returns", Journal of Finance 47(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1992.tb04681.x`, Wiley link `https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1540-6261.1992.tb04681.x`. The no-write screen tested next-bar ES continuation after breakouts from completed rolling intraday ranges, with RTH-only entries and 16:00 ET or earlier flattening. Narrow 2021-2022 core pockets were strong, including 15m lookback 12 / 4-tick buffer / max 24-tick range / 13:00-15:30 signal to 16:00 flat with 140 trades, PF 2.076, and MAR 4.571. Targeted full-history validation rejected the family: the best enough-trade broad row, 5m lookback 12 / 4-tick buffer / max 8-tick range / 09:35-11:30 signal to 16:00 flat, had 1,466 full-history trades but only PF 1.209 and MAR 0.230; its WFA-style period had PF 1.138 and MAR 0.184. Other targeted rows either had PF near 1.0, negative incubation, too few trades, or WFA-style PF/MAR far below the 1.5 gates. Rejected as a recent/core breakout pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Round-number clustered-order screen: rejected before implementation. Sources reviewed: Osler (2003), "Currency Orders and Exchange-Rate Dynamics: An Explanation for the Predictive Success of Technical Analysis", Journal of Finance 58(5), DOI `10.1111/1540-6261.00588`, and Schwartz, Van Ness, and Van Ness (2004), "Clustering in the futures market: Evidence from S&P 500 futures contracts", Journal of Futures Markets 24(5), DOI `10.1002/fut.10129`. A no-write ES-only screen tested next-bar reversal and breakout behavior around 50- and 100-point round numbers, with one trade per day and same-day RTH exits. The best 2021-2022 core pocket was a 5m 50-point breakout continuation from 13:00-15:30, held 60 minutes, with 223 trades, PF 1.445, and MAR 2.116. The same fixed row failed outside the core window: 2011-2020 had 473 trades, PF 0.653, MAR -0.100, and net -32,682.50; 2023-2026 had 390 trades, PF 0.976, MAR -0.042, and net -2,962.50. Rejected as a 2021-2022 round-number breakout pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Leveraged-ETF/end-of-day rebalancing-flow screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Barbon and coauthors, "Liquidity Provision to Leveraged ETFs and Equity Options Rebalancing Flows" (working paper; formerly "The Role of Leveraged ETFs and Option Market Imbalances on End-of-Day Price Dynamics"), stable URL `https://www.abarbon.com/papers/liquidity-provision-to-leveraged-etfs-and-equity-options-rebalancing-flows`. The no-write ES-only translation traded same-direction late-day ES continuation after large same-day RTH moves, with entries around 14:30-15:30 and exits no later than 15:55 ET. Core 2021-2022 had positive pockets, including 15:30 same-direction after at least 64 ticks of same-day movement to a 15:55 exit with 283 trades, PF 1.343, and MAR 1.829. The same row was flat in 2011-2020 with 448 trades, PF 1.004, MAR 0.003, and net 317.50, then negative in 2023-2026 with 504 trades, PF 0.726, MAR -0.285, and net -30,560. Other nearby rows, such as 15:30/48 ticks and 14:30/48 ticks, were likewise weak or negative outside the 2021-2022 core. Rejected as a recent late-day flow pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Adjacent-contract short-term basis reversal screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Rossi, Zhang, and Zhu (2025/2026), "Short-Term Basis Reversal", SSRN `https://ssrn.com/abstract=5250499`, DOI `10.2139/ssrn.5250499`. The source thesis is relative-value reversal in return spreads between adjacent futures maturities. Local raw Databento data include multiple ES maturities, so the no-write screen used the roll calendar to map the active front contract and next adjacent maturity. As an outright front-contract ES proxy, the strongest 2021-2022 core rows were promising, including 5m / 20-minute spread lookback / 09:35-15:30 signal / zero threshold / 120-minute hold with 508 trades, PF 1.438, MAR 2.962, and net 70,492.50. The same fixed row failed 2011-2020 with 2,513 trades, PF 0.881, MAR -0.104, and net -47,895, and was roughly flat-negative in 2023-2026 with 866 trades, PF 0.992, MAR -0.021, and net -2,852.50. A faithful paired calendar-spread version, with one front leg and one adjacent-maturity leg, next-bar entries, same-day exits, and double commissions/slippage, found zero 2021-2022 core rows with at least 60 trades and PF above 1.05. Rejected both as an ES outright proxy and as a practical intraday ES calendar-spread candidate.
- CFTC/TFF trader-position sentiment screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Chen and Maher (2013), "On the predictive role of large futures trades for S&P500 index returns: An analysis of COT data as an informative trading signal", Journal of International Financial Markets, Institutions and Money 27, DOI `10.1016/j.intfin.2013.09.004`, plus Smales (2016), "Trading behavior in S&P 500 index futures", Review of Financial Economics 28, DOI `10.1016/j.rfe.2015.11.001`. The no-write screen used official CFTC TFF futures-only data (`gpe5-46if`) for E-mini S&P 500 code `13874A`, conservatively making each Tuesday report tradable only from the following Monday session. The best fixed daily rule was long ES from 10:00 to 16:00 after a positive 26-week z-score shock in Other Reportables' net position (`other_chg_z26 >= 0.50`): 1,077 trades, full PF 1.275/MAR 0.555, 2021-2022 core PF 1.683/MAR 3.238, WFA-period PF 1.304/MAR 0.748 with 587 trades, and 2023-2026 incubation PF 1.328/MAR 1.022. A focused 1-minute path-management screen over the same family with percent stops and fixed-R targets improved some pockets but produced no approximate pass candidate; the best managed row was 11:00 to 16:00 with `stop_pct=0.0045` and `target_r=4.0`, WFA PF 1.393/MAR 0.747/expectancy R 0.142, incubation PF 1.216/MAR 1.000/expectancy R 0.106. Rejected because public weekly COT/TFF information did not reach the default WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates after current ES costs and close-compliant same-day exits.
- Prior-day implied-volatility regime screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Giot (2005), "Relationships Between Implied Volatility Indexes and Stock Index Returns", Journal of Portfolio Management 31(3), DOI `10.3905/jpm.2005.500363`, and official Cboe daily history for VIX/VIX9D/VIX3M/VVIX. The no-write screen used only volatility-index values available after the prior cash-session close, then traded same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Features included VIX level z-scores/ranks, one-day and five-day VIX shocks, VIX/VIX3M and VIX9D/VIX term-structure ratios, VVIX z-score, and optional prior-ES-down/up filters. Best fixed rows were holdout-skewed rather than WFA-pass-shaped: for example `vix9d_vix_z63` two-sided continuation after a prior down RTH session from 10:30 to 12:00 had 1,092 trades, full PF 1.229/MAR 0.216, core PF 1.450/MAR 1.829, WFA PF 1.145/MAR 0.177 with 579 trades, and incubation PF 1.588/MAR 2.283. The strongest WFA rows were still only around PF 1.26/MAR 0.49, with no near-pass rows meeting broad WFA plus incubation shape. Rejected as a 2023-2026 volatility-regime pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Volatility-filtered late-session source-return continuation screen: rejected before implementation under the overlap rule. This was a targeted audit of the previously rejected late-session return family that had one isolated WFA PF-above-1.5 fixed row but failed incubation. The no-write screen combined completed ES source returns such as 09:35/10:00 to 13:30/14:30 with prior-day VIX/VIX9D/VIX3M/VVIX filters from the Giot-style implied-volatility thesis, then entered at the source-window end and flattened by 15:30 or 16:00 ET. Best balanced fixed row was 09:35 to 13:30 long-only continuation after at least 6 ES points, filtered by prior VIX one-day shock z-score <= 1.0, entered 13:30 and exited 15:30: 1,034 trades, full PF 1.322/MAR 0.364, core PF 2.032/MAR 2.946, WFA PF 1.452/MAR 0.661 with 550 trades, and incubation PF 1.327/MAR 0.859. A focused 1-minute stop/target path screen on the strongest fixed rows did not produce an approximate pass; rows with WFA PF above 1.5 remained incubation-failed, such as 10:00 to 13:30 two-sided continuation after 12 points with VIX shock z <= 1.0 and `stop_pct=0.0100`, `target_r=1.25`, which had WFA PF 1.562/MAR 0.999 but incubation PF 0.962/MAR -0.086. Stable long-only path rows stayed below WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates, with the best scoring long row around WFA PF 1.400/MAR 0.935/expectancy R 0.058. Rejected as a volatility-conditioned rename of a failed late-session source-return edge, not a new staged campaign.
- Prior-day SKEW/tail-risk regime screen: rejected before implementation. Source family reviewed: Suh (2021), "Stock market tail risk, tail risk premia, and return predictability", Journal of Futures Markets, DOI `10.1002/fut.22226`, plus Cboe's official SKEW/implied-correlation/dispersion index histories. A no-write screen used only prior available Cboe daily values for SKEW, COR3M, DSPX, VIX, and VIX3M, then traded same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Best fixed row was long ES from 10:30 to 15:30 after prior ES down days when prior SKEW 126-day rank was at least 0.8: 401 full-history trades, full PF 1.376/MAR 0.255, core PF 1.050/MAR 0.076, WFA-period PF 1.421/MAR 0.439 with 284 trades, and incubation PF 1.735/MAR 1.279 with 115 trades. The approximate WFA selector over the strongest rows early-exited on window 1 because the selected 2011-2014 train PF was 0.939, below the 1.0 early-exit floor; net-profit selection found no train candidate with the 60-trades/year minimum. Rejected as an incubation-skewed tail-risk regime pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Variance-risk-premium regime screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Bollerslev, Tauchen, and Zhou (2009), "Expected Stock Returns and Variance Risk Premia", Review of Financial Studies 22(11), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhp008`. The no-write screen computed prior-session tradable variance risk premium as prior Cboe VIX implied variance minus rolling ES realized variance, plus implied/realized variance ratios, then traded same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Best fixed row was short ES from 10:00 to 15:30 after prior ES up days when the 21-day implied/realized variance ratio z-score was at least 0.5: 447 full-history trades, full PF 1.374/MAR 0.239, core PF 1.574/MAR 0.480, WFA-period PF 1.431/MAR 0.335 with 312 trades, and incubation PF 1.638/MAR 1.582 with 130 trades. Other high-scoring rows were similar: incubation-positive but WFA MAR, expectancy, and trade count stayed below default gates. Approximate WFA selection early-exited on window 1 because the selected 2011-2014 train PF was 0.731, below the 1.0 early-exit floor; net-profit selection found no train candidate with the 60-trades/year minimum. Rejected as a holdout-skewed VRP regime pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Prior-session illiquidity regime screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Amihud (2002), "Illiquidity and Stock Returns: Cross-Section and Time-Series Effects", Journal of Financial Markets 5(1), DOI `10.1016/S1386-4181(01)00024-6`. The no-write screen computed prior-session ES price-impact proxies from absolute return per notional volume, range per volume, volume rank, range rank, and absolute-return rank, then traded same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Best fixed row was long ES from 09:35 to 15:30 after prior ES down days with prior 63-day volume rank at least 0.8: 571 full-history trades, full PF 1.309/MAR 0.180, core PF 1.308/MAR 0.886, WFA-period PF 1.167/MAR 0.126 with 375 trades, and incubation PF 1.991/MAR 1.986 with 128 trades. Other rows showed the same pattern: 2023-2026 incubation strength but weak WFA-period PF/MAR and low train-window density. Approximate WFA selection found no window-1 train candidate meeting the 60-trades/year minimum. Rejected as another incubation-skewed liquidity/volume pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Signed-volume/order-imbalance screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Chordia and Subrahmanyam (2004), "Order Imbalance and Individual Stock Returns: Theory and Evidence", Journal of Financial Economics 72(3), DOI `10.1016/S0304-405X(03)00175-2`. The no-write ES translation approximated order imbalance from completed 1-minute bars before entry using signed volume, buy/sell volume ratio, source-window return, and source-window range, then traded same-session RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The best fixed row was long ES from 11:00 to 15:30 after positive source returns with a low 63-day rank of completed source range: 402 full-history trades, full PF 1.291/MAR 0.282, core PF 2.372/MAR 3.125, WFA-period PF 1.575/MAR 0.529 with only 258 trades, and incubation PF 1.100/MAR 0.210 with 99 trades. Higher-trade rows had WFA PF around 1.23-1.36 and MAR well below 1.0. Approximate WFA selection found no window-1 train candidate meeting the 60-trades/year minimum. Rejected as a low-density 2021-2022 order-flow/range pocket, not a staged candidate.
- Cboe put/call option-volume sentiment screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Pan and Poteshman (2006), "The Information in Option Volume for Future Stock Prices", Review of Financial Studies 19(3), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhj024`, plus Cboe total/index/equity/ETP/VIX put/call-ratio archives and dated Cboe daily market-statistics pages. The no-write ES translation used only prior-day Cboe ratio features available before the next RTH session, then traded one separated same-day ES RTH window with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Corrected parsing loaded 3,253 archive rows for total/index/equity/ETP ratios through 2019-10-04, 3,427 VIX-ratio rows, and 1,670 post-archive dated daily pages through 2026-05-29, including SPX+SPXW ratios. A first pass accidentally aggregated overlapping windows and was discarded. The corrected separated-window pass found no near candidate with WFA trade count >=500. Best valid row was long ES from 13:30 to 16:00 after a prior ES down session when VIX put/call 63-day z-score was <= -0.5: 616 full-history trades, full PF 1.609/MAR 5.372, WFA-period PF 1.753/MAR 9.145 with 390 trades, and incubation PF 2.452/MAR 7.022 with 129 trades, but the 2021-2022 core pocket failed at PF 0.968/MAR -0.110 and WFA trade count missed the 500-trade gate. Other high-WFA-PF rows were similar low-density or incubation/core-skewed late-session pockets. Approximate WFA selection over the strongest separated rows found no first-window train candidate meeting the 60-trades/year minimum. Rejected because valid non-overlapping option-volume sentiment translations did not satisfy the default WFA trade-count and core robustness gates after current ES costs and close-compliant same-day exits.
- Prior-session realized higher-moment / return-rank screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Amaya, Christoffersen, Jacobs, and Vasquez (2015), "Does realized skewness predict the cross-section of equity returns?", Journal of Financial Economics 118(1), DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2015.02.009`. The no-write ES translation computed only completed prior-session realized moments and path-shape features from 1-minute RTH bars: realized skewness, kurtosis, realized variance, positive-variance share, extreme 1-minute returns, range, close location, and prior RTH return ranks/z-scores. The strongest screened row was not a skewness effect but a prior-session downside reversal proxy: long ES from 11:00 to 15:30 after prior RTH return ranked in the bottom 20% of its 21-day history. Flat-hold 15m results were 795 full-history trades, full PF 1.441/MAR 6.900, 2021-2022 core PF 1.253/MAR 1.284, 2011-2020 PF 1.510/MAR 6.116 with 509 trades, and 2023-2026 incubation PF 1.482/MAR 3.197 with 159 trades. A direct annual OOS audit from 2015 through 2026 fell below the real WFA stitched gates at PF 1.456, MAR 6.182, expectancy R 0.184, and 557 trades; 2022, 2023, and partial-2026 were negative. A focused 1-minute stop/target path check around the best prior-down bottom-20%-rank candidate, with entries at 10:00/10:30/11:00, exits at 15:30/16:00, stops from 0.20% to 0.70%, and targets from 1R to 5R, found zero managed rows meeting WFA PF >=1.5 and expectancy R >=0.2 while preserving incubation/core gates.
