Rejected as an overlap with the already rejected prior-session reversal family; the added realized-moment features did not produce a distinct pass-shaped edge.
- Europe-to-US international transmission screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lin, Engle, and Ito (1994), "Do bulls and bears move across borders? International transmission of stock returns and volatility", Review of Financial Studies 7(3), DOI `10.1093/rfs/7.3.507`. The no-write ES translation used same-day European cash-index daily returns from DAX, Euro Stoxx 50, FTSE 100, and CAC 40, with ES entries only at or after 13:30 ET so the European cash close was already known. Features included same-day open-to-close and close-to-close returns, rolling z-scores, rolling ranks, and a four-index Europe average. Best separated row was long ES from 13:30 to 15:30 after DAX same-day close-to-close return ranked in the bottom 20% of its 21-day history: 749 full-history trades, full PF 1.308/MAR 3.999, 2021-2022 core PF 1.574/MAR 2.749, stitched 2015-2026 PF 1.330/MAR 3.784/expectancy R 0.153 with 557 trades, and incubation PF 1.403/MAR 3.328/expectancy R 0.194. Other rows were weaker; the only rows near stitched expectancy had poor core or incubation. No candidate met the WFA PF >=1.5 and expectancy R >=0.2 shape, and approximate WFA selection found no first-window train candidate meeting the 60-trades/year minimum. Rejected because the international-transmission signal was directionally plausible but too weak after ES costs and close-compliant late-session exits.
- Prior-day cross-asset credit/risk-appetite proxy screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Chen, Roll, and Ross (1986), "Economic Forces and the Stock Market", Journal of Business 59(3), 383-403, DOI `10.1086/296344`. The no-write ES translation used prior-day liquid ETF proxy returns, ranks, z-scores, and spreads for credit (`HYG`, `LQD`), duration (`TLT`, `IEF`, `SHY`), safe-haven/real-asset proxies (`GLD`, `UUP`, `USO`), and combinations such as credit/duration and dollar/gold risk appetite. Signals were known before the next RTH session and traded one separated ES window with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The best balanced rows were short ES from 09:35 to 15:30 after strong prior-dollar conditions (`prior_UUP_ret_rank126 >= 0.8`): 798 full-history trades, full PF 1.299/MAR 7.075, 2021-2022 core PF 1.227/MAR 1.325/expectancy R 0.098, stitched 2015-2026 PF 1.367/MAR 7.548/expectancy R 0.176 with 589 trades, and incubation PF 1.388/MAR 4.390/expectancy R 0.178. No row reached the WFA PF >=1.5 and expectancy R >=0.2 gates while preserving core/incubation shape. Approximate WFA selectors over the strongest rows early-exited immediately; the first selected OOS slice had only 63 trades and PF about 0.652 with negative MAR. Rejected because macro/credit/risk-appetite ETF proxies remained too weak after ES costs and close-compliant same-day exits.
- Overnight/pre-open ES/NQ price-discovery screen: rejected before implementation. Source family reviewed previously under Hasbrouck (2003) intraday index-market price discovery. The no-write screen used full active-contract ES and NQ Databento caches and allowed only information known before or at the ES RTH open: ES/NQ overnight return, open gap, Asia segment, Europe/pre-open segment, NQ-minus-ES relative moves, and prior-session RTH return. A first scratch pass was discarded because it accidentally included same-day RTH open-to-close return as a morning-entry feature; the corrected pass shifted RTH return to prior session only. Corrected top fixed rows with strong WFA metrics were holdout failures: for example long ES from 11:00 to 15:30 after top-quintile 63-day ES overnight/gap rank had WFA PF about 1.60 and 525 trades, but 2021-2022 core PF was about 0.91 and 2023-2026 incubation PF was about 0.92. The best broad prior-session-reversal row, long ES after weak prior RTH return, reached WFA PF around 1.92-2.06 in some fixed rows but failed incubation near PF 0.74-0.88, and overlaps the already rejected prior-session reversal family. Approximate WFA selection over the near rows stitched only PF about 1.38, MAR about 5.26, expectancy R about 0.155, and 431 trades, below the default PF/expectancy/trade-count gates. Rejected as either a core/incubation-failed overnight pocket or a renamed prior-session reversal edge.
- Prior-day sector-rotation / industry-momentum screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Moskowitz and Grinblatt (1999), "Do Industries Explain Momentum?", Journal of Finance 54(4), 1249-1290, DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00146`. The no-write ES translation used prior-day Yahoo daily sector ETF data (`XLK`, `XLF`, `XLY`, `XLP`, `XLI`, `XLE`, `XLV`, `XLU`, `XLB`, `IYR`, `SPY`) to build one-day and five-day sector returns, sector-minus-SPY relative returns, cyclical-minus-defensive spreads, breadth, rolling ranks, and rolling z-scores. All inputs were merged only from completed prior ETF closes before the ES RTH session, then traded one separated ES RTH window with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The best fixed rows were concentrated in defensive-sector relative weakness/strength filters, especially `XLP_rel_spy5` and `XLU_rel_spy5`: some rows had WFA PF around 1.55-1.80 and incubation PF above 1.5, but many failed the 2021-2022 core window, such as `XLP_rel_spy5_rank63 <= 0.2` with prior ES up: core PF about 0.73 despite WFA PF about 1.76 and incubation PF about 1.55. Approximate WFA selection over the near rows did not meet gates: stitched PF about 1.39, MAR about 4.36, expectancy R about 0.165, win rate about 57.5%, and only 468 trades. A later bounded overlap rerun, `/private/tmp/sector_risk_rotation_narrow.py`, wrote `/private/tmp/sector_risk_rotation_narrow_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/sector_risk_rotation_narrow_all.csv`; it tested 11,396 prior-day sector-risk rows with zero pass-shaped and zero near rows, with top rows again below WFA/incubation density. Rejected because sector-rotation information was directionally useful in places but not strong or dense enough for the default WFA PF/expectancy/trade-count gates after ES costs.
- Prior-session volume-profile reference-level screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Blume, Easley, and O'Hara (1994), "Market Statistics and Technical Analysis: The Role of Volume", Journal of Finance 49(1), 153-181, DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1994.tb04424.x`. The no-write ES translation computed completed prior-session volume-profile references from RTH 1-minute bars only: prior VWAP, one-point-binned POC, 70% value-area high/low, profile width/range, POC volume share, close-to-POC/VWAP distance, and current RTH open location versus those prior references. Best profile-specific fixed rows were not WFA-pass-shaped. For example, long ES from 11:00 to 15:30 after a large open below prior value-area high and prior down session reached full PF about 1.73 and incubation PF about 3.49, but WFA-period PF was only about 1.20. Rows with WFA PF above 1.8 usually reduced to the already rejected prior-session downside reversal family and failed 2023-2026 incubation, such as prior RTH return z21 <= -0.5 with open above prior POC. Approximate WFA selection over the near rows again chose plain prior-session return reversal and stitched only PF about 1.38, MAR about 5.26, expectancy R about 0.155, and 431 trades. Rejected because prior volume-profile levels did not add a distinct, robust ES edge beyond the failed prior-session reversal mechanic.
- Same-day Asia-to-US international-transmission screen: rejected before implementation. Source family reviewed previously under Lin, Engle, and Ito (1994), "Do bulls and bears move across borders? International transmission of stock returns and volatility", Review of Financial Studies 7(3), DOI `10.1093/rfs/7.3.507`. The no-write ES translation used Yahoo daily cash-index closes for Nikkei, Hang Seng, Shanghai Composite, KOSPI, TAIEX, and ASX signals that should be known before or during the US RTH session, then traded one separated close-compliant ES window with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Two initial scratch passes were discarded because New York-date and UTC-date alignment could shift Asian exchange trading days, especially ASX. The valid pass aligned each cash index by its own local exchange date before merging to the ES trade date. Top fixed rows were holdout failures: a Nikkei 5-day z-score downside-reversal short from 13:30 to 16:00 after prior ES up had WFA PF about 1.82 but 2021-2022 core PF about 0.85 and incubation PF about 1.42; KOSPI late shorts had WFA strength but core PF around 0.58-0.67. A Shanghai bottom/top-rank row had broad PF around 1.56 and decent holdout shape but only 475 full-history trades, below the density gate. The best approximate WFA selector over the near rows stitched only PF about 1.40, MAR about 5.61, expectancy R about 0.176, win rate about 56.2%, and 420 trades. Rejected because valid Asia cash-index transmission was directionally plausible but did not meet WFA PF/expectancy/trade-count gates after current ES costs and close-compliant same-day exits.
- Weekly initial-jobless-claims macro-news screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Xu and You (2025), "Main Street's Pain, Wall Street's Gain", Journal of Financial Economics 168, plus Boyd, Hu, and Jagannathan (2005), "The Stock Market's Reaction to Unemployment News: Why Bad News Is Usually Good for Stocks", Journal of Finance 60(2), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.2005.00742.x`. The no-write ES translation treated weekly initial claims as an 08:30 ET scheduled labor-market announcement and used only release-day signals available after the release. A first pass used the American Default FRED/DOL mirror as a provisional data source; because that mirror may contain revised claims values, any pass would have required replacement with unrevised ETA-538 data before acceptance. Both post-release pre-RTH reaction windows and RTH continuation windows were weak. Best broad rows such as claims-change "good news" from 09:35 to 13:30 reached only WFA PF about 1.12, MAR about 0.08, expectancy R about 0.056, and 575 trades, despite 2021-2022 core PF about 1.51. Release-reaction windows were similarly weak: the best 09:35-10:00 z-score row had WFA PF about 1.14 and expectancy R about 0.074. Rejected because weekly labor news did not produce a stable cost-adjusted ES intraday edge, and no result was strong enough to justify solving the unrevised ETA-538 ingestion.
- Fama-French cross-sectional factor spillover screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Fama and French (2015), "A five-factor asset pricing model", Journal of Financial Economics 116(1), DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2014.10.010`; data came from the Kenneth French daily factor library and was shifted one trading day before ES entries. The no-write ES translation tested prior completed SMB, HML, RMW, CMA, and simple factor-spread ranks/z-scores as cross-sectional risk-factor spillovers into next-session ES RTH holds. The strongest flat-hold family was long ES after weak prior SMB factor readings: `SMB_1d_rank126 <= 0.2`, 09:35-16:00, had 798 full-history trades, full PF about 1.30, 2021-2022 core PF about 1.42, WFA-period PF about 1.33/expectancy R about 0.157 with 571 trades, and incubation PF about 1.83. A focused 1-minute stop/target path screen over the strongest SMB/HML definitions did not improve the pass shape; best managed WFA PF stayed around 1.38 with expectancy R about 0.165 and MAR below 0.40, and other definitions were weaker. Rejected because factor spillovers were directionally useful but below the WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates after current ES costs.
- 52-week-high anchoring / momentum screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: George and Hwang (2004), "The 52-Week High and Momentum Investing", Journal of Finance 59(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.2004.00695.x`, plus index-return evidence under Malin and Bornholt (2010), "Predictability of future index returns based on the 52-week high strategy". The no-write ES translation used only completed prior RTH closes and prior 252-session high/low anchors, then traded next-session RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Enough-trade high-anchor rows failed broad validation: `h52_rank252 >= 0.8` long from 11:00 to 16:00 had 868 full-history trades, WFA PF about 1.09, MAR about 0.08, and incubation PF about 1.01; high-anchor short rows were near flat. Low-anchor rows had small pockets but were too sparse for WFA density, such as `l52_ratio <= 1.1` long from 13:30 to 16:00 with only 271 WFA-period trades and WFA PF about 1.11. Rejected because the ES translation collapsed into weak long-term trend/anchor exposure and did not meet trade-count-adjusted WFA economics.
- Cross-sectional momentum/reversal factor spillover screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Jegadeesh and Titman-style cross-sectional momentum and short-term reversal factor evidence, using the Kenneth French daily momentum, short-term reversal, and long-term reversal factor libraries shifted one trading day before ES entries. The no-write ES translation tested whether completed prior factor strength or reversal pressure spilled into next-session ES RTH. The strongest flat-hold family was long ES after top-quintile prior 5-day short-term reversal factor: `ST_REV_5d_rank126 >= 0.8`, 09:35-15:30, with 832 full-history trades, full PF about 1.34/MAR about 0.39/expectancy R about 0.149, 2021-2022 core PF about 1.15 but expectancy R only about 0.068, WFA-period PF about 1.37/MAR about 0.53/expectancy R about 0.164 with 599 trades, and incubation PF about 1.47/MAR about 1.27/expectancy R about 0.202. A focused 1-minute stop/target path screen over the ST-reversal near-misses did not improve the WFA shape; best managed rows stayed around WFA PF 1.31 with core expectancy near zero or weaker. Rejected because the factor branch remained below WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates and core economics were too weak to promote.
- Scheduled macro-announcement premium screen: rejected before implementation. Sources reviewed: Savor and Wilson (2013), "How Much Do Investors Care About Macroeconomic Risk? Evidence from Scheduled Economic Announcements", Journal of Financial and Quantitative Analysis 48(2), DOI `10.1017/S002210901300015X`, and Wachter and Zhu (2018), "A Model of Two Days: Discrete News and Asset Prices", NBER Working Paper 24432, DOI `10.3386/w24432`. The no-write ES translation used exact FOMC dates from the Federal Reserve calendar plus provisional employment/inflation announcement proxies after BLS schedule pages blocked shell retrieval: employment was the first Friday of each month, and inflation proxies were the first business day on or after the 10th and 14th. Event sets were sparse for exact FOMC (44 days), employment (204 days), inflation proxies (408 days), and combined macro sets (653 days). The only strong-looking rows were too sparse, such as `employment_first_friday` long from 11:00 to 15:30 with full PF about 1.36, WFA PF about 1.45, expectancy R about 0.18, but only 128 WFA-period trades. Broader announcement baskets were weak: `savor_core_macro` long from 11:00 to 15:30 reached only WFA PF about 1.15, MAR near zero, expectancy R about 0.07, and 433 WFA-period trades; `macro_no_fomc` long from 11:00 to 16:00 reached about WFA PF 1.21 and expectancy R 0.09 with 392 trades. Rejected at the pre-screen density/economics gate because event-only scheduled macro exposure cannot reach the 500-trade WFA gate without broadening into weak baskets, and no result justified exact BLS-date ingestion.
- Market-breadth participation screen: rejected before implementation at the data-source gate. Source reviewed: Zaremba, Szyszka, Karathanasopoulos, and Mikutowski (2021), "Herding for profits: Market breadth and the cross-section of global equity returns", Economic Modelling 97, DOI `10.1016/j.econmod.2020.04.006`. The intended no-write ES translation used prior-day index participation breadth, such as advance-minus-decline share and percentages of stocks above moving averages, then traded same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Yahoo Finance did not expose usable historical market-breadth index series (`^ADVN`, `^DECN`, `^UVOL`, and related symbols returned 404 or zero rows), and a current-S&P-500 constituent reconstruction was rate-limited for all 503 names and would have been survivorship-biased even if it downloaded. Rejected before screening because the accessible data path was not robust enough to support a valid Apex acceptance candidate.
- News-based economic-policy-uncertainty screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Baker, Bloom, and Davis (2016), "Measuring Economic Policy Uncertainty", Quarterly Journal of Economics 131(4), DOI `10.1093/qje/qjw024`; daily data came from `policyuncertainty.com/media/All_Daily_Policy_Data.csv` and was shifted so only values dated before the ES session were used. The no-write ES translation tested prior EPU levels, shocks, percent changes, rolling sums, z-scores, and ranks against same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The strongest dense row was a low-EPU-sum long from 13:30 to 16:00 (`epu_sum5_rank21 <= 0.1`) with 510 full-history trades, full PF about 1.42, WFA PF about 1.44/MAR about 0.32/expectancy R about 0.20 with 377 WFA trades, and incubation PF about 1.85/MAR about 0.95 with 109 trades. Other rows with WFA PF above 1.5, such as long after a low 10-day EPU percent-change z-score, had only 336-348 WFA trades. Rejected because the family either missed the 500-trade WFA density gate or, when dense enough, fell well short of the WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates.
- Daily news-sentiment screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Shapiro, Sudhof, and Wilson (2020), "Measuring News Sentiment", FRB San Francisco Working Paper 2017-01, plus Buckman, Shapiro, Sudhof, and Wilson (2020), "News Sentiment in the Time of COVID-19"; data came from the San Francisco Fed Daily News Sentiment Index Excel file and was parsed directly from the XLSX XML, then shifted so only values dated before the ES session were used. The no-write ES translation tested prior news-sentiment levels, changes, rolling means, z-scores, and ranks against same-day ES RTH long/short windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Flat-hold screening produced the strongest new near-miss: low 21-day sentiment rank (`sent_mean21_rank252 <= 0.1`) long from 09:35 to 16:00 had 624 full-history trades, full PF about 1.42/MAR about 0.30/expectancy R about 0.18, 2021-2022 core PF about 1.94/MAR about 4.95, WFA-period PF about 1.49/MAR about 0.46/expectancy R about 0.21 with 512 trades, and incubation PF about 1.52/MAR about 0.83 with 115 trades. A lower-density sentiment-change row (`sent_chg5_rank21 <= 0.1`, 11:00 to 15:30) reached WFA PF about 1.57 and expectancy R about 0.24 but had only 336 WFA trades. A focused 1-minute stop/target path-management screen over the strongest sentiment rules did not improve the pass shape; conservative stop-first fills pushed the best managed WFA rows below PF 1.05 and most were loss-making. A same-thesis multi-slot audit increased trade density but compressed the edge; the original single 09:35-16:00 low-sentiment hold remained the strongest WFA profile, while multi-slot rows stayed below WFA PF/MAR gates. Rejected because the flat-hold edge missed WFA MAR and incubation MAR by a wide margin, while path management and multi-slot densification did not improve robustness.
- Rates-volatility / stock-bond linkage screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Fleming, Kirby, and Ostdiek (1998), "Information and volatility linkages in the stock, bond, and money markets", Journal of Financial Economics 49(1), DOI `10.1016/S0304-405X(98)00019-1`. The no-write ES translation used prior-day Yahoo daily values for the ICE BofA MOVE index (`^MOVE`), Treasury yield proxies (`^TNX`, `^TYX`), bond/credit ETFs (`TLT`, `IEF`, `HYG`, `LQD`), and the dollar index, then tested levels, returns, changes, ranks, z-scores, and simple spreads against same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The strongest high-PF rows were too sparse, such as low 5-day MOVE-return rank (`MOVE_ret5_rank21 <= 0.1`) long from 09:35 to 16:00 with WFA PF about 1.87 and expectancy R about 0.39 but only 278 WFA trades. Dense MOVE rows were directionally useful but not pass-shaped: `MOVE_ret5_rank252 <= 0.2` long from 13:30 to 16:00 had 737 full-history trades, WFA PF about 1.41/MAR about 0.34/expectancy R about 0.19 with 546 WFA trades, and incubation PF about 2.00/MAR about 1.07 with 166 trades. A focused 1-minute stop/target path-management screen on dense MOVE/Treasury rows failed; conservative stop-first fills pushed the best managed WFA rows below PF 1.0. A same-thesis multi-slot audit densified sparse low-MOVE rows above the 500-trade WFA gate, but the best two-slot row (`MOVE_ret5_rank21 <= 0.1`, 09:35-12:00 plus 14:30-15:30) still reached only WFA PF about 1.65 and MAR about 0.54, far below the MAR gate. Rejected because rates-volatility information was economically plausible but could not meet the WFA PF/MAR gates after current ES costs, and ETF/rates rows overlapped the previously rejected cross-asset risk-appetite branch without improving it.
- Cross-asset option-volatility spillover screen: rejected before implementation under the volatility-overlap rule. Source family reviewed under Fleming, Kirby, and Ostdiek (1998) volatility-linkage evidence and the already rejected Giot-style implied-volatility regime branch. The no-write ES translation used prior-day Yahoo daily values for `^VIX`, `^VXN`, `^OVX`, `^GVZ`, `^EVZ`, and `^VVIX`, then tested levels, returns, spreads, ratios, z-scores, and ranks against same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. High-PF rows were again too sparse or holdout-skewed, such as low 5-day GVZ-return rank with WFA PF above 1.5 but only about 262 WFA trades. The best dense rows did not improve on the rejected VIX/MOVE shapes: `VVIX_ret5_rank252 <= 0.2` long from 13:30 to 15:30 had 771 full-history trades, full PF about 1.29, core PF about 2.04, WFA PF about 1.45/MAR about 0.42/expectancy R about 0.20 with 550 WFA trades, and incubation PF about 1.82/MAR about 1.41 with 164 trades. Rejected because the non-equity/Nasdaq vol additions remained below the WFA PF and MAR gates and did not create a distinct non-overlapping edge.
- Baker-Wurgler / credit-market sentiment data audit: rejected before implementation at the data-horizon gate. Source reviewed: Baker and Wurgler (2006), "Investor Sentiment and the Cross-Section of Stock Returns", Journal of Finance 61(4), plus Greenwood and Hanson-style high-yield-share credit sentiment data hosted by Harvard Business School. The HBS workbook `InvestorCreditSentiment.xlsx` was accessible and parsable as XLSX XML, but its monthly sentiment sheets ended at September/December 2015 and the page notes the current Baker-Wurgler version was updated in April 2019. Because the source cannot provide valid inputs for the required 2023-2026 simulated incubation period, no ES screen was run and the source is not an acceptance candidate without a newer point-in-time dataset.
- Consumer-confidence sentiment screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lemmon and Portniaguina (2006), "Consumer Confidence and Asset Prices: Some Empirical Evidence", Review of Financial Studies 19(4), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhj038`. A provisional no-write pre-screen used an eco3min monthly consumer-sentiment CSV through April 2026, conservatively making each monthly value tradable only from the following calendar month; any pass would still have required official release-date and vintage reconstruction before acceptance. The ES translation tested prior monthly sentiment levels, changes, percent changes, z-scores, and ranks against same-day RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Best rows were not close to the default gates: `sent_chg1_z12 <= -1.0` long from 13:30 to 15:30 had 650 full-history trades but only WFA PF about 1.27/MAR about 0.27/expectancy R about 0.126 with 500 WFA trades, despite incubation PF about 1.69/MAR about 1.23. The strongest sparse row, `sent_chg1_z60 <= -1.0` long from 13:30 to 15:30, reached WFA PF about 1.43/MAR about 0.36 with only 354 WFA trades. Rejected because monthly consumer-confidence state did not provide enough WFA PF/MAR/expectancy after costs, and the data path was provisional.
- Geopolitical-risk news index screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Caldara and Iacoviello (2022), "Measuring Geopolitical Risk", American Economic Review 112(4), DOI `10.1257/aer.20191823`; data came from the authors' current daily GPR Excel file and was shifted so only prior-day GPR values were used before the ES RTH session. The no-write ES translation tested GPR level, threat, act, moving-average, article-count, shock, rank, and z-score features against same-day RTH long/short windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Flat-hold screening produced dense near-misses but no pass: `n10d_mean5_rank21 >= 0.9` long from 09:35 to 16:00 had 721 full-history trades, WFA PF about 1.49/MAR about 0.52/expectancy R about 0.218 with 510 WFA trades, but core PF was only about 1.19. A cleaner GPR-act row, `gprd_act_chg21_z21 <= -1.0` long from 11:00 to 15:30, had 731 full-history trades, core PF about 1.61, WFA PF about 1.44/MAR about 0.34/expectancy R about 0.202 with 513 WFA trades, and incubation PF about 1.89/MAR about 1.43. A focused 1-minute stop/target path screen over the six strongest GPR definitions degraded the edge; top managed WFA PF rows were below 1.0, with zero near-pass managed candidates. A same-thesis multi-slot audit tried up to four non-overlapping RTH trades per selected high-GPR day to densify sparse high-PF rows; best dense two-slot high-GPR combinations reached WFA PF about 1.52-1.56, but WFA MAR stayed below about 0.68 and no row satisfied the full WFA/MAR/core/incubation shape. Rejected because the geopolitical-risk signal was directionally useful but below WFA PF/MAR and core robustness gates after costs.
- AAII survey investor-sentiment screen: rejected before implementation at the provisional pre-screen gate. Source reviewed: Brown and Cliff (2004), "Investor Sentiment and the Near-Term Stock Market", Journal of Empirical Finance 11(1), DOI `10.1016/j.jempfin.2002.12.001`. AAII's official historical download was blocked by Incapsula in shell, so a no-write pre-screen used the Edgmap AAII dashboard's embedded historical series through 2026-06-04; any pass would have required official AAII data access or a documented licensed data path before acceptance. The ES translation conservatively shifted weekly survey values so each reading was tradable only after its dated survey day, then tested bullish, bearish, neutral, bull-bear spread, pointer, weekly changes, rolling means, ranks, and z-scores against same-day RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The best enough-trade row was falling bearish sentiment (`bearish_chg4 <= -7.2512`) long from 11:00 to 15:30: 798 full-history trades, core PF about 1.52/MAR about 1.74, WFA PF about 1.46/MAR about 0.31/expectancy R about 0.198 with 550 WFA trades, and incubation PF about 1.47/MAR about 0.56. Several high-PF rows were too sparse, such as four-week bull-bear spread jumps with WFA PF about 1.67 but only 236 WFA trades. Rejected because the survey-sentiment branch missed WFA PF/MAR and incubation MAR, and the data path was provisional.
- Cryptocurrency-to-equity spillover screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Corbet, Meegan, Larkin, Lucey, and Yarovaya (2018), "Exploring the dynamic relationships between cryptocurrencies and other financial assets", Economics Letters 165, DOI `10.1016/j.econlet.2018.01.004`. The no-write ES translation used Coin Metrics public daily BTC and ETH reference prices, spot-volume, transaction-count, and active-address fields, shifted one daily row so all signals were known before the next ES RTH session, then traded same-day long/short RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Yahoo and Stooq crypto data paths were unavailable from shell due rate limiting/browser challenge, but Coin Metrics data were accessible through 2026-06-01. Flat-hold screening found one dense near-miss: low ETH transaction-count shock (`eth_TxCnt_chg1_z252 <= -0.5`) long from 09:35 to 16:00 had 510 trades, core PF about 2.00/MAR about 2.59, WFA PF about 1.51/MAR about 0.37/expectancy R about 0.209, and incubation PF about 1.60/MAR about 0.62. A focused 1-minute stop/target path audit over the ETH transaction-count and BTC transaction-count near rows did not rescue the WFA drawdown profile; best path-managed enough-trade row was low BTC 5-day transaction-count rank long 11:00-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.0045` and `target_r=4.0`, WFA n615, PF about 1.42, MAR about 0.80, expectancy R about 0.210, core PF about 1.58/MAR about 2.59, and incubation PF about 1.58/MAR about 1.53. Rejected because the crypto-spillover branch remained below the WFA PF and MAR gates after current ES costs, even after conservative stop-first path management.
- Official financial-stress / Fed-liquidity conditions screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Hakkio and Keeton (2009), "Financial Stress: What Is It, How Can It Be Measured, and Why Does It Matter?", Federal Reserve Bank of Kansas City Economic Review 94(2), plus Federal Reserve financial-condition-index literature. The no-write ES translation used official FRED series that were responsive from shell: St. Louis Fed Financial Stress Index version 4 (`STLFSI4`), Federal Reserve balance-sheet assets (`WALCL`), and reserve balances (`WRESBAL`). Several adjacent FRED endpoints (`NFCI`, `ANFCI`, `RRPONTSYD`, `BAA10Y`, `T10Y3M`) timed out and were not used. All weekly observations were shifted by one series row plus seven calendar days before ES entries, then tested as levels, changes, percent changes, rolling means, ranks, z-scores, and balance-sheet-minus-reserve changes against same-day RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. High-PF financial-stress rows were too sparse or holdout-skewed: `STLFSI4_chg4_z26 <= -1.0` long 11:00-15:30 had WFA n161, PF about 1.76, MAR about 0.46, and incubation n42. Dense high-stress-state rows missed economics: `STLFSI4_mean4 >= 0.07205` long 09:35-16:00 had WFA n519, PF about 1.31, MAR about 0.41, and incubation only 19 trades. Fed balance-sheet/liquidity rows had similar density problems, such as `WALCL_rank104 >= 0.9` long 09:35-12:00 with 574 full-history trades but WFA n270 and incubation n12. Rejected because official financial-condition state did not produce enough WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and incubation density after conservative availability shifting.
- Presidential political-cycle screen: rejected before implementation as overlap-adjacent to the rejected calendar-seasonality branch. Source reviewed: Santa-Clara and Valkanov (2003), "The Presidential Puzzle: Political Cycles and the Stock Market", Journal of Finance 58(5), DOI `10.1111/1540-6261.00590`. The no-write ES translation used only deterministic, known-in-advance political calendar states: presidential term year, quarter, election-year quarter, incumbent party, and divided/unified Congress, then traded same-day RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Narrow quarter cells were too sparse for WFA density and often had no 2021-2022 core representation, such as `term3_q2` long 11:00-13:30 with WFA n188, PF about 1.45, MAR about 0.40, and zero core trades. The only broader rows with enough full-history density were weak: `term_year_1` long 11:00-15:30 had 996 trades, WFA n747, PF about 1.14, MAR about 0.17, and incubation PF about 1.08; `post_election_h1` long 09:35-15:30 had 495 full-history trades and WFA n371, below the 500-trade WFA gate, with PF about 1.17. Rejected because the political-cycle branch did not meet WFA PF/MAR/trade-count requirements and is not distinct enough from failed calendar seasonality to justify a staged campaign.
- Quarterly buyback-blackout / earnings-season calendar screen: rejected before implementation as overlap-adjacent to calendar seasonality. Source reviewed: Bettis, Coles, and Lemmon (2000), "Corporate policies restricting trading by insiders", Journal of Financial Economics 57(2), DOI `10.1016/S0304-405X(00)00055-6`, plus open-market repurchase literature on buyback announcement/blackout timing. The no-write ES translation used deterministic quarter-relative windows as an index-level proxy for corporate buyback blackout and re-opening flows: 45-to-16 and 30-to-1 days before quarter end, quarter-end week, post-quarter-end windows, earnings-month windows, and post-earnings buyback-reopen months. All signals were known in advance and traded one same-day RTH window with exits no later than 16:00 ET. The strongest dense expression was post-quarter-end strength (`post_qe_1_to_15`) long 11:00-16:00 with 636 full-history trades, core PF about 1.53/MAR about 1.41, WFA n455, PF about 1.34/MAR about 0.25/expectancy R about 0.15, and incubation PF about 1.51/MAR about 0.61. Broader buyback-reopen months had enough density but weak economics, e.g. `buyback_reopen_month` long 09:35-15:30 with WFA n940, PF about 1.15, MAR about 0.23, and expectancy R about 0.069. Rejected because the branch missed WFA trade-count/PF/MAR gates and mostly restates a failed calendar-flow family.
- Monthly real-activity macro-state screen: rejected before implementation at the provisional pre-screen gate. Source reviewed: Cooper and Priestley (2009), "Time-Varying Risk Premiums and the Output Gap", Review of Financial Studies 22(7), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhn087`. The no-write ES translation used responsive official FRED monthly series for industrial production (`INDPRO`), payrolls (`PAYEMS`), unemployment (`UNRATE`), CPI (`CPIAUCSL`), and Michigan sentiment (`UMCSENT`); `CFNAI` and recession-probability endpoints timed out. All values were shifted one monthly row and then to the second following month before ES entries to avoid release-date lookahead, so the screen is conservative but still revised-data based. The apparent high-PF rows were recession-era states with no 2023-2026 incubation representation: for example `INDPRO_mean12 <= 96.799958` long 09:35-13:30 had WFA n207, PF about 1.52, MAR about 6.24, and zero incubation trades; `UNRATE_mean12 >= 8.05` long 10:30-13:30 had WFA n86 and zero incubation trades. Broader macro rows with enough full-history density were near flat. Rejected because monthly real-activity state cannot meet WFA and incubation trade-density gates under conservative availability assumptions, and no result was strong enough to justify point-in-time vintage reconstruction.
- FINRA daily short-sale pressure screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Diether, Lee, and Werner (2009), "Short-Sale Strategies and Return Predictability", Review of Financial Studies 22(2), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhn047`. Official FINRA daily short-sale volume files were used from the public CDN for SPY, QQQ/QQQQ, and IWM; the interactive/API partition endpoint only exposed roughly the latest 250 trading days, so historical reconstruction used legacy `FNSQ`, `FNYX`, and `FNRA` files before the consolidated `CNMS` history began in August 2018. FINRA's own data notes were respected: these files are off-exchange/trade-reporting-facility short-sale volume, not short-interest positions, and are not consolidated with exchange activity. Signals were shifted one trading day because FINRA posts same-date daily files after the ES RTH session. Flat-hold screening found dense directionally useful rows but no WFA pass shape: the best enough-trade QQQ-vs-SPY dislocation row (`qqq_minus_spy_ratio_z21 >= 1.0`) long 10:00-12:00 had WFA n514, PF about 1.60, MAR about 0.60, expectancy R about 0.25, core PF about 1.73, and incubation PF about 1.88; the strongest dense IWM row (`IWM_ratio_mean5_rank252 <= 0.2`) long 11:00-15:30 path-managed with `stop_pct=0.006` and `target_r=4.0` had WFA n535, PF about 1.60, MAR about 0.68, expectancy R about 0.27, core PF about 1.69, and incubation PF about 1.68. A focused 1-minute stop/target path screen over dense FINRA rules found zero near rows with WFA MAR above 1.0, and an OR/majority union audit improved sparse PF pockets but produced no 500-trade row with adequate MAR. Rejected because the official short-sale pressure signal remained below the WFA MAR gate after current ES costs and Apex-compatible RTH exits.
- FINRA consolidated short-interest position screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Asquith, Pathak, and Ritter (2005), "Short Interest, Institutional Ownership, and Stock Returns", Journal of Financial Economics 78(2), DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2005.01.001`, plus FINRA short-interest reporting documentation. The official FINRA `consolidatedShortInterest` Query API exposed SPY, QQQ, and IWM records from settlement dates 2017-12-29 through 2026-05-15, with current short position, average daily volume, days-to-cover, and percentage-change fields. To avoid publication-date lookahead, each settlement record was made tradable only after a conservative 10-business-day lag. The data horizon is shorter than ideal for the full ES WFA sample, but a no-write screen was still run over 2018-2026. Tail thresholds produced strong but sparse rows, such as `iwm_minus_spy_change_z24 <= -1.5` long 10:00-12:00 with n150, PF about 2.24, MAR about 1.54, core PF about 2.49, and incubation PF about 2.92. Broader thresholds needed for the 500-trade gate diluted the edge: the best dense row was high average ETF short-interest change (`etf_short_change_avg >= 4.296667`) long 09:35-15:30 with n524, PF about 1.36, MAR about 0.60, expectancy R about 0.16, core PF about 1.36, and incubation PF about 1.49. Rejected because the official short-interest-position signal either missed WFA trade density or, when broadened enough, fell well short of PF/MAR/expectancy gates; the shorter 2018-start history also makes it unsuitable as an Apex acceptance candidate without an exceptional margin of safety.
- FINRA aggregate margin-debt / customer-credit screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Burger and Curtis (2017), "Aggregate Margin Debt and the Divergence of Price from Accounting Fundamentals", Contemporary Accounting Research, DOI `10.1111/1911-3846.12314`, plus Domian and Racine (2006), "An empirical analysis of margin debt", International Review of Economics & Finance, DOI `10.1016/j.iref.2004.08.007`. Official FINRA margin-statistics data were parsed from the FINRA XLSX download, covering month-end observations from 1997-01-31 through 2026-04-30. The screen used a conservative month-end plus 25-calendar-day availability lag, consistent with FINRA's note that updates are generally published in the third week after the reference month. Features included debit balances, cash and margin free-credit balances, total/net credit, debt-to-credit ratios, 1/3/12-month changes, percent changes, z-scores, and ranks, then traded same-day ES RTH windows with exits no later than 16:00 ET. Strong-looking rows were sparse or lacked holdout coverage; e.g. low cash-credit z120 had only 22 WFA/incubation trades and no 2021-2022 core trades. The only dense near-miss was a sharp negative monthly net-credit shock (`net_credit_pct1_z24 <= -1.0`) long 09:35-16:00: full n569, PF about 1.36, MAR about 0.24, WFA n510, PF about 1.40, MAR about 0.33, expectancy R about 0.17, core n23 with PF about 2.56, and incubation n147 with PF about 1.59/MAR about 0.97. Rejected because monthly margin-credit state did not meet WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates and had thin core-window representation.
- SEC fails-to-deliver data status: superseded by later corrected-cache rejections at entries 611 and 694; this is no longer blocked or open. The earlier source branch used SEC CNS fails-to-deliver files for SPY, QQQ/QQQQ, and IWM, with academic FTD/short-sale-constraint literature still pending final source selection at that time. Direct SEC file requests succeeded earlier, but a parallel cache build triggered `HTTP 429: Too Many Requests`; the partial cache only covered 2010-01-04 through 2016-04-29 and could not support WFA or incubation. A later repair completed `/private/tmp/sec_ftd_etf_cache.csv` through 2026-05-14 and the corrected screens found zero pass-shaped or near rows, so do not treat this old block note as an unresolved candidate.
- CFTC combined TFF hedging-pressure overlap audit: rejected before implementation as not distinct enough from the prior CFTC/TFF trader-position branch. Source reviewed: de Roon, Nijman, and Veld (2000), "Hedging Pressure Effects in Futures Markets", Journal of Finance, DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00253`, plus official CFTC historical compressed Traders in Financial Futures futures-and-options combined reports. The audit broadened the earlier COT screen to E-mini S&P 500, S&P 500 consolidated, Nasdaq mini, and Russell mini/e-mini aliases from 2010-2026, shifted Tuesday report states to the following Monday RTH session, and tested own/cross-market dealer, asset-manager, leveraged-money, other-reportable, open-interest, rank, z-score, and 1/4/13-week change features. Flat holds found a dense SPX open-interest pressure row, but it missed staged WFA shape. A focused 1-minute stop/target audit over the strongest dense rules found the best staged-style row at `SPX_open_interest_chg13 >= 47442`, long 11:00-15:30, `stop_pct=0.006`, `target_r=4.0`: full n655, PF about 1.57/MAR about 0.96/expectancy R about 0.26; WFA-style pre-incubation n506, PF about 1.58/MAR about 1.02/expectancy R about 0.27; 2021-2022 core n119, PF about 1.43/MAR about 1.67; last-18-month incubation n129, PF about 1.59/MAR about 3.82. Rejected because the COT hedging-pressure expansion still misses the hard WFA MAR >=1.5 gate and overlaps an already rejected public-COT sentiment edge.
- Frog-in-the-pan daily path-smoothness screen: rejected before implementation after the user narrowed the search back to strategies testable from existing 1-minute ES price/volume data. Source reviewed: Da, Gurun, and Warachka (2014), "Frog in the Pan: Continuous Information and Momentum", Review of Financial Studies 27(7), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhu003`. The no-write ES translation used only RTH daily closes derived from local 1-minute bars and tested prior 5/10/21/42/63-day smooth versus discrete trend continuation/fade into Apex-compatible same-day RTH holds. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/fip_momentum_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Top rows were too sparse and weak, such as a five-day discrete-down fade entered 09:35 and flattened 12:00 with 192 full-history trades, WFA-style n116, PF about 1.72, MAR about 0.33, and only 21 last-18-month incubation trades. Rejected because the local OHLCV-only FIP translation cannot reach the 500-trade WFA gate without diluting the edge.
- Lee-Swaminathan volume-conditioned momentum screen: rejected before implementation after the same local-data pivot. Source reviewed: Lee and Swaminathan (2000), "Price Momentum and Trading Volume", Journal of Finance 55(5), DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00280`. The no-write ES translation used only local 1-minute RTH-derived daily volume, returns, range, and rolling ranks, then tested prior 3/5/10/21/42/63-day return continuation/fade conditioned on high/low volume or range, with same-day Apex-compatible exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/volume_momentum_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The strongest visible rows were sparse or unstable: for example a 42-day high-range up-move fade had only 72 WFA-style trades, and a 63-day low-volume down-momentum short had 113 WFA-style trades. Broader rows did not preserve PF/MAR through incubation. Rejected because the local OHLCV-only volume/momentum interaction does not provide enough dense WFA robustness after current ES costs.
- VPIN / order-flow-toxicity overlap audit: rejected before implementation as overlap-adjacent to the failed signed-volume/order-imbalance branch. Source reviewed: Easley, Lopez de Prado, and O'Hara (2012), "Flow Toxicity and Liquidity in a High-frequency World", Review of Financial Studies 25(5), 1457-1493, DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhs053`. The no-write ES translation used only local active-contract 1-minute RTH bars, constructing bulk signed-volume imbalance and volume-clock VPIN proxies from completed bars before each signal. Scratch paths: `/private/tmp/vpin_toxicity_screen.py` and `/private/tmp/vpin_toxicity_path_screen.py`. Sparse top-decile toxicity rows had high PF but far too few WFA/incubation trades. Widening to dense thresholds produced one useful near-miss: `vpin_b010_l5` 21-day rank >= 0.5 plus positive session return, long 13:30-15:30, had 997 full-history trades, WFA-style n615, PF about 1.56, MAR about 0.41, expectancy R about 0.25, core PF about 2.11/MAR about 2.18, and incubation PF about 1.49/MAR about 1.27. A focused conservative stop-first path audit around the same family did not fix the WFA drawdown profile; best dense managed rows reached WFA PF about 1.59 but MAR only about 0.42-0.62, and higher-MAR rows were too sparse. Rejected because the local VPIN translation is economically interesting but remains well below the WFA MAR >=1.5 gate and is not distinct enough from the prior order-imbalance rejection to promote without a pass-shaped result.
- Brock-style moving-average/filter-rule screen: rejected before implementation as a direct OHLCV-only audit of the moving-average/filter-rule half of Brock, Lakonishok, and LeBaron (1992), "Simple Technical Trading Rules and the Stochastic Properties of Stock Returns", Journal of Finance 47(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1992.tb04681.x`. The prior ledger entry under this source rejected rolling trading-range breakouts; this no-write follow-up tested completed-bar price-vs-SMA distance, SMA slope, and fast/slow MA spread filters from local ES 1-minute RTH bars at fixed Apex-compatible RTH entry/exit windows. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/ma_filter_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Top rows were sparse, such as a 15-minute SMA fade from 13:00 to 13:30 with WFA-style n89, PF about 2.08, and MAR about 0.66, or recent/core-only MA continuation pockets with poor holdout behavior. Enough-trade MA continuation rows had WFA PF/MAR far below default gates, e.g. 240-minute SMA continuation with WFA n556, PF about 1.24, and MAR about 0.15. Rejected because the direct intraday MA/filter translation does not add a dense robust edge beyond the already failed trend-flag/regime and range-breakout branches.
- Candlestick / OHLC price-pattern screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Caginalp and Laurent (1998), "The Predictive Power of Price Patterns", Applied Mathematical Finance 5(3-4), DOI `10.1080/135048698334637`, plus later candlestick profitability tests. The no-write ES translation used only local 1-minute RTH bars aggregated to 5m/15m/30m OHLCV bars, then tested hammer, shooting-star, bullish/bearish engulfing, outside-bar reversal, and wide-body continuation patterns with next-bar entry, one non-overlapping trade per day, conservative current ES costs, and same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/candlestick_pattern_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Sparse rows could look strong, such as 15m outside-reversal-down with WFA-style n102, PF about 1.74, and MAR about 0.67, but they failed trade density and/or incubation. Dense rows were weak after costs, such as 15m wide-body down continuation with WFA n1178, PF about 1.07, MAR about 0.09, and expectancy R about 0.04. Rejected because classic OHLC candlestick patterns did not produce a dense, robust ES intraday edge under Apex-compatible exits.
- RSI/MACD oscillator screen: rejected before implementation as a standalone local OHLCV audit of Chong and Ng (2008), "Technical Analysis and the London Stock Exchange: Testing the MACD and RSI Rules Using the FT30", Applied Economics Letters 15(14), DOI `10.1080/13504850600993598`. This was distinct from the old intraday-capitulation RSI module because it tested generic RSI reversal/continuation, RSI-with-short-context, MACD cross, and MACD histogram rules on 5m/15m/30m ES RTH bars, with first next-bar signal per day, conservative current costs, and same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/oscillator_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The best-looking dense rows were still far below WFA gates, such as 30m RSI(14) oversold reversal held 12 bars with 699 WFA-style trades, PF about 1.15, MAR about 0.17, and expectancy R about 0.07, despite strong last-18-month incubation. MACD rows were similarly weak: a 30m MACD(24,52,18) cross-continuation long held 6 bars had 418 WFA trades, PF about 1.22, and MAR about 0.19. Rejected because standalone RSI/MACD oscillators do not provide a robust Apex-compatible ES edge after costs.
- Bollinger-band / rolling-dispersion screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lento, Gradojevic, and Wright (2007), "Investment Information Content in Bollinger Bands?", Applied Financial Economics Letters 3(4), DOI `10.1080/17446540701206576`. The no-write ES translation used only local 1-minute RTH bars aggregated to 5m/15m/30m, then tested lower/upper band reversal, lower/upper band breakout, low-width squeeze breakouts, and high-width reversal states from 20/50/100-bar rolling means and standard deviations, with first next-bar signal per day and same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/bollinger_band_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The strongest rows were wide lower-band reversal variants, but they were too sparse or missed WFA economics: 30m wide lower reversal with 20-bar/1.5-sigma bands held 2 bars had WFA n288, PF about 1.39, MAR about 0.37, and incubation PF about 2.91; broader lower-band reversal rows with WFA density had PF around 1.02-1.22 and MAR far below 1.5. Rejected because rolling-dispersion band signals did not create a dense robust ES edge beyond the already failed technical-rule families.
- Intraday variance-ratio/autocorrelation screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lo and MacKinlay (1988), "Stock Market Prices Do Not Follow Random Walks: Evidence from a Simple Specification Test", Review of Financial Studies 1(1), DOI `10.1093/rfs/1.1.41`. The no-write ES translation used only completed local 1-minute RTH returns to compute rolling intraday variance ratios over 5/15/30-minute horizons and 60/120/240-minute lookbacks, then conditioned recent 15/30/60-minute source-return continuation or fade on persistent versus mean-reverting VR states at fixed Apex-compatible RTH entry/exit windows. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/variance_ratio_screen.py`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Top rows were again sparse, such as 5-minute VR very-reverting plus a 60-minute positive source return, long 11:00-12:00, with WFA n66, PF about 2.57, MAR about 1.02; enough-trade variants did not approach the WFA gates. Rejected because variance-ratio state does not densify into a robust ES intraday edge and mostly confirms the already failed high-frequency reversal/continuation family.
- Current-session realized-jump detection screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lee and Mykland (2008), "Jumps in Financial Markets: A New Nonparametric Test and Jump Dynamics", Review of Financial Studies 21(6), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhm056`. The no-write ES translation used only local active-contract 1-minute RTH bars and current-session completed-bar jump statistics before the entry: extreme return z-scores, jump-share proxies, source-window returns, and same-window volume shocks, with Apex-compatible next-bar entries and same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/realized_jump_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/realized_jump_screen_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/realized_jump_screen_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Sparse flat-hold jump rows had high PF but far too little density, such as a 10:00 negative high-jump-volume fade long to 15:30 with only 76 WFA-style trades. The best dense stop-managed row was `jshare_rank0.5_pos_ret0.001_cont`, long 13:30-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.0035` and `target_r=1.0`: full n821, PF about 1.20, MAR about 0.13; WFA-style n498, PF about 1.25, MAR about 0.27, expectancy R about 0.11; core PF about 1.64/MAR about 2.42; incubation n88, PF about 1.63/MAR about 2.57. Rejected because current-session jump detection could not reach the WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates, and higher-PF rows were too sparse for the 500-trade WFA requirement.
- Intraday volume-curve surprise screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Admati and Pfleiderer (1988), "A Theory of Intraday Patterns: Volume and Price Variability", Review of Financial Studies 1(1), DOI `10.1093/rfs/1.1.3`. The no-write ES translation used only local active-contract 1-minute RTH bars, comparing cumulative or recent same-session volume to prior same-clock history, then conditioning same-day ES entries on source return, low/high volume surprise, absorbed-volume states, and volume-per-return price-impact ranks. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/volume_curve_surprise_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/volume_curve_surprise_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/volume_curve_surprise_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. High-PF flat rows were sparse, such as low same-clock cumulative volume with positive source return from 13:00 to 16:00: WFA n70, PF about 2.94, MAR about 0.81, and only 9 incubation trades. The strongest dense managed rows were economically weak, such as `v63_lo0.9_pos_ret0.001_cont`, long 13:30-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.016` and `target_r=0.75`: WFA n455, PF about 1.23, MAR about 0.16, expectancy R about 0.11; incubation n76, PF about 1.38, MAR about 1.17. A denser high-volume negative-return fade had WFA n536 but only PF about 1.08 and MAR about 0.10. Rejected because volume-curve surprise did not create a dense robust edge beyond the already failed volume-shock/order-flow families.
- Current-session volume-profile acceptance screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed under Blume, Easley, and O'Hara (1994), "Market Statistics and Technical Analysis: The Role of Volume", Journal of Finance 49(1), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1994.tb04424.x`, but this audit used current-session profile state rather than the previously rejected prior-session profile references. The no-write ES translation built a one-point-binned current-session profile from completed RTH bars before entry, then tested POC distance, POC concentration, profile width, and POC migration as continuation/fade signals with Apex-compatible same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/current_profile_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/current_profile_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/current_profile_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The highest-PF rows were too sparse, such as narrow-profile negative-return fade long 10:30-13:30 with WFA n94, PF about 2.26, MAR about 0.72, and only 8 incubation trades. The best dense-looking profile continuation row was `wide0.6_pos_ret0.0005_cont`, long 13:30-15:30, with WFA n507, PF about 1.21, MAR about 0.32, expectancy R about 0.10, and incubation n68. Conservative stop/target path management did not improve the dense WFA shape; the top managed rows remained sparse variants of the same narrow-profile fade. Rejected because current-session profile acceptance did not add a robust edge beyond the failed VWAP/current-feature and volume-profile branches.
- Roll implicit-spread / bid-ask-bounce screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Roll (1984), "A Simple Implicit Measure of the Effective Bid-Ask Spread in an Efficient Market", Journal of Finance 39(4), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1984.tb03897.x`, Wiley link `https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1540-6261.1984.tb03897.x`. The no-write ES translation used only completed local active-contract 1-minute RTH price changes before entry to estimate first-order serial covariance, Roll-style implicit spread, sign-alternation/bid-ask-bounce share, zero-return share, and noise-to-range ratios, then tested noisy-source fades and clean-source continuations with Apex-compatible same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/roll_spread_noise_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/roll_spread_noise_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/roll_spread_noise_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The best flat broad row, low sign-alternation plus positive source return, long 13:30-16:00, had WFA n471, PF about 1.36, MAR about 0.44, expectancy R about 0.16, core PF about 1.54, and incubation PF about 2.28. Path management did not solve the gates; the strongest managed row on the same family reached WFA n471, PF about 1.37, MAR about 0.59, expectancy R about 0.18, with incubation PF about 1.88, still below the WFA trade-count, PF, MAR, and expectancy requirements. Rejected because the implicit-spread/noise state is directionally useful in recent and core periods but too weak and under-dense for the default WFA gate.
- Lo-Mamaysky-Wang intraday path-pattern recognition screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lo, Mamaysky, and Wang (2000), "Foundations of Technical Analysis: Computational Algorithms, Statistical Inference, and Empirical Implementation", Journal of Finance 55(4), DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00265`, Wiley link `https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/0022-1082.00265`. The no-write ES translation used only normalized completed intraday price paths and volume-curve fragments before each entry, then selected long or short only from prior-session nearest-neighbor analog outcomes. Unlike the prior adaptive ridge/bucket audit, this screen matched raw path templates directly and used no future labels for each trade date. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/knn_path_pattern_screen.py`; summary CSV: `/private/tmp/knn_path_pattern_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Results were strongly holdout-skewed: the top row, 13:30 entry using a 120-minute source path, 15:30 exit, 1008-session history, k=50, and $50 edge threshold, had full n841, PF about 1.12, core PF about 1.02, WFA n603 with PF about 0.97 and negative MAR, but incubation n221 with PF about 1.54 and MAR about 2.31. Other rows showed the same pattern: recent incubation strength but weak or negative WFA-period behavior. Rejected because prior-only template matching did not produce a stable ES intraday edge under the WFA gate and overlaps the broader failed technical-pattern/adaptive-model families without improving them.
- Rescaled-range / fractal path-efficiency screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lo (1991), "Long-Term Memory in Stock Market Prices", Econometrica 59(5), DOI `10.2307/2938368`, MIT abstract `https://web.mit.edu/Alo/www/Papers/lo-91.html`. The no-write ES translation used only completed local active-contract 1-minute RTH bars before entry to compute path efficiency, rescaled-range-style statistics, Hurst proxies, fractal roughness proxies, source returns, range, and volume ranks, then tested efficient-path continuation and rough-path fade/continuation rules with Apex-compatible same-session exits. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/fractal_path_efficiency_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/fractal_path_efficiency_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/fractal_path_efficiency_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. High-PF flat rows were sparse, such as a 14:00 low-efficiency positive-return continuation to 15:30 with WFA n79, PF about 2.50, MAR about 0.62, and only 12 incubation trades. Path management found the best dense row at 10:30 30-minute high-R/S positive-return continuation to 15:30 with `stop_pct=0.0045`, `target_r=3.0`: WFA n504, PF about 1.27, MAR about 0.37, expectancy R about 0.14, core PF about 1.68, and incubation PF about 1.49. Rejected because path-efficiency/fractal state did not reach WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates and mostly restates the already failed trend/reversal and variance-ratio state families.
- Round-number psychological-barrier screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Donaldson and Kim (1993), "Price Barriers in the Dow Jones Industrial Average", Journal of Financial and Quantitative Analysis 28(3), DOI `10.2307/2331416`, Cambridge link `https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/journal-of-financial-and-quantitative-analysis/article/abs/price-barriers-in-the-dow-jones-industrial-average/ED089C700C6B674DA8BD1BFB10CA0B85`. The no-write ES translation used only local active-contract 1-minute RTH OHLCV before each entry, measuring distance to 25/50/100-point psychological price grids, completed source-window approach direction, touch/rejection counts, and high-volume round-number breaks. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/round_number_barrier_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/round_number_barrier_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/round_number_barrier_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The strongest flat and stop-managed rows were sparse 100-point barrier reactions, such as `100pt_near8_down_approach_reject`, long 13:00-15:30 after a downside approach, with about 125 full-history trades, WFA n70, PF about 2.48-2.56, MAR about 0.59-0.63, and only 17 incubation trades. Broader 25/50-point rows that traded more often lost too much PF/MAR after costs. Rejected because fixed round-number barriers may matter locally but cannot reach the 500-trade WFA gate without diluting into weak broad grids, and the best rows are far below required WFA/incubation trade density.
- Current-session realized skewness/kurtosis screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Amaya, Christoffersen, Jacobs, and Vasquez (2015), "Does realized skewness predict the cross-section of equity returns?", Journal of Financial Economics 118(1), DOI `10.1016/j.jfineco.2015.02.009`, ScienceDirect link `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0304405X15000339`. The no-write ES translation used only completed same-session 1-minute RTH returns before each entry, computing realized skewness, kurtosis, realized variance, positive-return share, left/right tail quantiles, volume ratios, and trailing same-clock ranks. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/current_realized_moments_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/current_realized_moments_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/current_realized_moments_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Sparse high-kurtosis or low-skew rows had high PF but too few trades, such as low-skew negative-return inverse shorts from 13:00 to 13:30 with WFA n82-115 and incubation n16-21. The broadest managed low-skew thesis row, long 11:00-16:00 with `stop_pct=0.0025` to `0.0045` and `target_r=4.0`, reached WFA n503 but only PF about 1.21-1.26, MAR about 0.23-0.31, and expectancy R about 0.12-0.13. Rejected because current-session realized moments either stay sparse or dilute into weak volatility-state exposure below the default WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates, and they do not improve on the already rejected semivariance/jump/current-volatility families.
- VPIN local-volatility/liquidity filter refinement: rejected before implementation as a targeted rescue audit of the already rejected local VPIN/toxicity near-miss. Source remains Easley, Lopez de Prado, and O'Hara (2012), "Flow Toxicity and Liquidity in a High-frequency World", Review of Financial Studies 25(5), DOI `10.1093/rfs/hhs053`. The no-write refinement kept the strongest local base family (`vpin_b010_l5` 21-day rank >= roughly 0.45-0.60 plus positive session return, long 13:30-15:30) and added at most one completed pre-entry RTH filter at a time: session realized variance, range, cumulative volume, path efficiency, drawdown, or runup rank. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/vpin_local_filter_refine.py`; summary CSV: `/private/tmp/vpin_local_filter_refine_top.csv`. The refinement found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Drawdown-rank filters improved PF but cut density below gates; for example rank >=0.4 with VPIN cutoff 0.50 and session return >=0.001 produced WFA n321, PF about 2.06, MAR about 0.74, expectancy R about 0.42, and incubation n61. Broader variants preserving more density still missed MAR or incubation count, such as cutoff 0.50/session return >=0.0005/rank >=0.3 with WFA n439, PF about 1.98, MAR about 0.66, and incubation n81, still under the WFA trade-count and MAR gates. Rejected because the only way to improve VPIN PF is to over-filter into under-dense samples; it remains below the Apex acceptance criteria and should not be re-run as a renamed toxicity/positive-return edge.
- Prior-down reversal morning-filter rescue audit: rejected before implementation as a targeted overlap audit of the already rejected prior-session reversal / realized-moment branch. Source remains Amaya, Christoffersen, Jacobs, and Vasquez (2015) for the realized-moment/return-rank framing, but the tested effect again reduced to short-horizon prior-session downside reversal. The no-write refinement used only local active-contract 1-minute RTH data and tested prior RTH return rank thresholds plus one prior-session or current-morning filter at a time: prior range/volume/close-location, current morning return, range, close location, volume, or realized variance. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/prior_down_reversal_morning_filter.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/prior_down_reversal_morning_filter_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/prior_down_reversal_morning_filter_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. The best flat row was prior 21-day return rank <=0.25 with prior volume rank >=0.4 and current session range rank >=0.2, long 10:30-15:30: full n748, core PF about 1.90, WFA n461 with PF about 1.34/MAR about 0.39/expectancy R about 0.149, and incubation n77 with PF about 1.96/MAR about 2.18. Rows with WFA PF above 1.5 were too sparse, and the only path-management candidate degraded to WFA PF about 1.22 and expectancy R below 0.10. Rejected because current-morning confirmation does not lift the prior-down reversal above the WFA PF/expectancy/trade-count gates, and further revisions would be renamed versions of an already failed edge.
- Permutation-entropy / forbidden-pattern screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Zunino, Zanin, Tabak, Perez, and Rosso (2009), "Forbidden patterns, permutation entropy and stock market inefficiency", Physica A 388(14), DOI `10.1016/j.physa.2009.03.042`, ScienceDirect link `https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0378437109002593`. The no-write ES translation used only completed local active-contract 1-minute RTH returns before each entry, computing normalized permutation entropy, forbidden ordinal-pattern fraction, pattern concentration, source returns, realized variance, volume ratios, and trailing same-clock ranks. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/permutation_entropy_screen.py`; summary CSVs: `/private/tmp/permutation_entropy_flat_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/permutation_entropy_path_top.csv`. The screen found zero near-pass and zero pass-shaped rows. Sparse low/high-entropy rows had high PF but far too few trades, such as low-entropy positive-return continuation at 13:30-15:30 with WFA n115, PF about 1.83, MAR about 0.50, and incubation n19. The densest managed rows were economically weak: high pattern concentration with positive source return at 13:30-15:30 had WFA n529, PF about 1.22-1.24, MAR about 0.33-0.40, expectancy R about 0.11-0.13, and incubation PF around 1.85-1.95. Rejected because ordinal-pattern inefficiency does not produce enough cost-adjusted WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and overlaps the broader failed path-efficiency/template-recognition branch without improving it.
- 52-week-high anchoring screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: George and Hwang (2004), "The 52-Week High and Momentum Investing", Journal of Finance 59(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.2004.00695.x`, Wiley link `https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1111/j.1540-6261.2004.00695.x`. The no-write ES translation used only local active-contract 1-minute RTH OHLCV, explicit roll-calendar filtering, and prior completed RTH sessions to compute the prior close's nearness to the trailing 252-session high/low and channel position. It then tested Apex-compatible same-day fixed-window long/short variants around near-high, near-low, far-from-high, low-channel, and high-channel states with one-tick slippage and current commission. Scratch table: `/tmp/anchor52_wide.parquet`. The screen tested 684 rows and found zero rough pass-shape rows under the length-adjusted 10-year WFA MAR benchmark of about 0.659. High-PF rows were too sparse, such as low-channel long with only 6 WFA-period trades. The best broader row, far-from-high long with threshold 0.99 and 09:35-15:30 hold, had 1,597 WFA-period trades but only PF 1.042, MAR 0.101, and expectancy R 0.021, with incubation PF 1.248 and MAR 1.395. A stronger but still insufficient row, far-from-high long threshold 0.90 from 11:00 to 15:30, had 375 WFA-period trades, PF 1.307, MAR 0.604, and expectancy R 0.164. Rejected because the single-instrument ES 52-week anchor does not produce enough WFA PF/expectancy/trade-count quality to justify a full staged campaign, and the broad variants overlap the already failed daily time-series momentum family without improving it.
- Length-adjusted MAR backscan of saved scratch summaries: reviewed 72 `*top.csv` scratch summary files under the new roughly 10-year WFA MAR benchmark of about 0.659. Pass-shaped rows existed only in external-data branches, especially COT/TFF hedging pressure and FINRA short-sale pressure, so they were not promoted under the user's instruction to focus on strategies easily tested with existing 1-minute price/volume data. Local OHLCV-only rows remained below the combined WFA trade-count/PF/MAR/expectancy and incubation gates. Best local near-misses were still VPIN/toxicity (`vpin_b010_l5`, cutoff 0.45, session return >=0.0005, drawdown-rank filter, 13:30-15:30) with WFA n472, PF about 1.87, MAR about 0.72, but below the 500-trade WFA gate; the denser base VPIN row had WFA n549 but only PF about 1.45 and MAR about 0.62; Roll-style bid-ask-bounce/noise had WFA n471, PF about 1.37, MAR about 0.59. Conclusion: the dynamic MAR rule does not currently rescue a 1-minute OHLCV-only staged candidate.
- External datasets now allowed by user if they can be used reliably without hindsight and in real time. Promote only point-in-time datasets with documented publication lag and conservative availability alignment.
- CFTC TFF hedging-pressure staged campaign started. Academic source: Campbell, Grossman, and Wang (1993), "Trading Volume and Serial Correlation in Stock Returns", DOI `10.2307/2118454`; implementation uses official CFTC TFF futures-only history with Tuesday report positions made tradable no earlier than the following Monday RTH. Campaign/config family: `configs/campaigns/cftc_tff_hedging_pressure`. First staged candidate `configs/campaigns/cftc_tff_hedging_pressure/variants/ES/5m/broad_spx_open_interest_expansion.yaml` failed. Result path: `data/reports/campaigns/cftc_tff_hedging_pressure/ES/1m_full_history/5m/broad_spx_open_interest_expansion/campaign_tests`. First failed gate: walk-forward analysis. Limited core grid passed with 108 combinations, 104 profitable iterations (96.30%), zero Apex violations; limited monkey passed with net-profit beat rate 96.25%, max-drawdown beat rate 99.35%, zero Apex violations. WFA rejected after early exit at window 2: window 1 selected threshold 65000, entry 10:30, stop 0.45%, target 3R and lost OOS; window 2 skipped because selected in-sample PF 0.90 < 1.00. Stitched OOS metrics at halt: 25 trades, PF 0.522, MAR -7.892, expectancy R -0.153, win rate 44.0%, Apex violations 0. Rejection reason: corrected point-in-time COT feature looked pass-shaped in coarse scratch screens but did not survive real staged WFA parameter selection.

- U.S. Treasury auction-cycle screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Treasury-supply/liquidity and auction-demand literature; data came from the official FiscalData `auctions_query` API. The no-write screen loaded 5,629 Treasury auction records from 2010 onward, treated same-day auction-result variables as tradable only after the result and next-day duplicates as pre-RTH features, and tested event, offering-size, bid-to-cover, dealer-share, direct-bidder-share, and indirect-bidder-share features across bills, coupon buckets, and long/intermediate auctions. - New York Fed/OFR reference-rate plumbing screen: rejected before implementation after the user allowed reliable real-time external datasets. Source reviewed: official New York Fed reference rates and the OFR API mirror for `fnyr` SOFR/EFFR/OBFR/BGCR/TGCR rates, percentiles, and volumes. Result path: `/private/tmp/nyfed_reference_rates_screen_top.csv`; ES scratch cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. The 10:30-16:00 sibling had similar WFA density but missed WFA MAR and also failed incubation economics. A same-session FRED liquidity refresh was attempted for `RRPONTSYD`, `RPONTSYD`, `WALCL`, `WRESBAL`, and `WTREGEN`, but the graph CSV endpoints timed out from shell, so no new FRED liquidity result was recorded.
- Official Treasury yield-curve state screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: Fama and French-style time-varying expected-return/business-condition evidence plus official Treasury Daily Par Yield Curve Rates. It produced 9,997 rows after the full-history filter, with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows under the 2014-01-01 to 2024-11-29 dynamic WFA MAR requirement of 0.621. The highest-scoring rows were sparse 5-day Treasury-rate-drop states, e.g. `5 Yr_chg5 <= -0.20` long 09:35-15:30 had full n152/PF 1.876, core n23/PF 8.172, WFA n107/PF 3.077/MAR 0.580, and incubation n12/PF 0.752/MAR -0.503. Rejected because official yield-curve state either over-filters into sparse historical rate-shock pockets or dilutes into WFA PF/MAR/expectancy far below staged acceptance levels.

- Pre-FOMC drift window screen: rejected before implementation as a density-aware follow-up to the previously rejected exact scheduled-macro event screen. Source reviewed: Lucca and Moench (2015), "The Pre-FOMC Announcement Drift", Journal of Finance 70(1), plus official Federal Reserve FOMC historical meeting pages and current FOMC calendar `https://www.federalreserve.gov/monetarypolicy/fomccalendars.htm`. Result path: `/private/tmp/pre_fomc_window_screen_top.csv`; ES scratch cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. The no-write screen parsed 133 scheduled FOMC statement dates from 2010 through 2026, excluding unscheduled/cancelled/conference-call/notation-vote historical rows, then tested known-in-advance meeting-day, pre-meeting, and post-meeting trading-day windows such as `pre_1_to_5`, `pre_1_to_10`, `pre_1_to_15`, and `pre_1_to_20` across Apex-compatible same-day ES RTH holds. It tested 280 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Exact meeting-day long 09:35-12:00 had WFA PF 1.521 and MAR 0.297 but only 83 WFA trades, while broader pre-meeting windows reached density but were flat or negative after costs; for example `pre_1_to_20` long 11:00-16:00 had WFA n1,596/PF 1.016/MAR 0.023/expectancy R 0.007 and incubation n239/PF 1.122/MAR 0.572. Rejected because the deterministic pre-FOMC drift translation cannot satisfy both WFA trade density and WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates in ES intraday RTH form; do not revisit scheduled-policy timing unless using a materially different source variable, not just wider event windows.
- ICI weekly mutual-fund/ETF flow pressure source audit: rejected before implementation at the data-access gate after the user allowed reliable real-time external datasets. Source reviewed: Investment Company Institute weekly estimated flow pages, including `https://www.ici.org/topics/weekly-estimated-flow-reports`, `https://www.ici.org/research/stats/flows`, and `https://www.ici.org/research/stats/combined_flows`. The thesis would have used public weekly estimated domestic-equity mutual fund and ETF net flows, shifted by at least one full week after the week-ended Wednesday reference date, as a no-hindsight demand-flow state for ES RTH holds. The current/recent annual files such as `https://www.ici.org/flows_data_2025.xls`, `https://www.ici.org/flows_data_2026.xls`, `https://www.ici.org/combined_flows_data_2025.xls`, and `https://www.ici.org/combined_flows_data_2026.xls` are directly downloadable, but old annual files for 2010/2014/2020/2024 return 404 and the historical files listed on the weekly-flow reports page, including `/statistical-report/combined_flows_data_hist_2026.xls`, `/statistical-report/flows_data_hist_2026.xls`, and `/statistical-report/etf_flows_data_hist_2026.xls`, are marked as disabled/member-login reports in the page markup and direct requests return 403. Rejected because there is no reliable public historical data path spanning WFA and incubation; do not use ICI flows for an acceptance candidate unless a documented licensed/member data path or another point-in-time public archive is added.
- Month-end stock-bond rebalancing pressure screen: rejected before implementation. Source family reviewed: month-end target-allocation/pension-fund and target-date-fund rebalancing literature, including Mazzoleni and Melone, "The Unintended Consequences of Rebalancing" (NBER working paper 33554), plus the prior turn-of-month/rebalancing evidence already audited. Scratch result paths: `/private/tmp/month_end_stock_bond_rebalance_screen_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/month_end_stock_bond_rebalance_screen_all.csv`; raw ETF cache: `/private/tmp/yahoo_stock_bond_rebalance_cache.csv`; ES scratch cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. It tested 116,342 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Best dense rows improved over generic calendar exposure but stayed below WFA gates: `turn_last5_first5` with `spy_ief_mtd_diff <= 0.0`, long 11:00-15:30, had WFA n500/PF 1.366/MAR 0.369/expectancy R 0.156 and incubation n65/PF 1.374/MAR 0.878; `turn_last5_first5` with `spy_ief_mtd_diff_rank60 <= 0.4`, long 11:00-15:30, had WFA n542/PF 1.361/MAR 0.418/expectancy R 0.157 and incubation n72/PF 1.436/MAR 0.967; `first_7td` with `spy_ief_mtd_diff_z60 <= 0.0`, long 11:00-15:30, cleared incubation at n78/PF 1.676/MAR 1.652 but failed WFA at n531/PF 1.360/MAR 0.306/expectancy R 0.155. High-PF rows were underdense event artifacts. Rejected because stock-bond month-end rebalancing conditioning does not satisfy WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and incubation density under current costs; do not rerun as a simple stock-bond month-end/turn-window variant without materially new evidence.
