Dense rows were recent-holdout artifacts rather than WFA edges: `vx1_ret1_rank63 >= 0.7`, long 09:35-15:30, had WFA n812/PF 1.053/MAR 0.056/expectancy R 0.026 while incubation was strong at n118/PF 2.073/MAR 4.319. Rejected because official VX futures term-structure information is reliable and point-in-time with a one-session lag, but it does not meet WFA PF/MAR/expectancy or incubation density gates for ES intraday execution under current costs; do not rerun as a VIX-futures-contango or VX-basis variant without materially new structure.
- Official Cboe aggregate VIX-futures activity screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: VIX-futures basis/activity timing literature, using the official Cboe CFE aggregate daily volume/open-interest CSV `https://cdn.cboe.com/data/us/futures/market_statistics/historical_data/cfevoloi.csv`. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_targeted_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_fine_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_path_screen.py`, and `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_path_top.csv`; raw cache: `/private/tmp/cboe_cfevoloi.csv`; ES caches: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet` plus active-roll Databento 1-minute paths. The no-write fixed-window screens shifted each CFE daily observation by one ES session, tested aggregate VX total volume, total open interest, volume/OI ratio, changes, ranks, and z-scores against Apex-compatible RTH windows, and then ran a narrow managed-path audit on the strongest low-open-interest late-day long cluster with stop-first 1-minute stop/target handling. The broad fixed screen tested 49,344 rows with zero pass-shaped rows and one near row; the best was `vx_total_oi_rank63 <= 0.10`, long 13:30-15:30, with WFA n450/PF 1.460/MAR 0.461/expectancy R 0.214 and incubation n76/PF 1.384/MAR 1.256. The managed-path audit tested 291,060 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows; the best score remained `z63 <= -1.275`, long 13:30-15:45 with `stop_pct=0.012` and `target_r=2.0`, at WFA n486/PF 1.495/MAR 0.879/expectancy R 0.225, core n98/PF 2.494, and incubation n91/PF 1.577/MAR 2.602. Rows with enough WFA density diluted below the PF gate, e.g. `rank42 <= 0.15`, long 13:30-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.012` and `target_r=2.0`, had WFA n573/PF 1.452/MAR 0.696/expectancy R 0.214 with solid core/incubation. Rejected because official Cboe aggregate VX activity is reliable point-in-time data with a conservative one-session lag, but the edge still cannot clear WFA trade count and PF together under current costs; do not rerun as a low-VX-open-interest or VIX-futures-activity late-day long variant without materially new structure.

Source reviewed: Federal Reserve balance-sheet/liquidity state and intermediary-risk-capacity literature; the official H.4.1 release page says the data are generally released Thursday at 4:30 p.m., and data came from public FRED mirrors of official H.4.1 weekly series for total Fed assets (`WALCL`), reserve balances (`WRESBAL`), and Treasury General Account (`WTREGEN`). Rejected because weekly Fed liquidity state is usable with conservative lag, but the ES intraday edge remains below WFA PF/expectancy and incubation MAR/economics; do not rerun as a simple Fed-balance-sheet/reserves/TGA liquidity-state variant without adding a materially different source variable such as a reliable official daily RRP feed.

- Official credit/default-spread data-source audit: rejected before implementation at the data gate for the intended OAS and Treasury-spread construction. Source reviewed: default-spread and credit-risk expected-return literature. The intended source variables were public FRED graph CSV series for ICE BofA high-yield OAS (`BAMLH0A0HYM2`), broad corporate OAS (`BAMLC0A0CM`), Moody Baa-minus-10Y (`BAA10Y`), and Aaa-minus-10Y (`AAA10Y`). Direct downloads of the two ICE BofA OAS series succeeded only with a 2023-06-09 start date, leaving no usable WFA history. Direct 60-second downloads of `BAA10Y` and `AAA10Y` repeatedly timed out with zero bytes received. A 2026-06-14 retry confirmed the data gate for those series: the FRED series pages were reachable, but plain graph CSV downloads still timed out with zero bytes, cookie-jar graph CSV attempts failed with HTTP/2 internal errors, HTTP/1.1 graph CSV attempts timed out, and `/private/tmp/fred_credit_spread_retry` contained only tiny cookie files rather than usable observation CSVs. Rejected for the intended OAS/BAA10Y/AAA10Y branch because no unattended public data path currently supplies enough reliable, long-history observations; a separate Moody Baa/Aaa monthly-yield follow-up is rejected below.
- Moody Baa/Aaa corporate-yield spread ES mean-reversion screen: rejected before staged implementation as the reopened no-cost credit-spread follow-up. Source was the official FRED graph CSVs for Moody seasoned Baa and Aaa corporate bond yields (`BAA`, `AAA`), cached in `/private/tmp/fred_credit_spread_retry_20260614/BAA.csv` and `/private/tmp/fred_credit_spread_retry_20260614/AAA.csv` with 1,289 monthly rows from 1919-01-01 through 2026-05-01. Scratch outputs: `/private/tmp/fred_moody_corporate_spread_raw.csv`, `/private/tmp/fred_moody_corporate_spread_features.csv`, `/private/tmp/fred_moody_corporate_spread_es_screen_all.csv`, and `/private/tmp/fred_moody_corporate_spread_es_screen_top.csv`; ES cache: `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet`. No-lookahead handling made each monthly observation eligible only after month-end plus 45 calendar days and one business day. The screen built Baa yield, Aaa yield, Baa-minus-Aaa spread, Baa/Aaa ratio, 1/3/6/12-month changes and percentage changes, 3/6/12-month mean gaps, 12/24/60/120-month ranks and z-scores, and credit-stress composites. It tested 1,340 credit-state thresholds across 42,880 ES same-day mean-reversion rows (`prior_down` long or `prior_up` short), using entries `09:35`, `10:00`, `10:30`, `11:00`, `13:30`, and `14:30`, exits `12:00`, `15:30`, and `15:59`, one ES contract, and `$30` round-turn cost. Results: zero pass-like rows, zero near-like rows, zero loose-like rows, zero rows with `wfa_n >= 500` and `wfa_pf >= 1.5`, zero rows with `wfa_n >= 500` and `wfa_pf >= 1.4`, zero rows with `wfa_n >= 400`, `wfa_pf >= 1.4`, `incubation_n >= 50`, and `incubation_pf >= 1.2`, and zero rows with `wfa_n >= 300`, `wfa_pf >= 1.35`, `incubation_n >= 40`, and `incubation_pf >= 1.1`. Top-scoring rows were sparse WFA artifacts or failed incubation, e.g. `baa_minus_aaa_mean12 <= 0.681667`, `prior_up` short `10:30 -> 12:00`, with WFA n31/PF 2.203/MAR 3.931/avg `$228.87`, core n17/PF 3.216, incubation n157/PF 0.924/MAR -0.292, and early n28/PF 0.598. Rejected because the simple long-history Baa/Aaa credit-state translation does not produce a dense, split-stable ES intraday mean-reversion edge; do not rerun simple Moody Baa, Aaa, Baa-minus-Aaa, Baa/Aaa ratio, credit-stress rank, z-score, shock, or relief variants without materially different point-in-time credit data or execution confirmation.
- New York Fed ACM Treasury term-premium data-source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: Adrian, Crump, and Moench (2013), "Pricing the Term Structure with Linear Regressions", Journal of Financial Economics, and the New York Fed Treasury Term Premia page. The page exposes `/medialibrary/media/research/data_indicators/acmPlot_data.csv` and `https://www.newyorkfed.org/medialibrary/media/research/data_indicators/ACMTermPremium.xls`; scratch downloads: `/private/tmp/nyfed_acmPlot_data.csv` and `/private/tmp/ACMTermPremium.xls`. The CSV is monthly only, while the Excel workbook contains a daily `ACM Daily` sheet from 1961-06-14 through the latest month with fitted yields, term premia, and risk-neutral yields for maturities 1-10. However, the NY Fed notes that the ACM model is re-estimated once a month and this can change historical decompositions of Treasury yields. Without point-in-time vintage workbooks, a backtest using the current daily sheet would see revised historical term-premium estimates that were not necessarily available on each trade date. Rejected before screening because the public current workbook is not a reliable no-hindsight dataset for acceptance; revisit only if archived monthly ACM vintage files or another point-in-time term-premium source are available.
- OFR Financial Stress Index daily stress-state screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: official Office of Financial Research FSI page `https://www.financialresearch.gov/financial-stress-index/`, which describes the OFR FSI as a daily market-based stress snapshot and states that it publishes data current from two business days prior. Raw data endpoint used: `https://www.financialresearch.gov/financial-stress-index/data/fsi.csv`, cached at `/private/tmp/ofr_fsi.csv` with 6,686 observations from 2000-01-03 onward. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/ofr_fsi_fast_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/ofr_fsi_fast_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/ofr_fsi_path_screen.py`, and `/private/tmp/ofr_fsi_path_screen_top.csv`; ES caches: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet` plus active-roll Databento 1-minute paths. The no-write screen shifted each OFR observation by two business days before ES eligibility, then tested headline, category, and regional stress levels/changes/ranks/z-scores across Apex-compatible intraday windows. The fixed-window scan tested 249,480 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and three near rows. Best fixed row was `other_advanced_economies_diff21_rank21 <= 0.20`, long 09:35-16:00, with WFA n700/PF 1.380/MAR 0.490/expectancy R 0.170 versus required MAR 0.622, and incubation n84/PF 1.530/MAR 1.476/expectancy R 0.189. A narrow stop-first managed-path audit around the near clusters tested 5,292 rows with zero pass-shaped rows and 11 near rows; best managed row was the same stress-reversal cluster, long 10:00-16:00 with `stop_pct=0.010` and `target_r=1.0`, at WFA n700/PF 1.353/MAR 0.458/expectancy R 0.153 and incubation n84/PF 1.558/MAR 1.643/expectancy R 0.226. Rejected because OFR FSI is reliable and real-time-usable with conservative two-business-day lag, but the edge cannot meet WFA PF/MAR/expectancy under current costs; do not rerun as a renamed official-financial-stress, safe-asset-stress, or global-stress reversal filter without materially new structure.
- NY Fed/OFR primary-dealer securities-lending and fails screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: New York Fed Primary Dealer Statistics and the OFR Short-term Funding Monitor `nypd` dataset. The OFR page states these series are typically published weekly on Thursday by the New York Fed for the prior week and added to OFR the following business day. Raw endpoint used: `https://data.financialresearch.gov/v1/series/dataset?dataset=nypd`, cached at `/private/tmp/ofr_nypd_dataset.json`; source docs: `https://www.financialresearch.gov/short-term-funding-monitor/datasets/nypd/` and `https://www.newyorkfed.org/markets/primarydealers`. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/ofr_primary_dealer_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/ofr_primary_dealer_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/ofr_primary_dealer_path_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/ofr_primary_dealer_path_screen_top.csv`, and series map `/private/tmp/ofr_primary_dealer_series_map.csv`. The no-write fixed screen kept only current series with at least 500 non-null weekly observations and latest 2026 coverage, shifted Wednesday observations by two business days before ES eligibility, and tested securities-lending/securities-borrowed/fails levels, changes, percent changes, ranks, and z-scores across Apex-compatible RTH windows. It used 50 live series, 3,150 generated features, tested 1,317,988 rows, and found zero pass-shaped rows and 22 near rows. Best fixed row was `sl_treasury_excluding_tips_overnight_open_diff1_rank52 <= 0.30`, long 10:30-15:30, with WFA n646/PF 1.398/MAR 0.587/expectancy R 0.177 versus required MAR 0.691, and incubation n130/PF 1.507/MAR 1.579/expectancy R 0.203. A focused stop-first managed-path audit over the 22 near rows tested 1,540 rows, found zero pass-shaped rows and 398 near rows; the best managed row was the same securities-lending contraction cluster with `stop_pct=0.012` and `target_r=2.0`, at WFA n646/PF 1.429/MAR 0.891/expectancy R 0.191 and incubation n130/PF 1.545/MAR 2.625/expectancy R 0.218. Rejected because the external data are public and real-time-usable with conservative publication lag, but the strongest dealer-balance-sheet plumbing edge still misses WFA PF 1.5 and expectancy R 0.2 under current costs; do not rerun as a renamed primary-dealer securities-lending, dealer-fails, or Treasury-collateral-pressure filter without materially new structure.
- Official Nasdaq daily market-breadth data-source follow-up: rejected before implementation at the data-source gate. The public Nasdaq Trader Daily Market Files page exposes current-year files such as `https://nasdaqtrader.com/dynamic/dailyfiles/daily2026.csv` with date, index levels, trades, volume, dollar volume, market value, advances, declines, and unchanged counts. Shell probes confirmed the 2026 CSV is real, but deterministic historical URLs for 2006, 2010, 2014, 2020, 2024, and 2025 returned HTML error pages despite HTTP 200, and the page markup only listed 2024 links that are no longer reliable. Rejected because there is no unattended official historical data path spanning WFA and incubation; do not reopen market-breadth/advance-decline participation unless a licensed or official archival source is added.
- Wikimedia pageview investor-attention screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: Da, Engelberg, and Gao (2011), "In Search of Attention", Journal of Finance 66(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.2011.01679.x`; data source was the official Wikimedia Analytics Pageviews API documentation `https://doc.wikimedia.org/generated-data-platform/aqs/analytics-api/reference/page-views.html`, which states pageview analytics endpoints start on 2015-07-01. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/wiki_attention_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/wiki_attention_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/wiki_attention_path_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/wiki_attention_path_top.csv`; raw cache: `/private/tmp/wiki_attention_pageviews.csv`; ES caches: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet` plus active-roll 1-minute Databento files. The no-write screen downloaded 16 English Wikipedia article series from 2015-07-01 through 2026-06-08, used `all-access/user` daily counts, and made each UTC daily pageview observation tradable only from the next calendar day before ES RTH. Features included log pageviews, one-/three-/seven-day changes, rolling means, ranks, z-scores, and aggregate risk/market attention sums for pages such as `Stock_market_crash`, `Recession`, `Inflation`, `Federal_Reserve`, `S&P_500`, `VIX`, `Bear_market`, and `Treasury_bond`. The fixed-window screen tested 1,372,466 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and 10 near rows. Best fixed row was low Treasury-bond page attention, `treasury_bond_mean3_rank252 <= 0.20`, long 11:00-16:00, with full n702/PF 1.471/MAR 0.778/expectancy R 0.222, core n106/PF 1.306/MAR 0.696/expectancy R 0.150, WFA n622/PF 1.354/MAR 0.592/expectancy R 0.169 versus required MAR 0.718, and incubation n80/PF 2.220/MAR 2.228/expectancy R 0.519. A focused stop-first managed-path audit around the near clusters tested 11,529 rows, found zero pass-shaped rows and 78 near rows. Best managed row was the same Treasury-bond attention-low cluster, long 11:00-16:00 with `stop_pct=0.008` and `target_r=4.0`, at full n702/PF 1.484/MAR 0.828/expectancy R 0.232, core n106/PF 1.201/MAR 0.423/expectancy R 0.101, WFA n622/PF 1.392/MAR 0.759/expectancy R 0.190, and incubation n80/PF 1.986/MAR 1.834/expectancy R 0.419. Rejected because public web-attention data are reliable and real-time-usable with a one-day lag, but the dense ES intraday translations miss WFA PF/expectancy and/or core robustness; do not rerun as Wikipedia attention, web-search attention proxy, or low-crisis-attention long exposure without materially new data or structure.
- OFR U.S. Money Market Fund Data Release source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: official OFR STFM `mmf` dataset page `https://www.financialresearch.gov/short-term-funding-monitor/datasets/mmf/` and API endpoint `https://data.financialresearch.gov/v1/series/dataset?dataset=mmf`. The endpoint is public and returned 42 monthly series; most aggregate series span 2010-11-30 through 2026-04-30, while the shorter manager-year subset starts in 2016. However, the series metadata for the 2010-start aggregates explicitly lists `vintage_approach` and `vintage` as `Monthly Revisions - Complete Series`, and the release is based on SEC Form N-MFP filings plus OFR mappings. Rejected because the current OFR API would use revised historical series and mappings without point-in-time vintages. Do not use OFR MMF as an acceptance candidate unless raw SEC N-MFP filings are reconstructed by filing date or OFR point-in-time monthly vintages are available.
- OFR Hedge Fund Monitor SEC Form PF source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: official OFR Hedge Fund Monitor API page `https://www.financialresearch.gov/hedge-fund-monitor/api/` and dataset endpoint `https://data.financialresearch.gov/hf/v1/series/dataset?dataset=fpf`. The default endpoint returned 329 quarterly SEC Form PF aggregate hedge-fund series from 2013-03-31 through 2025-12-31, but metadata labels the data `Current vintage, as of last update`; documented `vintage=f`, `vintage=p`, and `vintage=a` dataset requests returned HTTP 502 from the public API during the audit. Rejected because the available public aggregate history is current-vintage only and not reconstructible point-in-time from this endpoint. Do not use OFR Form PF hedge-fund aggregates unless the API vintage requests are repaired and release lags are modeled, or raw Form PF aggregates are available as point-in-time vintages.
- OFR Hedge Fund Monitor SCOOS dealer-financing survey screen: rejected before implementation as a conservative survey-state pre-screen. Source reviewed: OFR HFM API `scoos` dataset, which returned 13 quarterly Senior Credit Officer Opinion Survey-style dealer-financing series from 2011-09-30 through 2026-03-31, also labeled `Current vintage, as of last update`. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/hfm_scoos_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/hfm_scoos_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/hfm_scoos_screen_all.csv`; raw cache: `/private/tmp/ofr_hfm_scoos.csv`. The highest-scoring rows were not valid candidates: `internalcharges_diff2 <= -1`, long 11:00-15:45, had full n725/PF 1.355/MAR 0.564/expectancy R 0.158, WFA n558/PF 1.252/MAR 0.435/expectancy R 0.116, no 2021-2022 core trades, and incubation n42/PF 2.531/MAR 31.38/expectancy R 0.547, below incubation density. Other hedge-fund credit-availability rows were strong only in the latest holdout but had WFA PF near 1.10. Rejected because SCOOS survey state does not meet WFA PF/MAR/expectancy or core/incubation density under conservative availability assumptions; do not rerun as a dealer-financing survey or hedge-fund-credit-conditions state without materially new structure.
- New York Fed overnight reverse-repo liquidity screen: rejected before implementation after confirming the official daily source path is usable. Source reviewed: New York Fed Repo Operations page and reverse-repo FAQ; the page says operation results include repo and reverse-repo operations, and the FAQ says ON RRP operations are scheduled every business day from 12:45 p.m. to 1:15 p.m. ET. Raw endpoint used: `https://markets.newyorkfed.org/api/rp/reverserepo/propositions/search.csv?startDate=2010-01-01&endDate=2026-06-09`, cached at `/private/tmp/nyfed_repo_rrp_operations.csv`; the paired repo endpoint returned HTTP 400 and was not used. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/nyfed_repo_rrp_liquidity_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/nyfed_repo_rrp_liquidity_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/nyfed_repo_rrp_liquidity_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/nyfed_repo_rrp_multislot_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/nyfed_repo_rrp_multislot_all.csv`. The no-write fixed-window screen loaded 3,251 RRP operation rows from 2010-08-04 through 2026-06-08, shifted each observation by one business day before ES eligibility, built total accepted amount plus bank/GSE/MMF/primary-dealer accepted amount changes, percent changes, ranks, and z-scores, then tested Apex-compatible RTH windows. It evaluated 213,012 fixed rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and six near rows. Best fixed cluster was high five-day RRP change, `reverserepo_total_bil_diff5_z504 >= 0.5`, long late-day: 14:30-15:30 had WFA n513/PF 1.557/MAR 0.869/expectancy R 0.274 and core n184/PF 2.050, but incubation was only n61/PF 1.307/MAR 1.008/expectancy R 0.146, below density and incubation economics. The 14:30-16:00 sibling had incubation PF/MAR but WFA PF only 1.415 and incubation n61. A focused non-overlapping multislot rescue over the same RRP cluster tested 3,298 rows and found zero pass-shaped or near rows; adding early slots lifted incubation trade count but diluted WFA PF and expectancy, e.g. `diff5_z504 >= 0.5`, 09:35-11:00 plus 14:30-16:00, had WFA n1,037/PF 1.200/MAR 0.393 despite incubation n125/PF 1.648. Rejected because official RRP data are reliable and real-time-usable with a conservative next-business-day lag, but the ES edge cannot satisfy WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and incubation density together. Do not rerun as a simple RRP-drain, money-market-liquidity, or Fed-liability-substitution state without materially new source structure.

- CME Group ES daily volume/open-interest public FTP audit: rejected before implementation at the data-access gate. Source reviewed: CME Group Volume and Open Interest page, Daily Bulletin page, and public `daily_volume` FTP listing. CME documents that the Daily Volume and Open Interest report is released at end of trading day as preliminary data and official data appears in the Daily Bulletin the following morning, so the dataset would be point-in-time usable with a next-session lag if an approved feed were available. However, unattended shell/Python requests for files such as `https://www.cmegroup.com/ftp/daily_volume/daily_volume_20170103.xlsx` and `daily_volume_20260605.xlsx` returned HTTP 403 JSON stating the IP is blocked for suspected scraping and that automated/commercial access should use other CME delivery methods. The local Databento cache contains only `ohlcv-1m` bars, not daily open interest. Rejected because the public CME website/FTP path is not a reliable automatable source for acceptance; revisit only if a licensed/approved CME/Databento daily VOI or open-interest feed is added.

- FINRA OTC Transparency ATS/non-ATS security-level volume source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data gate. Source reviewed: FINRA OTC Transparency data-download API documentation and the public Query API datasets for `weeklySummary` and `weeklySummaryHistoric`. The current weekly endpoint returned valid 2024 SPY records with `initialPublishedDate`, `lastReportedDate`, `tierIdentifier`, MPID, share quantity, notional, and trade count fields, so the data would be real-time usable for recent observations with the documented two-week Tier 1 delay. However, the historical endpoint rejected 2018-06-25 and 2020-06-22 requests with `minDate=2021-06-08 maxDate=2025-06-07`; a 2024-06-24 request succeeded. Because the available unattended official history spans only about four years and cannot cover the required full WFA/incubation protocol, no ES screen was run. Do not reopen this as a simple FINRA OTC volume, ATS-share, TRF-share, or ETF off-exchange activity state unless a full official historical archive or licensed point-in-time data feed is added.
- OCC underlying option-volume pressure source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data gate. Source reviewed: official OCC Volume Query and Volume Query Batch Processing documentation. The endpoint `https://marketdata.theocc.com/volume-query` supports daily option-volume CSV downloads by underlying symbol, call/put, account type, exchange, and report date, so recent SPY/SPX option-volume pressure would be real-time usable after the session close. Shell probes confirmed recent data for SPY and SPX on 2024-06-24 and SPY on 2026-06-05, including `quantity`, `underlying`, `symbol`, `actype`, `porc`, `exchange`, and `actdate`. However, the same endpoint rejected 2010-06-15 and 2019-05-31 SPY/SPX requests with `Report date cannot be prior to  2 years`. Because the official unattended underlying-level history is limited to roughly two years, no ES screen was run. Do not reopen this as SPY/SPX/QQQ/IWM option-volume pressure, underlying put/call volume, or account-type option-flow state unless a licensed/historical OCC or OPRA-derived point-in-time archive is added.
- NYSE program-trading / index-arbitrage flow source audit: rejected before implementation at the public data-access gate. Source family reviewed: NYSE weekly Program Trading Reports and index-arbitrage/program-trading microstructure literature. Old public static PDFs such as `PT030110.pdf` and `PT122812.pdf` are still reachable, confirming the historical report format, but guessed current 2025/2026 report URLs returned 404. The current NYSE reports page states its equities reports are produced for permit holders and distributed through NYSE Managed File Transfer after account setup; it did not expose a reliable public current/full-history download path for program-trading reports. - OCC combined Reg SHO threshold-securities source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data gate. Source reviewed: official OCC Threshold Securities List and Batch Processing documentation. The endpoint `https://marketdata.theocc.com/threshold-securities?reportDate=YYYYMMDD` returns current/recent pipe-delimited combined threshold-security lists with symbol, security name, market category, and Reg SHO threshold flag; recent probes for 2026-05-15 through 2026-06-05 succeeded. - Federal Reserve H.8 commercial-bank credit source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: official Federal Reserve/FRED/ALFRED H.8 weekly commercial-bank balance-sheet series such as total bank credit (`TOTBKCR`), commercial and industrial loans (`BUSLOANS`), and real-estate loans (`REALLN`). - SEC EDGAR filing-activity / disclosure-congestion screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source framing: investor-attention and disclosure-congestion literature such as Hirshleifer, Lim, and Teoh (2009), "Driven to Distraction: Extraneous Events and Underreaction to Earnings News"; data source was the official SEC EDGAR master index at `https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/full-index/{year}/QTR{quarter}/master.idx`, with spot checks against daily index files such as `https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/daily-index/2024/QTR2/master.20240624.idx`. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/sec_edgar_filing_activity_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_edgar_filing_activity_screen_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_edgar_filing_activity_screen_all.csv`; raw quarterly index cache: `/private/tmp/sec_edgar_full_index_cache`. The no-write screen parsed 16,847,828 EDGAR filing rows from 2010-Q2 through 2026-Q2, collapsed them into 5,842 daily form-count observations, shifted each daily filing-count feature by one business day before ES eligibility, then tested 1,375 filing-count/share/change/rank/z-score features against Apex-compatible same-day RTH windows. It evaluated 1,328,094 fixed-window rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and one near row. The only near row was high 21-day registration-filing activity, `log_registration_count_mean21_rank504 >= 0.80`, long 10:00-13:30, with full n719/PF 1.298/MAR 0.243/expectancy R 0.134, core n103/PF 1.733/MAR 7.676/expectancy R 0.285, WFA n478/PF 1.469/MAR 0.897/expectancy R 0.205 versus required MAR 0.653, and incubation n86/PF 1.114/MAR 0.453/expectancy R 0.051. Dense rows that cleared WFA n>=500 and PF>=1.5, such as high issuance/prospectus pressure late-day longs, failed incubation badly with PF below 0.75 and negative MAR. Rejected because official EDGAR filing activity is public and point-in-time reconstructible with daily-index reconstruction plus a conservative one-business-day lag, but simple aggregate filing-count/disclosure-congestion states do not meet WFA trade-count/PF and incubation economics together. Do not rerun as a simple EDGAR filing-count, registration-filing pressure, 8-K share, prospectus/issuance pressure, insider-filing pressure, or disclosure-congestion state without materially new structure and daily-index point-in-time reconstruction.
- CFTC TFF tiered hedging-pressure staged candidate: rejected after promotion from the external-data ensemble/tiered pre-screen. Source remains de Roon, Nijman, and Veld (2000), "Hedging Pressure Effects in Futures Markets", DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00253`; data source is the existing official CFTC TFF feature file `data/external/cftc_tff_hedging_pressure_features.csv`, using Tuesday report positions no earlier than following Monday RTH. First failed gate: walk-forward analysis. Limited core grid passed with 108 combinations, 106 profitable iterations (98.15%), and zero Apex violations. Rejected because tiered CFTC TFF timing can pass core and monkey but does not survive rolling WFA selection; do not rerun as a high-vs-broad CFTC TFF tier, priority COT fallback, or CFTC open-interest expansion ensemble without materially new data or structure.

- Event no-trade post-hoc audit on completed WFA near-pass logs: rejected before implementation. Targeted the only existing configs that reached 10-window WFA with meaningful OOS logs, `morning_intraday_momentum_continuation/5m/long_only_strength`, `long_only_pf_selector`, and `long_only_strong_signal`. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/wfa_event_day_posthoc_screen.csv`. Removing FOMC-day trades helped PF/MAR slightly but still failed WFA economics and, for the 508-trade variants, dropped total trades below the 500 WFA gate: best post-hoc row was `long_only_pf_selector` FOMC-day removal with 498 trades, PF 1.137, MAR 0.244, expectancy R 0.063 versus required PF 1.5, MAR 1.5, expectancy R 0.2, and 500 trades. NFP-day removal worsened all three variants; combined FOMC+NFP removal also failed. Rejected because macro-day removal does not rescue the only WFA-complete morning momentum near-pass family and should not be promoted to retrained WFA unless a future pre-screen shows PF/MAR/expectancy can move by much more than simple event-day deletion.
- Event no-trade rescue audit, `opening_range_filtered_breakout/2m/vwap_aligned_fixed_r`: rejected before implementation. This was the next strongest limited-monkey near-pass after the PDH/PDL fresh-close test; the original default core had 203 trades, net $1,062.50, max DD $3,780, and failed limited monkey only on net-profit beat rate at 76.10% while max-DD beat rate passed at 99.8625%. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/event_blackout_orb_vwap_2m.csv`. Removing FOMC days improved net profit to $2,565 and monkey net/DD beat rates to 80.25%/99.8625%, but still missed the 90% net-profit beat gate. Removing approximate NFP days gave net/DD beat rates 75.4625%/99.9125%. Removing FOMC+NFP gave 80.825%/99.85%. All variants had zero Apex violations but failed limited monkey; do not promote a simple FOMC/NFP macro-day blackout for this ORB/VWAP-aligned breakout.
- Event no-trade core-grid rescue audit, `pdh_pdl_breakout_continuation/2m/gap_hold_continuation`: rejected before implementation. This candidate had failed limited core by a narrow breadth miss: 72/108 profitable iterations, 66.67%, versus the 70% threshold. Scratch path: `/private/tmp/event_blackout_gap_hold_2m_core_grid.csv`, with detailed grids at `/private/tmp/event_blackout_gap_hold_2m_fomc_day_core_grid_results.csv` and `/private/tmp/event_blackout_gap_hold_2m_nfp_day_approx_core_grid_results.csv`. Removing FOMC days worsened breadth to 70/108 profitable iterations, 64.81%, top net $14,820, PF 1.385, MAR 1.702, zero Apex violations. Removing approximate NFP days also worsened breadth to 70/108, 64.81%, top net $15,470, PF 1.439, MAR 1.886, zero Apex violations. The combined FOMC+NFP grid was stopped after both component filters moved the first gate in the wrong direction and the combined run was progressing slowly. Rejected because simple macro-day blackouts do not rescue the core-grid robustness failure for this gap-hold family.
- Prior-session range-compression / NR breakout audit: rejected before implementation as a local 1-minute OHLCV technical-rule follow-up. Source framing: Brock, Lakonishok, and LeBaron (1992), "Simple Technical Trading Rules and the Stochastic Properties of Stock Returns", Journal of Finance 47(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1992.tb04681.x`, which tests trading-range-break rules. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/prior_range_compression_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/prior_range_compression_flat_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/prior_range_compression_flat_all.csv`, and `/private/tmp/prior_range_compression_path_top.csv`. The no-write ES translation used only completed prior RTH daily range/inside-day state (`NR4`, `NR7`, `NR14`, inside day, and prior range-rank compression) plus current-session completed source return, break, expansion, and close-location confirmation before next-bar entries, with Apex-compatible same-session exits no later than 16:00 ET. It evaluated 6,604 flat rows and a bounded 300-row stop/target rescue subset, with zero dynamic near rows and zero dynamic pass-shaped rows under the length-adjusted WFA MAR rule. Top rows were too sparse despite high PF, e.g. `nr7_strong_close_0.2_cont`, long 13:00-15:30, had WFA n111/PF 2.602/MAR 1.218 versus required MAR 0.671, but only core n27 and incubation n19. Dense rows with WFA n>=450, core n>=50, and incubation n>=50 diluted into weak or negative economics; for example `range_rank21_lo30_up_break_x0.25_cont`, long 13:30-15:30, had WFA n467/PF 1.037/MAR 0.032 and incubation PF 0.844/MAR -0.206. Rejected because prior-session range compression can create sparse high-PF pockets but cannot meet WFA trade-count, core density, and incubation economics together; do not rerun as simple NR4/NR7/NR14, inside-day, prior-range-rank compression, or trading-range-break confirmation without materially new structure.
- ICI aggregate fund-flow / money-market-fund asset source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data-access gate. Source reviewed: Investment Company Institute weekly estimated long-term mutual fund flows, weekly combined mutual-fund/ETF flows, weekly ETF net issuance, and weekly money-market-fund assets pages. The current public release pages expose recent summary XLS files and tables, but the ICI weekly estimated-flow reports page lists the historical long-term flow and ETF net-issuance XLS reports behind "Login or click here to get access to our Member Statistical Report"; the money-market-fund-assets pages likewise provide recent summary data while full historical reports are member/subscription-gated, and the public release notes say weekly money-market assets for only the last 20 weeks are available. Because the accessible public history is far too short for WFA/incubation and the full historical source requires member/statistical-subscription access, no ES screen was run. Do not reopen as ICI mutual-fund flows, ETF net issuance, combined fund flows, or money-market-fund asset-flow state unless a licensed/approved historical feed with release timing is added.
- Low-volatility overextension reversion screen: rejected before implementation as a local 1-minute OHLCV overlap follow-up to the already rejected intraday overreaction, VWAP/large-bar reversion, and prior-session reversal branches. Scratch result paths: `/private/tmp/low_vol_overextension_reversion_screen_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/low_vol_overextension_reversion_screen_all.csv`. The no-write screen tested same-session overextension from the RTH open or prior close inside low prior-volatility/range regimes, with Apex-compatible same-day exits. It found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. The highest-ranked rows were one-trade artifacts. The densest rows had no acceptable WFA shape; for example low 20-day range rank <=0.3, short/long overextension from prior close with 13:00 or 13:30 entry and 16:00 exit reached full n581, but only WFA n352-358, WFA PF about 1.11-1.13, WFA MAR about 0.06, and incubation n61-68. Rejected because low-volatility overextension reversion either over-filters into tiny samples or dilutes into weak WFA economics; do not rerun as simple low-vol range-bound overextension, open/previous-close deviation fade, or low-range mean reversion without materially new structure or true bid/ask/order-book data.
- Exchange-traded ES calendar-spread activity screen: rejected before implementation as a local Databento 1-minute OHLCV contract-structure candidate distinct from, but adjacent to, the already rejected front/next curve and adjacent-basis branches. Source reviewed: Holmes and Rougier (2005), "Trading volume and contract rollover in futures contracts", Journal of Empirical Finance 12(2), DOI `10.1016/j.jempfin.2004.01.003`, which documents futures volume seasonality around quarterly rollover and includes S&P 500 futures. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/es_calendar_spread_activity_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/es_calendar_spread_activity_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/es_calendar_spread_activity_all.csv`. The no-write screen used the existing ES active RTH cache `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` plus local Databento spread rows whose `contract_symbol` starts with `ES` and contains `-`, yielding 448,807 spread bars across 4,097 sessions. Features used only completed pre-entry spread bars: top spread symbol by source-window volume, spread-symbol volume, total spread volume, spread-symbol count, spread price change/absolute change, spread-volume share versus outright ES volume, and prior 21/63/126/252-session rolling ranks. It tested Apex-compatible 10:00, 10:30, 11:00, 13:00, 13:30, and 14:30 entries against same-session exits through 16:00 with current ES costs. It evaluated 1,867 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Dense rows were weak: the best positive-PF rows with high WFA trade counts had WFA n646-729, PF about 1.01-1.08, MAR about 0.007-0.081, and expectancy R near zero; sparse high-PF rows failed coverage, with examples showing WFA n20-58 and no 2021-2022 core trades. Rejected because exchange-traded calendar-spread activity either over-filters into tiny/no-core samples or dilutes into weak WFA economics; do not rerun as simple ES calendar-spread activity, spread-volume pressure, roll-spread volume, or roll-pressure seasonality without materially new data or structure.
- VIX ETP flow/pressure screen: rejected before implementation as an overlap-adjacent but distinct volatility-ETP candidate. Source reviewed: Bangsgaard and Kokholm (2024 revision), "The Stock Market Impact of Volatility Hedging: Evidence from End-of-Day Trading by VIX ETPs", SSRN `10.2139/ssrn.4470636`, which studies VIX ETP issuer demand and SPX futures impact. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/vix_etp_flow_pressure_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/vix_etp_flow_pressure_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/vix_etp_flow_pressure_all.csv`; raw provisional Yahoo cache: `/private/tmp/yahoo_vix_etp_daily_cache.csv`. The no-write ES translation used prior-day adjusted closes/volumes for VXX, VXZ, UVXY, SVXY, VIXY, VIXM, and TVIX, while XIV was unavailable from Yahoo. Features included ETP returns, dollar-volume changes, signed dollar-pressure proxies, long-vol aggregate pressure, inverse-vol aggregate pressure, and long-minus-inverse ETP imbalance ranks/z-scores. All signals were shifted one trading day before ES RTH eligibility and traded Apex-compatible same-session windows through `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current ES costs. It evaluated 30,006 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and one loose near row. The near row was low VIXM signed dollar pressure, `VIXM_signed_dollar_pressure1_rank126 <= 0.2`, long 09:35-13:30: full n697/PF 1.436/MAR 0.407, core n93/PF 1.468/MAR 0.858, WFA n508/PF 1.415/MAR 0.421/expectancy R 0.175 versus required MAR 0.622, and incubation n61/PF 1.642/MAR 2.145/expectancy R 0.273. A focused stop/target rescue script `/private/tmp/vix_etp_flow_pressure_path_screen.py` was started around this cluster but intentionally terminated after about 4:44 CPU minutes because the fixed near row already failed WFA PF, WFA MAR, core MAR, and incubation density, and the unoptimized path loop had not produced a result. Rejected because VIX ETP flow proxies are interesting but remain below WFA PF/MAR and incubation-density gates, and any future promotion would also require a production-grade point-in-time ETP OHLCV/AUM data feed rather than Yahoo; do not rerun as simple VXX/VXZ/VIXM/UVXY/SVXY return, volume, dollar-volume, or signed-pressure ES timing without materially new source structure.
- Equity-ETF liquidity/Amihud pressure screen: rejected before implementation as a distinct daily ETF OHLCV liquidity-state audit, not a FINRA short-sale or sector-return branch. Source reviewed: Amihud (2002), "Illiquidity and Stock Returns: Cross-Section and Time-Series Effects", Journal of Financial Markets 5(1), DOI `10.1016/S1386-4181(01)00024-6`. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/etf_liquidity_pressure_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/etf_liquidity_pressure_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/etf_liquidity_pressure_all.csv`; raw provisional Yahoo cache: `/private/tmp/yahoo_equity_etf_daily_cache.csv`. The no-write ES translation used prior completed daily OHLCV for SPY, QQQ, IWM, DIA, IVV, and VOO, shifted one trade date before ES eligibility; any promotion would require a production-grade point-in-time ETF market-data feed instead of Yahoo. Features included dollar-volume changes, log dollar volume, Amihud illiquidity, range proxies, signed dollar-pressure, up/down volume pressure, and QQQ/IWM-minus-SPY relative liquidity states, then traded Apex-compatible same-session ES RTH windows through `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current ES costs. The bounded screen evaluated 9,940 feature/window rows and found 2,162 positive rows, with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Best WFA-looking rows failed holdout/incubation: `QQQ_amihud_z63 <= -1.0`, long 13:30-15:30, had full n691/PF 1.230/MAR 0.106, core n89/PF 2.065/MAR 2.997, WFA n498/PF 1.657/MAR 0.809/expectancy R 0.277 versus required WFA density 500, but incubation n61/PF 0.670/MAR -0.528. The denser `qqq_minus_spy_amihud_z21 <= -1.0` sibling had WFA n522/PF 1.685/MAR 0.709 but incubation PF 0.682 and only 73 incubation trades. Rejected because ETF liquidity stress/relief states are core/WFA-useful in pockets but invert or fail in the 2024-2026 holdout; do not rerun as simple SPY/QQQ/IWM ETF dollar-volume, Amihud, range-liquidity, signed-volume, or ETF liquidity-pressure rank/z-score without materially new structure and a production data source.
- Philadelphia Fed ADS real-time business-conditions screen: rejected before implementation after confirming the official ADS page says the index is updated in real time as underlying data are released and that all real-time vintages are available in one file. Source reviewed: Aruoba, Diebold, and Scotti (2009), "Real-Time Measurement of Business Conditions," Journal of Business and Economic Statistics 27(4), pp. 417-27, as referenced by the Philadelphia Fed ADS page. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/ads_business_conditions_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/ads_realtime_diagonal.csv`, `/private/tmp/ads_business_conditions_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/ads_business_conditions_all.csv`; raw official workbook cache: `/private/tmp/ADS_All_Vintages.xlsx`. The no-write ES translation extracted each vintage column's last non-empty observation as the real-time ADS value available for that vintage, used only the latest vintage strictly before each ES trade date, built ADS level/change/mean/volatility/rank/z-score features, and tested Apex-compatible same-session RTH windows on `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current ES costs. It evaluated 39,416 feature/window rows and found 5,741 positive rows, with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Best rows were latest-holdout-skewed rather than robust: `ads_mean4_z26 <= -0.5`, long 10:00-13:30, had full n1,338/PF 1.171/MAR 0.116, core n184/PF 1.184/MAR 0.527, WFA n967/PF 1.091/MAR 0.080/expectancy R 0.042 versus required WFA MAR 0.626, and incubation n122/PF 1.835/MAR 3.118. The best WFA-PF rows were too sparse and still weak by MAR/core coverage, e.g. `ads_vol13_z156 <= -1.5`, long 11:00-13:30, had WFA n123/PF 1.526/MAR 0.273, core n8/PF 0.530, and incubation n22. Rejected because real-time ADS macro-state filters improve some recent long-only pockets but miss WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and/or density under point-in-time alignment; do not rerun as simple ADS level, ADS deterioration/improvement, business-conditions rank/z-score, or ADS-volatility regime filter without materially new structure.
- SEC Form 13F ETF institutional-demand screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance as a distinct official point-in-time holdings-flow branch, not a simple EDGAR filing-count rerun. Source reviewed: Gompers and Metrick (2001), "Institutional Investors and Equity Prices," Quarterly Journal of Economics 116(1), DOI `10.1162/003355301556392`, plus official SEC Form 13F Data Sets documentation/page (`https://www.sec.gov/data-research/sec-markets-data/form-13f-data-sets`, data.gov mirror `https://catalog.data.gov/dataset/form-13f-data-sets`). The SEC documentation says the flat files are extracted from EDGAR Form 13F XML filings, include 13F-HR/13F-HR/A/13F-NT forms, and are published quarterly; this audit used only initial `13F-HR` share rows and shifted every filing date by one business day before ES eligibility. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_path_rescue.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_multislot_rescue.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_path_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_path_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_multislot_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_multislot_all.csv`; raw/cache paths: `/private/tmp/sec_13f_data_sets`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_filtered.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_daily_features.csv`. The no-write screen downloaded/parsing-cached 53 official SEC 13F packages, filtered to non-option share rows for SPY, QQQ, IWM, IVV, and VOO, yielding 604,754 ETF holding rows from 159,129 filings and 2,735 daily feature rows. It built filing-date ETF holdings, filing counts, new positions, one-/5-/10-/21-/42-day filing aggregates, SPY/QQQ/IWM relative-demand deltas, and rolling rank/z-score features, then tested Apex-compatible ES RTH holds on `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current costs. The fixed-window screen evaluated 27,153 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and 16 near rows. Best fixed row was low one-day IWM-minus-SPY 13F ETF-value delta rank, `iwm_minus_spy_delta_value_sum1_rank63 <= 0.2`, long 10:00-15:30: full n551/PF 1.476/MAR 0.677/expectancy R 0.204, core n78/PF 1.623/MAR 1.953, WFA n453/PF 1.453/MAR 0.609/expectancy R 0.197 versus required MAR 0.65, and incubation n64/PF 1.612/MAR 1.842/expectancy R 0.239. A focused conservative stop-first path rescue over the near cluster evaluated 8,291 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and 260 near rows; the strongest path-managed row still missed density: `iwm_minus_spy_delta_value_sum1_rank63 <= 0.2`, long 09:35-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.012`, `target_r=1.0`, had WFA n445/PF 1.509/MAR 0.755/expectancy R 0.228, core n77/PF 1.898, and incubation n64/PF 1.623. A two-slot non-overlapping rescue densified the source but diluted WFA economics: 527 rows, zero pass, zero near; best dense row (`rank63 <= 0.15`, long 10:00-13:30 plus 13:30-15:30, `stop_pct=0.010`, `target_r=1.5`) had WFA n708/PF 1.298/MAR 0.482/expectancy R 0.132 despite incubation n112/PF 1.773. Rejected because official 13F ETF institutional-demand shocks are real-time-usable only with filing-date lag but either remain under-dense at acceptable PF/MAR or dilute below the WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates when densified; do not rerun as simple SPY/QQQ/IWM/IVV/VOO 13F holding, holding-delta, filing-count, new-position, low IWM-minus-SPY demand, high SPY demand, or two-slot 13F ETF-demand timing without materially new structure.
- SEC Form 4 insider transaction pressure screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance as a distinct official point-in-time transaction-content branch, not the prior EDGAR filing-count branch. Source reviewed: Lakonishok and Lee (2001), "Are Insiders' Trades Informative?", Review of Financial Studies 14(1), DOI `10.1093/rfs/14.1.79`, plus official SEC Insider Transactions Data Sets page (`https://www.sec.gov/data-research/sec-markets-data/insider-transactions-data-sets`), which documents quarterly Form 3/4/5 XML-derived data from January 2006 through March 2026. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_path_rescue.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_path_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_path_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_gross_value_focus_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_gross_value_focus_all.csv`; raw/cache paths: `/private/tmp/sec_insider_data_sets`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_transactions_filtered.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_daily_features.csv`. The no-write screen downloaded and parsed 81 official SEC quarterly packages, filtered to Form 4 non-derivative open-market purchase/sale rows (`TRANS_CODE` P/S) with positive shares and prices, shifted every filing date by one business day before ES eligibility, and built buy/sell count, dollar value, net/gross pressure, issuer-count, rolling-sum, rank, and z-score features. Fixed-window evaluation produced 3,347,235 transaction rows from 1,220,069 filings, 5,062 daily feature rows, and 16,871 positive fixed rows, with zero pass-shaped and zero near rows. Best fixed dense rows either failed incubation, e.g. low five-day filing z-score short 10:00-13:30 with WFA n507/PF 1.591/MAR 0.652/expectancy R 0.267 but incubation n91/PF 0.802, or failed core/incubation density. A bounded stop-first path rescue over 80 WFA-useful rows found zero pass-shaped rows and six near rows. A focused low-gross-value rescue over 5,607 rows also found zero pass-shaped rows and ten near rows; best was low five-day gross transaction value rank, `gross_value_sum5_rank126 <= 0.20`, long 10:30-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.010`, `target_r=1.5`, full n824/PF 1.333/MAR 0.191, core n124/PF 1.739/MAR 2.937, WFA n688/PF 1.399/MAR 0.657/expectancy R 0.179 versus required WFA PF 1.5 and expectancy R 0.2, and incubation n111/PF 1.176/expectancy R 0.071. Rejected because official Form 4 transaction pressure is reliable and reconstructible with filing-date lag, but simple insider buy/sell pressure, issuer-count spikes, low transaction-gross-value regimes, and low filing-volume regimes cannot satisfy WFA PF/expectancy and incubation economics together; do not rerun as simple SEC insider purchase/sale count, dollar-value imbalance, gross transaction value, issuer-count, filing-count, or Form 4 pressure state without materially new structure.
- FINRA OTC/ATS ETF dark-pool and non-ATS volume source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data gate. Source reviewed: official FINRA OTC Transparency page, FINRA OTC Transparency API specification, and FINRA Developer API metadata for `weeklySummary`/`weeklySummaryHistoric`. FINRA documents weekly ATS and non-ATS symbol-level volume/trade-count reports, `initialPublishedDate`, and the publication delay for NMS Tier 1 and other securities, so the data would be point-in-time usable with a one-business-day lag after `initialPublishedDate`. Shell probes confirmed the API returns aggregate weekly symbol rows for SPY, QQQ, IWM, IVV, and VOO with `summaryTypeCode` values `ATS_W_SMBL` and `OTC_W_SMBL`; for example the 2026-05-18 partition returned both ATS and OTC aggregate rows for all five ETFs with `initialPublishedDate=2026-06-08`. However, the public `weeklySummary` endpoint returned only 233 weekly rows per ETF from 2021-12-06 through 2026-05-18, and the `weeklySummaryHistoric` partition list covered only 2021-06-14 through 2025-06-02. No ES screen was run because the accessible public history is too short for the repo's default full-history WFA protocol and would early-exit older windows as missing data. Do not reopen as FINRA ATS volume, OTC/non-ATS volume, dark-pool share, SPY/QQQ/IWM off-exchange activity, or symbol-level OTC transparency state unless a full point-in-time archive back to at least the early ES sample is available.
- FINRA TRACE fixed-income market breadth/sentiment source audit: rejected before implementation at the data-access gate. Source reviewed: FINRA Developer metadata for `corporateMarketBreadth`, `corporateMarketSentiment`, `corporate144AMarketBreadth`, `corporate144AMarketSentiment`, `agencyMarketBreadth`, `agencyMarketSentiment`, and `treasuryDailyAggregates`. These datasets would be a plausible official fixed-income-liquidity/credit-risk state source under stock-bond liquidity-linkage literature, but in this environment only metadata was accessible. FINRA partition requests for all seven datasets returned HTTP 401, and direct POST data probes for corporate breadth, corporate sentiment, and Treasury daily aggregates returned `Failed to authenticate, check your authentication token`. No ES screen was run. Do not reopen as TRACE corporate-bond breadth, corporate-bond sentiment, 144A credit-flow, agency-bond breadth, Treasury TRACE aggregate, dealer-customer Treasury volume, or fixed-income market-liquidity state unless FINRA API credentials or an approved public historical export are available.
- Official Treasury par-yield-curve term-structure screen: rejected before implementation as a bounded official-rates audit adjacent to, but cleaner than, the rejected ETF/rates-volatility stock-bond screens. Source reviewed: U.S. Treasury Daily Treasury Par Yield Curve Rates XML feed, which was responsive year by year via `https://home.treasury.gov/resource-center/data-chart-center/interest-rates/pages/xml?data=daily_treasury_yield_curve&field_tdr_date_value=YEAR`; Treasury states these are daily par yield curve rates. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/treasury_yield_curve_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/treasury_yield_curve_daily.csv`, `/private/tmp/treasury_yield_curve_screen_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/treasury_yield_curve_screen_all.csv`. The no-write screen fetched 4,110 daily observations from 2010-01-04 through 2026-06-08, shifted each curve observation by one business day before ES eligibility, and built yield levels, one-/five-/21-day changes, slopes (`10y-2y`, `10y-3m`, `30y-5y`, `5y-2y`), five-year belly curvature, level, rolling ranks, and z-scores. It evaluated fixed Apex-compatible RTH windows on `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current ES costs, producing 12,463 positive rows with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Top rows were too sparse and/or split-period fragile: one-month/three-month yield or slope-shock shorts reached WFA PF around 1.6-1.8 in 176-316 WFA trades, but missed the 500-trade gate or failed core; dense change-rank rows had WFA PF below acceptance and weak incubation. Rejected because official yield-curve state does not meet WFA density, WFA PF/MAR/expectancy, and core/incubation robustness together; do not rerun as simple Treasury yield level, yield change, curve slope, curve inversion/steepening, or belly-curvature ES timing without materially new structure.
- Federal Reserve H.10 foreign-exchange / dollar-state screen: rejected before implementation after the FRED endpoint stalled but the official Federal Reserve Data Download Program path proved usable. Source reviewed: official Fed H.10/G.5 daily rates and daily dollar-index packages via `https://www.federalreserve.gov/datadownload/Output.aspx`; raw caches `/private/tmp/h10_daily_rates.csv` and `/private/tmp/h10_daily_indexes.csv`. Because H.10 publishes the previous business week's daily observations on Monday at 16:15 ET, the no-write screen conservatively made each observation eligible on the following business day before ES RTH entry. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/h10_fx_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/h10_fx_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/h10_fx_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/h10_fx_multislot_rescue_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/h10_fx_multislot_rescue_all.csv`. The fixed-window screen evaluated 27,232 positive rows from currency USD-strength returns, dollar-index returns, basket spreads, rolling ranks, and z-scores against Apex-compatible same-session ES RTH windows, with zero pass-shaped rows and one loose near row. - Volume-clock / transaction-time intraday screen: rejected before implementation as a local 1-minute OHLCV audit. Source framing: Clark (1973), "A Subordinated Stochastic Process Model with Finite Variance for Speculative Prices", Econometrica, DOI `10.2307/1913889`, and Ané and Geman (2000), "Order Flow, Transaction Clock, and Normality of Asset Returns", Journal of Finance, DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00286`. This was not true bid/ask orderflow and did not use the session's final volume as a signal input. It generated 3,557,450 expanded trade observations and 1,571 positive grouped rows, with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. The best family was short continuation after early downside movement, e.g. 21-day expected volume, 10% to 20% source, 95% expected-volume exit, 24-tick threshold: full n417/PF 1.217/MAR 0.125, core n94/PF 1.354/MAR 1.244, WFA n301/PF 1.535/MAR 0.736/expectancy R 0.235, but incubation n82/PF 0.815/MAR -0.482. Dense early short-continuation rows had WFA n632-741 with PF only 1.34-1.40 and incubation PF near 1.1 or worse. Rejected because volume-clock timing does not satisfy WFA density, WFA PF/MAR/expectancy, and incubation economics together; do not rerun as simple expected-volume-clock continuation, volume-clock reversal, volume-bar timing, or transaction-time proxy without materially new structure or true trade-count/orderflow data.

Source framing: Kacperczyk and Schnabl (2010), "When Safe Proved Risky: Commercial Paper During the Financial Crisis of 2007-2009", Journal of Economic Perspectives 24(1), 29-50, DOI `10.1257/jep.24.1.29`, plus Brunnermeier-Pedersen funding-liquidity logic. Best managed row (`threshold=0.7`, 09:35-15:59, `stop_pct=0.016`, `target_r=4.0`) improved drawdown/holdout at full n1,143/PF 1.476/MAR 0.515, core n159/PF 1.622/MAR 2.447, WFA n692/PF 1.451/MAR 0.797/expectancy R 0.202, and incubation n113/PF 1.817/MAR 2.652. Rejected because official CP funding-stress data are reliable and point-in-time usable with a conservative one-business-day lag, but the strongest high-issuance-count long condition misses the WFA PF 1.5 gate before and after path management; do not rerun as simple CP issuance-volume rank, CP rate/spread, A2/P2-minus-AA spread, financial-commercial-paper spread, CP term-slope, or commercial-paper funding-stress filter without materially new structure.

- Federal Reserve Beige Book text-state screen: rejected before campaign promotion as a distinct public text-source branch. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/beige_book_text_state_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/beige_book_text_releases.csv`, `/private/tmp/beige_book_text_state_all.csv`, and `/private/tmp/beige_book_text_state_top.csv`; ES cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. The no-write source audit parsed 128 official release HTML pages, exactly eight releases per year from 2010 through 2025, using paired PDF links to recover dates for newer sequence-numbered summary pages and old `fomc/beigebook/YYYY/YYYYMMDD/default.htm` pages for early history. Each release was made tradable only from the next business day, then forward-filled until the next release. Dictionary features covered activity sentiment, positive/negative intensity, inflation pressure, labor tightness, uncertainty, weak-demand terms, one-release changes, rolling release z-scores, and rolling release ranks. The Apex-compatible same-session ES RTH screen evaluated 16,000 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Top WFA-PF rows were too sparse or lacked incubation, e.g. low weak-demand 16-release z-score longs reached WFA n101/PF 2.119/MAR 0.959 but had zero incubation trades; dense rows were economically flat, e.g. high weak-demand 32-release rank long 11:00-15:30 had WFA n499/PF 1.201/MAR 0.409 and only three incubation trades, while broad text states had WFA PF near 1.0-1.2. Rejected because Beige Book text state is point-in-time usable but cannot satisfy WFA density, WFA PF/MAR/expectancy, and incubation coverage together; do not rerun as simple Beige Book sentiment, Beige Book inflation/labor/uncertainty text, district commentary text, or release-to-release Beige Book text-state timing without materially stronger NLP structure and pre-screen evidence.

- NOAA ISD-Lite cloud-cover weather state: rejected before ES screen at the no-hindsight/current-coverage data gate. This branch was distinct from the prior Central Park GHCN-D temperature/precipitation/weather screen because ISD-Lite field 10 is explicit sky-condition total cloud coverage, matching the Saunders-style cloudiness/weather-mood thesis more directly. Source audit found long-history NYC-area station candidates in official NOAA ISD history/inventory, including LaGuardia `725030-14732`, JFK `744860-94789`, Newark `725020-14734`, Teterboro `725025-94741`, and Central Park `725053-94728`, with dense monthly observations through 2024 and partial 2025. However, NOAA ISD-Lite file probes showed LaGuardia 2024 and 2025 files available while `https://www.ncei.noaa.gov/pub/data/noaa/isd-lite/2026/725030-14732-2026.gz` returned 404, and the 2025 file was last modified 2025-08-29. Because the repo's acceptance protocol requires the current 2024-11-30 through 2026 incubation window and a production-realistic no-hindsight feed, no ES screen was run. Do not reopen as simple NYC ISD-Lite cloud cover, sky-condition code, oktas, cloudy/clear day, or local cloudiness weather-mood state unless a reliable point-in-time source covers the full validation/incubation period through current ES data.

- Databento ES trade-side orderflow pre-purchase screen: positive limited-sample signal, not an accepted strategy. User-provided data path: `data/raw/ES/databento-es-trades`, schema `trades`, parent symbol `ES.FUT`, 14 DBN/ZST files from 2025-06-09 through 2026-06-09. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/es_tick_orderflow_viability.py`, `/private/tmp/es_trades_active_rth_1m_orderflow_full.parquet`, `/private/tmp/es_tick_orderflow_viability_full_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/es_tick_orderflow_viability_full_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/es_tick_orderflow_viability_full_top_trades.csv`, and `/private/tmp/es_tick_orderflow_viability_full_top50_threeway.csv`. The parser used Databento trade aggressor side (`B`/`A`), filtered outright ES contracts, selected the highest-RTH-volume active contract per session, aggregated completed RTH 1-minute trade bars, used current ES round-turn cost of $30, and excluded incomplete sessions, yielding 96,720 RTH minute bars across 248 complete sessions from 2025-06-09 through 2026-06-08. Tested objective families: flow pressure continuation/fade, price-confirmed CVD continuation, large-trade pressure continuation/fade, large-trade burst continuation, CVD-price divergence fade, absorption fade, and rolling sweep-reclaim flow fade. The full local-year screen evaluated 11,631 grouped rows and found 187 loose pre-purchase candidates requiring at least 50 trades, positive 2025 train and 2026 test PnL, train/test PF >=1.2, train/test expectancy R >=0.05, and positive months >=50%. Strongest cluster was morning CVD/large-trade continuation: e.g. `large_trade_pressure_continuation`, `large20_w15_imb0.1`, long 10:00-10:30, n50/net $8,975/PF 2.16/expectancy R 0.465, train PF 2.40, test PF 2.03, positive months 11/13; stricter three-way audit over the top 50 candidates found 29 with PF >=1.2 in 2025 train, 2026-Q1 validation, and 2026-Q2 holdout. Other robust clusters included 10:30 positive 5-minute CVD plus >=8 tick price continuation into 12:00/13:30, 11:00 15-minute pressure continuation, and 13:00/13:30 large-trade pressure fades. Recommendation: purchasing/obtaining longer ES `trades` history is justified for this branch because the signal clusters are simple, repeated, and survive the limited three-way split; however, do not accept or stage a tradable config until a full-history trade-side dataset clears default WFA/monkey/Monte Carlo plus Apex audit. This remains trade-side orderflow only; quote/depth-dependent concepts still require `mbp-1`, `tbbo`, or `mbo`.

Thesis is to trade ES against MES aggressive-flow pressure when the micro contract diverges from ES, treating MES as a smaller-participant/liquidity-demand proxy; academic support comes from individual-investor/small-trade order-imbalance and cross-market price-discovery literature including Kaniel/Saar/Titman, Barber/Odean/Zhu, and Hasbrouck-style cross-market work. Source used official U.S. Drought Monitor / NDMC data services for CONUS percent-area drought categories and DSCI: `/private/tmp/usdm_conus_area_percent_raw.csv`, `/private/tmp/usdm_conus_dsci_raw.csv`, merged raw cache `/private/tmp/usdm_conus_drought_raw.csv`, feature cache `/private/tmp/usdm_conus_drought_features.csv`, scratch script `/private/tmp/usdm_drought_es_screen.py`, screen results `/private/tmp/usdm_drought_es_screen_all.csv` and `/private/tmp/usdm_drought_es_screen_top.csv`; ES cache `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet`. Parsed 1,380 weekly rows from 2000-01-04 through 2026-06-09. No-lookahead handling used Tuesday map date plus two calendar days, matching the official Thursday morning release before ES RTH. The screen built D0-D4 cumulative area, DSCI, moderate/severe/extreme/exceptional-only area, weighted drought pressure, severe/extreme shares of drought, relief/stress composites, changes, percentage changes, rolling ranks, z-scores, and mean gaps. It evaluated 482,112 no-lookahead ES rows over 3,786 eligible sessions and 442 drought-derived features, with zero pass-like rows, one near-like row, two loose-shape rows, zero mean-reversion pass/near/loose rows, zero rows with `wfa_n >= 500` and `wfa_pf >= 1.5`, zero rows with `wfa_n >= 500` and `wfa_pf >= 1.4`, and zero rows with `wfa_n >= 400`, `wfa_pf >= 1.4`, `incubation_n >= 50`, and `incubation_pf >= 1.2`. The lone near row was continuation-shaped, not mean reversion: `moderate_only_pct1 <= -0.035103`, prior-up long `11:00 -> 15:30`, early n140/PF 0.933, WFA n404/PF 1.435/MAR 1.436, core n71/PF 1.585, incubation n63/PF 1.151/MAR 1.295, full n607/PF 1.316. A sibling `14:30 -> 15:30` row reached WFA PF 1.473 but had early PF 0.600 and incubation PF 1.015/MAR 0.151. Rejected because national drought state does not produce a pass-shaped or mean-reversion ES branch, and the only near row is a weak prior-up long continuation diagnostic. Do not rerun simple U.S. Drought Monitor D0-D4, DSCI, drought severity, drought relief/worsening, drought pressure, drought rank, drought z-score, or climate-stress variants without a materially different execution signal or cross-asset confirmation.

No-lookahead handling used each AQI date from the next business day, so ES trades only used completed prior-day AQI. Best broad long diagnostics had WFA PF near 1.15 or lower and failed early history. Rejected because NYC metro AQI does not produce even a loose ES intraday edge after current costs and prior-day timing; do not rerun simple EPA/AirNow AQI, PM2.5, ozone, AQI change, air-pollution stress, air-pollution relief, pollution rank, or pollution z-score variants without a materially different execution signal or a point-in-time monitor-level PM2.5 reconstruction.

- Philadelphia Fed SPF Anxious Index macro-expectations screen: rejected before staged implementation as a no-cost professional-forecaster uncertainty source distinct from consumer/active-manager sentiment, NFCI/CFNAI, WEI, CMDI, WUI, and price/orderflow continuation. Source was the official Philadelphia Fed Survey of Professional Forecasters Anxious Index workbook `https://www.philadelphiafed.org/-/media/frbp/assets/surveys-and-data/survey-of-professional-forecasters/anxious-index/anxious_index_chart.xlsx`, cached at `/private/tmp/philly_spf_anxious_index_chart.xlsx`; raw cache `/private/tmp/philly_spf_anxious_index_raw.csv`; feature cache `/private/tmp/philly_spf_anxious_index_features.csv`; screen results `/private/tmp/philly_spf_anxious_index_es_screen_all.csv` and `/private/tmp/philly_spf_anxious_index_es_screen_top.csv`; ES cache `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet`. Academic framing used survey-forecast disagreement/uncertainty and macro-expectations asset-pricing logic: high recession-probability expectations can proxy risk-aversion/liquidity stress and motivate a same-day ES reversal test after completed intraday weakness. Parsed 231 quarterly rows from 1969Q1 through 2026Q3. The workbook labels the quarter being forecast, so no-lookahead handling made each Anxious Index value eligible only from the first business day of that forecast quarter, which is later than the prior-quarter SPF survey publication but avoids using the ex-post recession-shading column. The screen built Anxious Index level, 1/2/4/8-quarter changes and percentage changes, 2/4/8-quarter mean gaps, 4/8/20/40-quarter ranks and z-scores, stress/relief composites, and tested only ES same-day mean-reversion rows (`prior_down` long or `prior_up` short) across entries `09:35`, `10:00`, `10:30`, `11:00`, `13:30`, and `14:30`, exits `12:00`, `15:30`, and `15:59`, one ES contract, and `$30` round-turn cost.
